61: Part I: Dedication
62: 
63: Again you show yourselves, you wavering Forms,
64: Revealed, as you once were, to clouded vision.
65: Shall I attempt to hold you fast once more?
66: Heart’s willing still to suffer that illusion?
67: You crowd so near! Well then, you shall endure,         5
68: And rouse me, from your mist and cloud’s confusion:
69: My spirit feels so young again: it’s shaken
70: By magic breezes that your breathings waken.
71: 
72: You bring with you the sight of joyful days,
73: And many a loved shade rises to the eye:               10
74: And like some other half-forgotten phrase,
75: First Love returns, and Friendship too is nigh:
76: Pain is renewed, and sorrow: all the ways,
77: Life wanders in its labyrinthine flight,
78: Naming the good, those that Fate has robbed            15
79: Of lovely hours, those slipped from me and lost.
80: 
81: They can no longer hear this latest song,
82: Spirits, to whom I gave my early singing:
83: That kindly crowd itself is now long gone,
84: Alas, it dies away, that first loud ringing!           20
85: I bring my verses to the unknown throng,
86: My heart’s made anxious even by their clapping,
87: And those besides delighted by my verse,
88: If they still live, are scattered through the Earth.
89: 
90: I feel a long and unresolved desire                    25
91: For that serene and solemn land of ghosts:
92: It quivers now, like an Aeolian lyre,
93: My stuttering verse, with its uncertain notes,
94: A shudder takes me: tear on tear, entire,
95: The firm heart feels weakened and remote:              30
96: What I possess seems far away from me,
97: And what is gone becomes reality.
98: Part I: Prelude On Stage
99: 
100: (Director, Dramatist, Comedian)
101: 
102: Director
103: 
104: You two, who’ve often stood by me,
105: In times of need, when trouble’s breaking,
106: Say what success our undertaking                  35
107: Will meet with, then, in Germany?
108: I’d rather like the crowd to enjoy it,
109: Since they live and let live, truly.
110: The stage is set, the boards complete,
111: And they await our festivity.                     40
112: They’re seated already, eyebrows raised,
113: Calmly hoping they’ll be amazed.
114: I know how to make the people happy:
115: But I’ve never been so embarrassed: not
116: That they’ve been used to the best, you see,      45
117: Yet they’ve all read such a dreadful lot.
118: How can we make it all seem fresh and new,
119: Weighty, but entertaining too?
120: I’d love to see a joyful crowd, that’s certain,
121: When the waves drive them to our place,           50
122: And with tremendous and repeated surging,
123: Squeeze them through the narrow gate of grace:
124: In the light of day they’re there already,
125: Pushing, till they’ve reached the window,
126: As if they’re at the baker’s, starving, nearly    55
127: Breaking their necks: just for a ticket. Oh!
128: Only poets can work this miracle on men
129: So various: the day is yours, my friend!
130: Dramatist
131: 
132: O, don’t speak to me of that varied crew,
133: The sight of whom makes inspiration fade.         60
134: Veil, from me, the surging multitude,
135: Whose whirling will drives us everyway.
136: No, some heavenly silence lead me to,
137: Where for the poet alone pure joy’s at play:
138: Where Love and Friendship too grace our hearts,   65
139: Created and inspired by heavenly arts.
140: 
141: Ah! What springs here from our deepest being,
142: What the shy trembling lips in speaking meant,
143: Now falling awry, and now perhaps succeeding,
144: Is swallowed in the fierce Moment’s violence.     70
145: Often, when the first years are done, unseeing,
146: It appears at last, complete, in deepest sense.
147: What dazzles is a Momentary act:
148: What’s true is left for posterity, intact.
149: 
150: Comedian
151: 
152: Don’t speak about posterity to me!                75
153: If I went on about posterity,
154: Where would you get your worldly fun?
155: Folk want it, and they’ll still have some.
156: The presence of a fine young man
157: Is nice, I think, for everyone.                   80
158: Who, comfortably, shares his wit,
159: And to their moods takes no exception:
160: He’ll make himself a greater hit,
161: And win a more secure reception.
162: Be brave, and show them what you’ve got,          85
163: Have Fantasy with all her chorus, yes,
164: Mind, Reason, Passion, Tears, the lot,
165: But don’t you leave out Foolishness.
166: Director
167: 
168: Make sure, above all, plenty’s happening there!
169: They come to look, and then they want to stare.         90
170: Spin endlessly before their faces,
171: So the people gape amazed,
172: You’ve won them by your many paces,
173: You’ll be the man most praised.
174: The mass are only moved by things en masse,             95
175: Each one, himself, will choose the bit he needs:
176: Who brings a lot, brings something that will pass:
177: And everyone goes home contentedly.
178: You’ll give a piece, why then give it them in pieces!
179: With such a stew you’re destined for success.           100
180: Easy to serve, it’s as easy to invent.
181: What use to bring them your complete intent?
182: The Public will soon pick at what you’ve dressed.
183: 
184: Dramatist
185: 
186: You don’t see how badly such work will do!
187: How little it suits the genuine creator!                105
188: Already, I see, it’s a principle with you.
189: The finest master is a sloppy worker.
190: 
191: Director
192: 
193: Such a reproach leaves me unmoved:
194: The man who seeks to be approved,
195: Must stick to the best tools for it,                    110
196: Think, soft wood’s the best to split,
197: And have a look for whom you write!
198: See, this is one that boredom drives,
199: Another’s from some overloaded table,
200: Or, worst of all, he’s one arrives,                     115
201: Like most, fresh from the daily paper.
202: They rush here mindlessly, as to a Masque,
203: And curiosity inspires their hurry:
204: The ladies bring themselves, and in their best,
205: Come and play their parts and ask no fee.        120
206: What dream of yours is this, exalted verse?
207: Doesn’t a full house make you happy?
208: Have a good look at your patrons first!
209: One half are coarse, the rest are chilly.
210: After the show he hopes for card-play:           125
211: He hopes for a wild night, and a woman’s kiss.
212: Why then do so many poor fools plague,
213: The sweet Muse, for such a goal as this?
214: I tell you, just give them more and more,
215: So you’ll never stray far from the mark,         130
216: Just seek to confuse them, in the dark:
217: To keep them happy, that’s hard - for sure.
218: And now what’s wrong? Delight or Pain?
219: Dramatist
220: 
221: Go, look for another scribbler by night!
222: Shall the poet throw away the highest right,         135
223: The right of humanity, that Nature gave,
224: Carelessly, so that you might gain!
225: How will he move all hearts again?
226: How will each element be his slave?
227: Is that harmony nothing, from his breast unfurled,   140
228: That draws back into his own heart, the world?
229: When Nature winds the lengthened filaments,
230: Indifferently, on her eternal spindle,
231: When all the tuneless mass of elements,
232: In their sullen discord, jar and jangle –            145
233: Who parts the ever-flowing ranks of creation,
234: Stirs them, so rhythmic measure is assured?
235: Who calls the One to general ordination,
236: Where it may ring in marvellous accord?
237: Who lets the storm wind rage with passion,           150
238: The sunset glow the senses move?
239: Who scatters every lovely springtime blossom
240: Beneath the footsteps of the one we love?
241: Who weaves the slight green wreath of leaves,
242: To honour work well done in every art?               155
243: What makes Olympus sure, joins deities?
244: The power of Man, revealed by the bard.
245: Comedian
246: 
247: So use it then, all this fine energy,
248: And drive along the work of poetry,
249: To show how we are driven in Love’s play.          160
250: By chance we meet, we feel, we stay,
251: And bit by bit we’re tightly bound:
252: Happiness grows, and then it’s fenced around:
253: We’re all inflamed then comes the sorrowing:
254: Before you know it, there’s a novel brewing!       165
255: Why don’t we give such a piece!
256: Grasp the life of man complete!
257: Everyone lives, though it’s seldom confessed,
258: And wherever you grasp, there’s interest.
259: In varied pictures there’s little light,           170
260: A lot of error, and a gleam of right,
261: So the best of drinks is brewed,
262: So the world’s cheered and renewed.
263: Then see the flower of lovely youth collect,
264: To hear your words, and view the offering,         175
265: And every tender nature will extract
266: A melancholy food from what you bring,
267: They’ll gain now this and that from your art,
268: So each sees what is present in their heart.
269: They’re readily moved to weeping or to laughter,   180
270: They’ll admire your verve, and enjoy the show:
271: What’s finished you can never alter after:
272: Minds still in growth will be grateful, though.
273: Dramatist
274: 
275: So give me back that time again,
276: When I was still ‘becoming’,                 185
277: When words gushed like a fountain
278: In new, and endless flowing,
279: Then for me mists veiled the world,
280: In every bud the wonder glowed,
281: A thousand flowers I unfurled,               190
282: That every valley, richly, showed.
283: I had nothing, yet enough:
284: Joy in illusion, thirst for truth.
285: Give every passion, free to move,
286: The deepest bliss, filled with pain,         195
287: The force of hate, the power of love,
288: Oh, give me back my youth again!
289: 
290: Comedian
291: 
292: Youth is what you need, dear friend,
293: When enemies jostle you, of course,
294: And girls, filled with desire, bend          200
295: Their arms around your neck, with force,
296: When the swift-run race’s garland
297: Beckons from the hard-won goal,
298: When from the swirling dance, a man
299: Drinks until the night is old.               205
300: But to play that well-known lyre
301: With courage and with grace,
302: Moved by self-imposed desire,
303: At a sweet wandering pace,
304: That is your function, Age,                  210
305: And our respect won’t lessen.
306: Age doesn’t make us childish, as they say,
307: It finds that we’re still children.
308: 
309: Director
310: 
311: That’s enough words for the moment,
312: Now let me see some action!                 215
313: While you’re handing out the compliments,
314: You should also make things happen.
315: Why talk so much of inspiration?
316: Delay won’t make it flow, you see.
317: Since Poetry gave the gift of creation,     220
318: Take your orders then from Poetry.
319: You know what’s wanted here,
320: We need strong ale to appear:
321: So brew me a barrel right away!
322: Tomorrow won’t do what’s undone today,      225
323: We shouldn’t waste a minute, so
324: Decide what’s possible, and just
325: Grasp it firmly like a hoe,
326: Make sure that you let nothing go,
327: And work it about, because you must.        230
328: On the German stage, you see,
329: Everyone tries out what he can:
330: Don’t fail to show me, I’m your man,
331: Your trap-doors, and your scenery.
332: Use heavenly lights, the big and small,     235
333: Squander stars in any number,
334: Rocky cliffs, and fire, and water,
335: Birds and creatures, use them all.
336: So in our narrow playhouse waken
337: The whole wide circle of creation,          240
338: And stride, deliberately, as well,
339: From Heaven, through the world, to Hell.
340: Part I: Prologue In Heaven
341: 
342: (God, the Heavenly Hosts, and then Mephistopheles.)
343: 
344: (The Three Archangels step forward.)
345: 
346: Raphael
347: 
348: The Sun sings out, in ancient mode,
349: His note among his brother-spheres,
350: And ends his pre-determined road,                     245
351: With peals of thunder for our ears.
352: The sight of him gives Angels power,
353: Though none can understand the way:
354: The inconceivable work is ours,
355: As bright as on the primal day.                       250
356: 
357: 
358: Gabriel
359: 
360: And swift, and swift, beyond conceiving,
361: The splendour of the Earth turns round,
362: A Paradisial light is interleaving,
363: With night’s awesome profound.
364: The ocean breaks with shining foam,                   255
365: Against the rocky cliffs deep base,
366: And rock and ocean whirl and go,
367: In the spheres’ swift eternal race.
368: 
369: Michael
370: 
371: And storms are roaring in their race
372: From sea to land, and land to sea,                    260
373: Their raging forms a fierce embrace,
374: All round, of deepest energy.
375: The lightning’s devastations blaze
376: Along the thunder-crashes’ way:
377: Yet, Lord, your messengers, shall praise              265
378: The gentle passage of your day.
379: All Three
380: 
381: The sight of it gives Angels power
382: Though none can understand the way,
383: And all your noble work is ours,
384: As bright as on the primal day.                         270
385: 
386: Mephistopheles
387: 
388: Since, O Lord, you near me once again,
389: To ask how all below is doing now,
390: And usually receive me without pain,
391: You see me too among the vile crowd.
392: Forgive me: I can’t speak in noble style,               275
393: And since I’m still reviled by this whole crew,
394: My pathos would be sure to make you smile,
395: If you had not renounced all laughter too.
396: You’ll get no word of suns and worlds from me.
397: How men torment themselves is all I see.                280
398: The little god of Earth sticks to the same old way,
399: And is as strange as on that very first day.
400: He might appreciate life a little more: he might,
401: If you hadn’t lent him a gleam of Heavenly light:
402: He calls it Reason, but only uses it                    285
403: To be more a beast than any beast as yet.
404: He seems to me, saving Your Grace,
405: Like a long-legged grasshopper: through space
406: He’s always flying: he flies and then he springs,
407: And in the grass the same old song he sings.            290
408: If he’d just lie there in the grass it wouldn’t hurt!
409: But he buries his nose in every piece of dirt.
410: 
411: God
412: 
413: Have you nothing else to name?
414: Do you always come here to complain?
415: Does nothing ever go right on the Earth?                295
416: Mephistopheles
417: 
418: No, Lord! I find, as always, it couldn’t be worse.
419: I’m so involved with Man’s wretched ways,
420: I’ve even stopped plaguing them, myself, these days.
421: 
422: God
423: 
424: Do you know, Faust?
425: 
426: Mephistopheles
427: 
428:                           The Doctor?
429: 
430: God
431:                                         My servant, first!
432: 
433: Mephistopheles
434: 
435: In truth! He serves you in a peculiar manner.                300
436: There’s no earthly food or drink at that fool’s dinner.
437: He drives his spirit outwards, far,
438: Half-conscious of its maddened dart:
439: From Heaven demands the brightest star,
440: And from the Earth, Joy’s highest art,                       305
441: And all the near and all the far,
442: Fails to release his throbbing heart.
443: 
444: God
445: 
446: Though he’s still confused at how to serve me,
447: I’ll soon lead him to a clearer dawning,
448: In the green sapling, can’t the gardener see                 310
449: The flowers and fruit the coming years will bring.
450: Mephistopheles
451: 
452: What do you wager? I might win him yet!
453: If you give me your permission first,
454: I’ll lead him gently on the road I set.
455: 
456: God
457: 
458: As long as he’s alive on Earth,                315
459: So long as that I won’t forbid it,
460: For while man strives he errs.
461: 
462: Mephistopheles
463: 
464: My thanks: I’ve never willingly seen fit
465: To spend my time amongst the dead,
466: I much prefer fresh cheeks instead.            320
467: To corpses, I close up my house:
468: Or it’s too like a cat with a mouse.
469: 
470: God
471: 
472: Well and good, you’ve said what’s needed!
473: Divert this spirit from his source,
474: You know how to trap him, lead him,
475: On your downward course,                       325
476: And when you must, then stand, amazed:
477: A good man, in his darkest yearning,
478: Is still aware of virtue’s ways.
479: 
480: Mephistopheles
481: 
482: That’s fine! There’s hardly any waiting.       330
483: My wager’s more than safe I’m thinking.
484: When I achieve my goal, in winning,
485: You’ll let me triumph with a swelling heart.
486: He’ll eat the dust, and with an art,
487: Like the snake my mother, known for sinning.   335
488: God
489: 
490: You can appear freely too:
491: Those like you I’ve never hated.
492: Of all the spirits who deny, it’s you,
493: The jester, who’s most lightly weighted.
494: Man’s energies all too soon seek the level,              340
495: He quickly desires unbroken slumber,
496: So I gave him you to join the number,
497: To move, and work, and play the devil.
498: But you the genuine sons of light,
499: Enjoy the living beauty bright!                          345
500: Becoming, that works and lives forever,
501: Embrace you in love’s limits dear,
502: And all that may as Appearance waver,
503: Fix firmly with everlasting Idea!
504: 
505: (Heaven closes, and the Archangels separate.)
506: 
507: Mephistopheles (alone)
508: 
509: I like to hear the Old Man’s words, from time to time,   350
510: And take care, when I’m with him, not to spew.
511: It’s very nice when such a great Gentleman,
512: Chats with the devil, in ways so human, too!
513: Part I Scene I: Night
514: 
515: (In a high-vaulted Gothic chamber, Faust, in a chair at his desk, restless.)
516: 
517: Ah! Now I’ve done Philosophy,
518: I’ve finished Law and Medicine,                                         355
519: And sadly even Theology:
520: Taken fierce pains, from end to end.
521: Now here I am, a fool for sure!
522: No wiser than I was before:
523: Master, Doctor’s what they call me,                                     360
524: And I’ve been ten years, already,
525: Crosswise, arcing, to and fro,
526: Leading my students by the nose,
527: And see that we can know - nothing!
528: It almost sets my heart burning.                                        365
529: I’m cleverer than all these teachers,
530: Doctors, Masters, scribes, preachers:
531: I’m not plagued by doubt or scruple,
532: Scared by neither Hell nor Devil –
533: Instead all Joy is snatched away,                                       370
534: What’s worth knowing, I can’t say,
535: I can’t say what I should teach
536: To make men better or convert each.
537: And then I’ve neither goods nor gold,
538: No worldly honour, or splendour hold:                                   375
539: Not even a dog would play this part!
540: So I’ve given myself to Magic art,
541: To see if, through Spirit powers and lips,
542: I might have all secrets at my fingertips.
543: And no longer, with rancid sweat, so,                                   380
544: Still have to speak what I cannot know:
545: That I may understand whatever
546: Binds the world’s innermost core together,
547: See all its workings, and its seeds,
548: Deal no more in words’ empty reeds.                                     385
549: O, may you look, full moon that shines,
550: On my pain for this last time:
551: So many midnights from my desk,
552: I have seen you, keeping watch:
553: When over my books and paper,                    390
554: Saddest friend, you appear!
555: Ah! If on the mountain height
556: I might stand in your sweet light,
557: Float with spirits in mountain caves,
558: Swim the meadows in twilight’ waves,             395
559: Free from the smoke of knowledge too,
560: Bathe in your health-giving dew!
561: Alas! In this prison must I stick?
562: This hollow darkened hole of brick,
563: Where even the lovely heavenly light             400
564: Shines through stained glass, dull not bright.
565: Hemmed in, by heaps of books,
566: Piled to the highest vault, and higher,
567: Worm eaten, decked with dust,
568: Surrounded by smoke-blackened paper,             405
569: Glass vials, boxes round me, hurled,
570: Stuffed with Instruments thrown together,
571: Packed with ancestral lumber –
572: This is my world! And what a world!
573: And need you ask why my heart                    410
574: Makes such tremors in my breast?
575: Why all my life-energies are
576: Choked by some unknown distress?
577: Smoke and mildew hem me in,
578: Instead of living Nature, then,                  415
579: Where God once created Men,
580: Bones of creatures, and dead limbs!
581: Fly! Upwards! Into Space, flung wide!
582: Isn’t this book, with secrets crammed,
583: From Nostradamus’ very hand,                     420
584: Enough to be my guide?
585: When I know the starry road,
586: And Nature, you instruct me,
587: My soul’s power, you shall flow,
588: As spirits can with spirits be.                  425
589: Useless, this dusty pondering here
590: To read the sacred characters:
591: Soar round me, Spirits, and be near:
592: If you hear me, then answer!
593: (He opens the Book, and sees the Symbol of the Macrocosm)
594: 
595: Ah! In a moment, what bliss flows                                   430
596: Through my senses from this Sign!
597: I feel life’s youthful, holy joy: it glows,
598: Fresh in every nerve and vein of mine.
599: This symbol now that calms my inward raging,
600: Perhaps a god deigned to write,                                     435
601: Filling my poor heart with delight,
602: And with its mysterious urging
603: Revealing, round me, Nature’s might?
604: Am I a god? All seems so clear to me!
605: It seems the deepest works of Nature                                440
606: Lie open to my soul, with purest feature.
607: Now I understand what wise men see:
608: “The world of spirits is not closed:
609: Your senses are: your heart is dead!
610: Rise, unwearied, disciple: bathe instead                            445
611: Your earthly breast in the morning’s glow!”
612: 
613: (He gazes at the Symbol.)
614: 
615: How each to the Whole its selfhood gives,
616: One in another works and lives!
617: How Heavenly forces fall and rise,
618: Golden vessels pass each other by!                                  450
619: Blessings from their wings disperse:
620: They penetrate from Heaven to Earth,
621: Sounding a harmony through the Universe!
622: Such a picture! Ah, alas! Merely a picture!
623: How then can I grasp you endless Nature?                            455
624: Where are your breasts that pour out Life entire,
625: To which the Earth and Heavens cling so,
626: Where withered hearts would drink? You flow
627: You nourish, yet I languish so, in vain desire.
628: 
629: (He strikes the book indignantly, and catches sight of the Symbol
630: of the Earth-Spirit.)
631: How differently it works on me, this Sign!                           460
632: You, the Spirit of Earth, are nearer:
633: Already, I feel my power is greater,
634: Already, I glow, as with fresh wine.
635: I feel the courage to engage the world,
636: Into the pain and joy of Earth be hurled,                            465
637: And though the storm wind is unfurled,
638: Fearless, in the shipwreck’s teeth, be whirled.
639: There’s cloud above me –
640: The Moon hides its light –
641: The lamp flickers!
642: Now it dies! Crimson rays dart                                       470
643: Round my head – Horror
644: Flickers from the vault above,
645: And grips me tight!
646: I feel you float around me,                                          475
647: Spirit, I summon to appear, speak to me!
648: Ah! What tears now at the core of me!
649: All my senses reeling
650: With fresh feeling!
651: I feel you draw my whole heart towards you!                          480
652: You must! You must! Though my Life’s lost, too!
653: 
654: (He grips the book and speaks the mysterious name of the Spirit. A crimson
655: flame flashes, the Spirit appears in the flame.)
656: 
657: Spirit
658: 
659: Who calls me?
660: 
661: Faust (Looking away)
662: 
663:                          Terrible to gaze at!
664: 
665: Spirit
666: 
667: Mightily you have drawn me to you,
668: Long, from my sphere, snatched your food,
669: And now –
670: Faust
671: 
672:                    Ah! Endure you, I cannot!                485
673: 
674: Spirit
675: 
676: You beg me to show myself, you implore,
677: You wish to hear my voice, and see my face:
678: The mighty prayer of your soul weighs
679: With me, I am here! – What wretched terror
680: Grips you, the Superhuman! Where is your soul’s calling?    490
681: Where is the heart that made a world inside, enthralling:
682: Carried it, nourished it, swollen with joy, so tremulous,
683: That you too might be a Spirit, one of us?
684: Where are you, Faust, whose ringing voice
685: Drew towards me with all your force?                        495
686: Are you he, who, breathing my breath,
687: Trembles in all your life’s depths,
688: A fearful, writhing worm?
689: 
690: Faust
691: 
692: Shall I fear you: you form of fire?
693: I am, I am Faust: I am your peer!                           500
694: 
695: Spirit
696: 
697: In Life’s wave, in action’s storm,
698: I float, up and down,
699: I blow, to and fro!
700: Birth and the tomb,
701: An eternal flow,                                            505
702: A woven changing,
703: A glow of Being.
704: Over Time’s quivering loom intent,
705: Working the Godhead’s living garment.
706: 
707: Faust
708: 
709: You who wander the world, on every hand,                    510
710: Active Spirit, how close to you I feel!
711: 
712: Spirit
713: 
714: You’re like the Spirit that you understand
715: Not me!
716: 
717: (It vanishes.)
718: 
719: Faust (Overwhelmed)
720: 
721: Not you?
722: Who then?                                                           515
723: I, the image of the Godhead!
724: Not even like you?
725: 
726: (A knock.)
727: 
728: Oh, fate! I know that sound – it’s my attendant –
729: My greatest fortune’s ruined!
730: In all the fullness of my doing,                                    520
731: He must intrude, that arid pedant!
732: 
733: (Wagner enters, in gown and nightcap, lamp in hand. Faust turns to him
734: impatiently.)
735: 
736: Wagner
737: 
738: Forgive me! But I heard you declaim:
739: Reading, I’m sure, from some Greek tragedy?
740: To profit from that art is my aim,
741: Nowadays it goes down splendidly.                                   525
742: I’ve often heard it claimed, you see
743: A priest could learn from the Old Comedy.
744: 
745: Faust
746: 
747: Yes, when the priest’s a comedian already:
748: Which might well seem to be the case.
749: Wagner
750: 
751: Ah! When a man’s so penned in his study,          530
752: And scarcely sees the world on holidays,
753: And barely through the glass, and far off then,
754: How can he lead men, through persuading them?
755: 
756: Faust
757: 
758: You can’t, if you can’t feel it, if it never
759: Rises from the soul, and sways                    535
760: The heart of every single hearer,
761: With deepest power, in simple ways.
762: You’ll sit forever, gluing things together,
763: Cooking up a stew from other’s scraps,
764: Blowing on a miserable fire,                      540
765: Made from your heap of dying ash.
766: Let apes and children praise your art,
767: If their admiration’s to your taste,
768: But you’ll never speak from heart to heart,
769: Unless it rises up from your heart’s space.       545
770: Wagner
771: 
772: Still, lecturing brings orators success:
773: I feel that I am far behind the rest.
774: 
775: Faust
776: 
777: Seek to profit honestly!
778: Don’t be an empty tinkling fool!
779: Understanding, and true clarity,              550
780: Express themselves without art’s rule!
781: And if you mean what you say,
782: Why hunt for words, anyway?
783: Yes, your speech, that glitters so,
784: Where you gather scraps for Man,              555
785: Is dead as the mist-filled winds that blow
786: Through the dried-up leaves of autumn!
787: 
788: Wagner
789: 
790: Oh, God! Art is long
791: And life is short.
792: Often the studies that I’m working on         560
793: Make me anxious, in my head and heart.
794: How hard it is to command the means
795: By which a man attains the very source!
796: Before a man has travelled half his course,
797: The wretched devil has to die it seems.       565
798: 
799: Faust
800: 
801: Parchment then, is that your holy well,
802: From which drink always slakes your thirst?
803: You’ll never truly be refreshed until
804: It pours itself from your own soul, first.
805: Wagner
806: 
807: Pardon me, but it’s a great delight                    570
808: When, moved by the spirit of the ages, we have sight
809: Of how a wiser man has thought, and how
810: Widely at last we’ve spread his word about.
811: 
812: Faust
813: 
814: Oh yes, as widely as the constellations!
815: My friend, all of the ages that are gone               575
816: Now make up a book with seven seals.
817: The spirit of the ages, that you find,
818: In the end, is the spirit of Humankind:
819: A mirror where all the ages are revealed.
820: And so often it’s all a mere misery                    580
821: Something we run away from at first sight.
822: A pile of sweepings, a lumber room, maybe
823: At best, a puppet show, that’s bright
824: With maxims, excellent, pragmatic,
825: Suitable when dolls’ mouths wax dramatic!              585
826: 
827: Wagner
828: 
829: But, the world! Men’s hearts and minds!
830: Something of those, at least, I’d like to know.
831: 
832: Faust
833: 
834: Yes, what men choose to understand!
835: Who dares to name the child’s real name, though?
836: The few who knew what might be learned,                590
837: Foolish enough to put their whole heart on show,
838: And reveal their feelings to the crowd below,
839: Mankind has always crucified and burned.
840: I beg you, friend, it’s now the dead of night,
841: We must break up this conversation.                    595
842: Wagner
843: 
844: I would have watched with you, if I might
845: Speak with you still, so learned in oration.
846: But tomorrow, on Easter’s first holy day,
847: I’ll ask my several questions, if I may.
848: I’ve pursued my work, zealously studying:          600
849: There’s much I know: yet I’d know everything.
850: (He leaves.)
851: 
852: Faust (Alone.)
853: 
854: That mind alone never loses hope,
855: That keeps to the shallows eternally,
856: Grabs, with eager hand, the wealth it sees,
857: And rejoices at the worms for which it gropes!     605
858: Dare such a human voice echo, too,
859: Where this depth of Spirit surrounds me?
860: Ah yet! For just this once, my thanks to you,
861: You sorriest of all earth’s progeny!
862: You’ve torn me away from that despair,             610
863: That would have soon overwhelmed my senses.
864: Ah! The apparition was so hugely there,
865: It might have truly dwarfed my defences.
866: I, image of the Godhead, already one,
867: Who thought the spirit of eternal truth so near,   615
868: Enjoying the light, both heavenly and clear,
869: Setting to one side the earthbound man:
870: I, more than Angel, a free force,
871: Ready to flow through Nature’s veins,
872: And, in creating, enjoy the life divine,           620
873: Pulsing with ideas: must atone again!
874: A word like thunder swept me away.
875: I dare not measure myself against you.
876: I possessed the power to summon you,
877: But not the power to make you stay.                625
878: In that blissful moment, then
879: I felt myself so small, so great:
880: Cruelly you hurled me back again,
881: Into Man’s uncertain state.
882: What shall I learn from? Or leave?                   630
883: Shall I obey that yearning?
884: Ah! Our actions, and not just our grief,
885: Impede us on life’s journey.
886: Some more and more alien substance presses
887: On the splendour that the Mind conceives:            635
888: And when we gain what this world possesses,
889: We say the better world’s dream deceives.
890: The splendid feelings that give us life,
891: Fade among the crowd’s earthly strife.
892: If imagination flew with courage, once,              640
893: And, full of hope, stretched out to eternity,
894: Now a little room is quite enough,
895: When joy on joy has gone, in time’s whirling sea.
896: Care has nested in the heart’s depths,
897: Restless, she rocks there, spoiling joy and rest,    645
898: There she works her secret pain,
899: And wears new masks, ever and again,
900: Appears as wife and child, fields and houses,
901: As water, fire, or knife or poison:
902: Still we tremble for what never strikes us,          650
903: And must still cry for what has not yet gone.
904: I am no god: I feel it all too deeply.
905: I am the worm that writhes in dust: see,
906: As in the dust it lives, and seeks to eat,
907: It’s crushed and buried by the passing feet.         655
908: Is this not dust, what these vaults hold,
909: These hundred shelves that cramp me:
910: This junk, and all the thousand-fold
911: Shapes, of a moth-ridden world, around me?
912: Will I find here what I’m lacking else,              660
913: Shall I read, perhaps, as a thousand books insist,
914: That Mankind everywhere torments itself,
915: So, here and there, some happy man exists?
916: What do you say to me, bare grinning skull?
917: Except that once your brain whirled like mine,       665
918: Sought the clear day, and in the twilight dull,
919: With a breath of truth, went wretchedly awry.
920: For sure, you instruments mock at me,
921: With cylinders and arms, wheels and cogs:
922: I stand at the door: and you should be the key:   670
923: You’re deftly cut, but you undo no locks.
924: Mysterious, even in broad daylight,
925: Nature won’t let her veil be raised:
926: What your spirit can’t bring to sight,
927: Won’t by screws and levers be displayed.          675
928: You, ancient tools, I’ve never used
929: You’re here because my father used you,
930: Ancient scroll, you’ve darkened too,
931: From smoking candles burned above you.
932: Better the little I had was squandered,           680
933: Than sweat here under its puny weight!
934: What from your father you’ve inherited,
935: You must earn again, to own it straight.
936: What’s never used, leaves us overburdened,
937: But we can use what the Moment may create!        685
938: Yet why does that place so draw my sight,
939: Is that flask a magnet for my gaze?
940: Why is there suddenly so sweet a light,
941: As moonlight in a midnight woodland plays?
942: I salute you, phial of rare potion,               690
943: I lift you down, with devotion!
944: In you I worship man’s art and mind,
945: Embodiment of sweet sleeping draughts:
946: Extract, with deadly power, refined,
947: Show your master all his craft!                   695
948: I see you, and my pain diminishes,
949: I grasp you, and my struggles grow less,
950: My spirit’s flood tide ebbs, more and more,
951: I seem to be where ocean waters meet,
952: A glassy flood gleams around my feet,             700
953: New day invites me to a newer shore.
954: A fiery chariot sweeps nearer
955: On light wings! I feel ready, free
956: To cut a new path through the ether
957: And reach new spheres of pure activity.           705
958: This greater life, this godlike bliss!
959: You, but a worm, have you earned this?
960: Choosing to turn your back, ah yes,
961: On all Earth’s lovely Sun might promise!
962: Let me dare to throw those gates open,            710
963: That other men go creeping by!
964: Now’s the time, to prove through action
965: Man’s dignity may rise divinely high,
966: Never trembling at that void where,
967: Imagination damns itself to pain,                 715
968: Striving towards the passage there,
969: Round whose mouth all Hell’s fires flame:
970: Choose to take that step, happy to go
971: Where danger lies, where Nothingness may flow.
972: Come here to me, cup of crystal, clear!           720
973: Free of your ancient cover now appear,
974: You whom I’ve never, for many a year,
975: Considered! You shone at ancestral feasts,
976: Cheering the over-serious guests:
977: One man passing you to another here.              725
978: It was the drinker’s duty to explain in rhyme
979: The splendour of your many carved designs
980: Or drain it at a draught, and breathe, in time:
981: You remind me of those youthful nights of mine.
982: Now I will never pass you to a friend,            730
983: Or test my wits on your art again.
984: Here’s a juice will stun any man born:
985: It fills your hollow with a browner liquid.
986: I prepared it, now I choose the fluid,
987: At last I drink, and with my soul I bid           735
988: A high and festive greeting to the Dawn!
989: 
990: (He puts the cup to his mouth.)

994: Choir of Angels
995: 
996: Christ has arisen!
997: Joy to the One, of us,
998: Who the pernicious,
999: Ancestral, insidious,                             740
1000: Fault has unwoven.
1001: Faust
1002: 
1003: What deep humming, what shining sound
1004: Strikes the glass from my hand with power?

1006: Proclaiming Easter’s festive course? Our                     745
1007: Choirs, do you already sing the hymn of consolation,
1008: Which once rang out, in deathly night, in Angels’ oration,
1009: That certainty of a new testament’s hour?

1011: Chorus of Women

1013: With pure spices
1014: We embalmed him,                                             750

1017: Linen and bindings,
1018: We unwound there,
1019: Ah! Now we find                                              755
1020: Christ is not here.

1022: Choir of Angels

1024: Christ has arisen!
1025: Blissful Beloved,
1026: Out of what grieved,
1027: Tested, and healed:                                          760
1028: His trial is won.
1029: 
1030: Faust
1031: 
1032: You heavenly sounds, powerful and mild,
1033: Why, in the dust, here, do you seek me?
1034: Ring out where tender hearts are reconciled.
1035: I hear your message, but faith fails me:                     765
1036: The marvellous is faith’s dearest child.
1037: I don’t attempt to rise to that sphere,
1038: From which the message rings:
1039: Yet I know from childhood what it sings,
1040: And I’m recalled to life once more.                          770
1041: In other times a Heavenly kiss would fall
1042: On me, in the deep Sabbath silence:
1043: The bell notes filled with presentiments,
1044: And a prayer was pleasure’s call:
1045: A sweet yearning, beyond my understanding,   775
1046: Set me wandering through woods and fields,
1047: And while a thousand tears were burning
1048: I felt a world around me come to be.
1049: Love called out the lively games of youth,
1050: The joy of spring’s idle holiday:            780
1051: Memory’s childish feelings, in truth,
1052: Hold me back from the last sombre way.
1053: O, sing on you sweet songs of Heaven!
1054: My tears flow, Earth claims me again!
1055: 
1056: Chorus of Disciples
1057: 
1058: Has the buried one                           785
1059: Already, living,
1060: Raised himself, alone,
1061: Splendidly soaring:
1062: Is he, in teeming air,
1063: Near to creative bliss:                      790
1064: Ah! In sorrow, we’re
1065: Here on Earth’s breast.
1066: Lacking Him, we
1067: Languish, and sigh.
1068: Ah! Master we                                795
1069: Cry for your joy!
1070: 
1071: Choir of Angels
1072: 
1073: Christ has arisen
1074: Out of corruption’s sea.
1075: Tear off your bindings
1076: Joyfully free!                               800
1077: Actively praising him,
1078: Lovingly claiming him,
1079: Fraternally aiding him,
1080: Prayerfully journeying,
1081: Joyfully promising,      805
1082: So is the Master near,
1083: So is he here!
1084: Part I Scene II: In Front Of The City-Gate
1085: 
1086: (Passers-by of all kinds appear.)
1087: 
1088: Several Apprentices
1089: 
1090: So, then, where are you away to?
1091: 
1092: Others
1093: 
1094: We’re away to the Hunting Lodge.
1095: 
1096: The Former
1097: 
1098: We’re off to saunter by the Mill.                810
1099: 
1100: An Apprentice
1101: 
1102: Off to the Riverside Inn, I’d guess.
1103: 
1104: A Second Apprentice
1105: 
1106: The way there’s not of the best.
1107: 
1108: The Others
1109: 
1110: What about you?
1111: 
1112: A Third
1113: 
1114:                    I’m with the others, still.
1115: 
1116: A Fourth
1117: 
1118: Come to the Castle, you’ll find there
1119: The prettiest girls, the finest beer,            815
1120: And the best place for a fight.
1121: A Fifth
1122: 
1123: You quarrelsome fool, are you looking
1124: For a third good hiding?
1125: Not for me, that place, I hate its very sight.
1126: 
1127: A Maidservant
1128: 
1129: No, No! I’m going back to town.                  820
1130: 
1131: Another
1132: 
1133: We’ll find him by those poplar trees for sure.
1134: 
1135: The First
1136: 
1137: Well that’s no joy for me, now:
1138: He’ll walk by your side, of course,
1139: He’ll dance with you on the green.
1140: Where’s the fun in that for me, then!            825
1141: 
1142: 
1143: The Other
1144: 
1145: I’m sure he’s not alone, he said
1146: He’d bring along that Curly-head.
1147: 
1148: A Student
1149: 
1150: My how they strut those bold women!
1151: Brother, come on! We’ll follow them.
1152: Fierce tobacco, strong beer,                     830
1153: And a girl in her finery, I prefer.
1154: A Citizen’s Daughter
1155: 
1156: They are handsome boys there, I see!
1157: But it’s truly a disgrace:
1158: They could have the best of company,
1159: And run after a painted face!                  835
1160: 
1161: Second Student (to the first)
1162: 
1163: Not so fast! Those two behind,
1164: They walk about so sweetly,
1165: One must be that neighbour of mine:
1166: I could fall for her completely.
1167: They pass by with demure paces,                840
1168: But in the end they’ll go with us.
1169: 
1170: The First
1171: 
1172: Brother, no! I shouldn’t bother, anyway.
1173: Quick! Before our quarry gets away.
1174: The hand that wields a broom on Saturday,
1175: Gives the best caress, on Sunday too, I say.   845
1176: 
1177: Citizen
1178: 
1179: No, the new mayor doesn’t suit me!
1180: Now he’s there he’s getting cocky.
1181: And what’s he done to help the town?
1182: Isn’t it getting worse each day?
1183: As always it’s us who must obey,               850
1184: And pay more money down.
1185: 
1186: A Beggar (sings)
1187: 
1188: Fine gentlemen, and lovely ladies,
1189: Rosy-cheeked and finely dressed,
1190: You could help me, for your aid is
1191: Needed: see, ease my distress!                 855
1192: Don’t let me throw my song away,
1193: Only he who gives is happy.
1194: A day when all men celebrate,
1195: Will be a harvest day for me!
1196: 
1197: Another Citizen
1198: 
1199: On holidays there’s nothing I like better     860
1200: Than talking about war and war’s display,
1201: When in Turkey far away,
1202: People one another batter.
1203: You sit by the window: have a glass:
1204: See the bright boats glide down the river,    865
1205: Then you walk back home and bless
1206: Its peacefulness, and peace, forever.
1207: 
1208: Third Citizen
1209: 
1210: Neighbour, yes! I like that too:
1211: Let them go and break their heads,
1212: Make the mess they often do:                  870
1213: So long as we’re safe in our beds.
1214: 
1215: An Old Woman (to the citizen’s daughter)
1216: 
1217: Ah! So pretty! Sweet young blood!
1218: Who wouldn’t gaze at you?
1219: Don’t be so proud! I’m very good!
1220: And what you want, I’ll bring you.            875
1221: 
1222: The Citizen’s Daughter
1223: 
1224: Agatha, come away! I must go carefully:
1225: No walking freely with such a witch as her:
1226: For on Saint Andrew’s Night she really
1227: Showed me who’ll be my future Lover.
1228: The Other
1229: 
1230: She showed me mine in a crystal ball,          880
1231: A soldier, with lots of other brave men:
1232: I look around: among them all,
1233: Yet I can never find him.
1234: 
1235: The Soldiers
1236: 
1237: Castles with towering
1238: Ramparts and wall,                             885
1239: Proud girls showing
1240: Disdain for us all,
1241: We want them to fall!
1242: The action is brave,
1243: And splendid the pay!                          890
1244: So let the trumpet,
1245: Do our recruiting,
1246: Calling to joy
1247: Calling to ruin.
1248: It’s a storm, blowing!                         895
1249: But it’s the life too!
1250: Girls and castles
1251: We must win you.
1252: The action is brave,
1253: Splendid the pay!                              900
1254: And the soldiers
1255: Go marching away.
1256: 
1257: (Faust and Wagner)
1258: 
1259: Faust
1260: 
1261: Rivers and streams are freed from ice
1262: By Spring’s sweet enlivening glance.
1263: Valleys, green with Hope’s happiness, dance:   905
1264: Old Winter, in his weakness, sighs,
1265: Withdrawing to the harsh mountains.
1266: From there, retreating, he sends down
1267: Impotent showers of hail that show
1268: In stripes across the quickening ground.       910
1269: But the sun allows nothing white below,
1270: Change and growth are everywhere,
1271: He enlivens all with his colours there,
1272: And lacking flowers of the fields outspread,
1273: He takes these gaudy people instead.           915
1274: Turn round, and from this mountain height,
1275: Look down, where the town’s in sight.
1276: That cavernous, dark gate,
1277: The colourful crowd penetrate,
1278: All will take the sun today,                   920
1279: The Risen Lord they’ll celebrate,
1280: And feel they are resurrected,
1281: From low houses, dully made,
1282: From work, where they’re constricted,
1283: From the roofs’ and gables’ weight,            925
1284: From the crush of narrow streets,
1285: From the churches’ solemn night
1286: They’re all brought to the light.
1287: Look now: see! The crowds, their feet
1288: Crushing the gardens and meadows,              930
1289: While on the river a cheerful fleet
1290: Of little boats, everywhere it flows.
1291: And over-laden, ready to sink,
1292: The last barge takes to the stream.
1293: From far off on the mountain’s brink,
1294: All the bright clothing gleams.
1295: I hear the noise from the village risen,
1296: Here is the people’s true Heaven,
1297: High and low shout happily:
1298: Here I am Man: here, dare to be!               940
1299: Wagner
1300: 
1301: Doctor, to take a walk with you,
1302: Is an honour and a prize:
1303: Alone I’d have no business here, true,
1304: Since everything that’s coarse I despise.
1305: Shrieking, fiddlers, skittles flying,                 945
1306: To me it’s all a hateful noise:
1307: They rush about possessed, crying,
1308: And call it singing: and call it joy.

1315: Under the linden-tree, already,

1317: Hey! Hey!

1398: How it must feel, O man of genius,

1410: Faust
1411: 
1412: Climb these few steps to that stone,

1423: Deserve a fraction of their glory.
1424: My father was a gloomy, honourable man,
1425: Who pondered Nature and the heavenly spheres,   1035
1426: Honestly, in his own fashion,
1427: With eccentric studies it appears:
1428: He, in his adepts’ company,
1429: Locked in his dark workshop, forever

1433: Wed the Lily, in a lukewarm bath, there
1434: In a fiery flame, both of them were
1435: Strained from one bride-bed into another,       1045

1471: I’d see, in eternal evening’s light,

1483: Heaven above me: and the waves below,

1485: Ah! Wings of the mind, so weightless           1090
1486: No bodily wings could ever be so.

1669: I could supply what’s missing, easily:         1215
1670: We learn to value what’s beyond the earthly,
1671: We yearn to reach revelation’s brink,
1672: That’s nowhere nobler or more excellent

1682: Impossible, for me to rate the word so highly

1685: I’ve written here: ‘In the Beginning was the Mind’.

1994: My friend you’ll win more
1995: For your senses, in an hour,
1996: Than in a whole year’s monotony.
1997: What the tender spirits sing,
1998: The lovely pictures that they bring,     1440
1999: Are no empty wizardry.
2000: First your sense of smell’s invited,
2001: Then your palate is delighted,
2002: And then your touch, you see.
2003: Now, I need no preparation,              1445
2004: We’re all here, so let’s begin!
2005: 
2006: Spirits
2007: 
2008: Vanish, you shadowy
2009: Vaults above!
2010: Cheerfully show,
2011: The friendliest blue                     1450
2012: Of aether, down here.
2013: Would that shadowy
2014: Clouds had gone!
2015: Starlight sparkling
2016: Milder sun                               1455
2017: Shining clear.
2018: Heavenly children
2019: In lovely confusion,
2020: Swaying and bending,
2021: Drifting past.                           1460
2022: Affectionate yearning,
2023: Following fast:
2024: Their garments flowing
2025: With fluttering ribbons,
2026: Cover the gardens,                       1465
2027: Cover the leaves,
2028: Where with each other
2029: In deep conversation
2030: Lover meets lover.
2031: Leaves on leaves!         1470
2032: Tendrils’ elation!
2033: Grapes beneath
2034: Crushed in a stream,
2035: Pressed to extreme,
2036: Crushed to fountain,      1475
2037: Of foaming wine,
2038: Trickling, fine,
2039: Through rocks divine,
2040: Leaving the heights,
2041: Spreading beneath,        1480
2042: Broad as the seas,
2043: Valleys it fills
2044: Round the green hills.
2045: And the wings still,
2046: Blissfully drunk,         1485
2047: Fly to the sun,
2048: Fly to the brightness,
2049: Towards the islands,
2050: Out of the waves
2051: Magically raised:         1490
2052: Now we can hear
2053: The choir of joy near,
2054: Over the meadow,
2055: See how they dance now,
2056: All in the air            1495
2057: Dispersing there.
2058: Some of them climbing
2059: Over the mountains,
2060: Others are swimming
2061: Over the ocean,           1500
2062: Others take flight:
2063: All towards Life,
2064: All towards distant,
2065: Love of the stars, and
2066: Approval’s bliss.         1505
2067: Mephistopheles
2068: 
2069: He’s asleep! Enough, you delicate children of air!
2070: You’ve sung to him faithfully, I declare!
2071: I’m in your debt for all this.
2072: He’s not yet the man to hold devils fast!
2073: Spellbind him with dream-forms, cast                 1510
2074: Him deep into illusions’ sea:
2075: Now, for the magic sill I must pass,
2076: I could use rat’s teeth: no need for me
2077: To conjure up a lengthier spell,
2078: One’s rustling here that will do well.               1515
2079: 
2080: The Lord of Rats and Mice,
2081: Of Flies, Frogs, Bugs and Lice,
2082: Summons you to venture here,
2083: And gnaw the threshold where
2084: He stains it with a little oil -                     1520
2085: You’ve hopped, already, to your toil!
2086: Now set to work! The fatal point,
2087: Is at the edge, it’s on the front.
2088: One more bite, then it’s complete –
2089: Now Faust, dream deeply, till we meet.               1525
2090: 
2091: Faust (Waking.)
2092: 
2093: Am I cheated then, once again?
2094: Does the Spirit-Realm’s deep yearning fade:
2095: So a mere dream has conjured up the devil,
2096: And only a dog, it was, that ran away?

2121: Mephistopheles
2122: 
2123:         Ah, now, you please me.
2124: I hope we’ll get along together:
2125: To drive away the gloomy weather,
2126: I’m dressed like young nobility,                      1535
2127: In a scarlet gold-trimmed coat,
2128: In a little silk-lined cloak,
2129: A cockerel feather in my hat,
2130: With a long, pointed sword,
2131: And I advise you, at that,                            1540
2132: To do as I do, in a word:
2133: So that, footloose, fancy free,
2134: You can experience Life, with me.
2135: Faust
2136: 
2137: This life of earth, its narrowness,
2138: Pains me, however I’m turned out,                            1545
2139: I’m too old to play about,
2140: Too young, still, to be passionless.
2141: What can the world bring me again?
2142: Abstain! You shall! You must! Abstain!
2143: That’s the eternal song                                      1550
2144: That in our ears, forever, rings
2145: The one, that, our whole life long,
2146: Every hour, hoarsely, sings.
2147: I wake in terror with the dawn,
2148: I cry, the bitterest tears, to see                           1555
2149: Day grant no wish of mine, not one
2150: As it passes by on its journey.
2151: Even presentiments of joy
2152: Ebb, in wilful depreciation:
2153: A thousand grimaces life employs                             1560
2154: To hinder me in creation.
2155: Then when night descends I must
2156: Stretch out, worried, on my bed:
2157: What comes to me is never rest,
2158: But some wild dream instead.                                 1565
2159: The God that lives inside my heart,
2160: Can rouse my innermost seeing:
2161: The one enthroned beyond my art,
2162: Can’t stir external being:
2163: And so existence is a burden: sated,                         1570
2164: Death’s desired, and Life is hated.
2165: 
2166: Mephistopheles
2167:

2171:

2174: Who, after the swift whirling dances,                        1575

2177: Before that enrapturing Spirit power!

2182: Liquid, drank not a drop, at midnight hour.   1580

2196: Then my other childhood feelings              1585
2197: Better times echoed, and allowed.
2198: So I curse whatever snares the soul,
2199: In its magical, enticing arms,
2200: Banishes it to this mournful hole,
2201: With dazzling, seductive charms!              1590
2202: Cursed be those high Opinions first,
2203: With which the mind entraps itself!
2204: Then glittering Appearance curse,
2205: In which the senses lose themselves!
2206: Curse what deceives us in our dreaming,       1595
2207: With thoughts of everlasting fame!
2208: Curse the flattery of ‘possessing’
2209: Wife and child, lands and name!
2210: Curse Mammon, when he drives us
2211: To bold acts to win our treasure:             1600

2213: For us to idle at our leisure!
2214: Curse the sweet juice of the grape!
2215: Curse the highest favours Love lets fall!

4277: Grateful for all the gifts of Christmas fare,               2700

4293: Formed an earthly angel within this.

4295: Filled her delicate breast,

4299: Why do I feel so deeply stirred?
4300: What do I seek? Why such a heavy heart?

4303: I urged myself on, to the deepest delight,
4304: And feel myself melt in Love’s dreaming flight!
4305: Are we the sport of every lightest breeze?
4306: And if she appeared at this instant,                        2725
4307: How to atone for being so indiscreet?

4373: Was faithful, to the grave,                            2760

4375: A golden goblet gave.
4376:

4378: At every feast it shone:
4379: His tears were brimming over,                          2765

4381:

4384: No wealth his heir denying,

4387: His knights around him, all,
4388: In his sea-girt turret,
4389: In his ancestral hall.
4390:

4393: Then threw the golden goblet
4394: Into the waves below.
4395:

4397: Sinking in the sea,                                                    2780

4400:

4404: I locked the chest when I was here before.

4407: And my mother’s granted a loan on it?

4409: I’m quite determined to open it.

4420: At once one looks so different.

4422: All that’s fine and good,
4423: But it’s discounted, in the end,                                       2800
4424: They praise us half in pity.
4425: To gold they tend,
4426: On gold depend,

4458: That woman’s a marvellous sense of smell,
4459: From nosing round in her prayer-book too well,
4460: And sniffs things, ever and again,
4461: To see if they’re holy or profane:                         2820

4469: Thinking: ‘Don’t look a gift horse in the mouth,

4471: He who left these fine things here.’               2830

4473: He’d scarcely let the game begin

5378: Part I Scene XIV: Forest and Cavern
5379: 
5380: 
5381: (Faust, alone.)
5382: 
5383: Sublime spirit, you gave me all, all,
5384: I asked for. Not in vain have you
5385: Revealed your face to me in flame.
5386: You gave me Nature’s realm of splendour,      3220
5387: With the power to feel it, and enjoy.
5388: Not merely as a cold, awed stranger,
5389: But allowing me to look deep inside,
5390: Like seeing into the heart of a friend.
5391: You lead the ranks of living creatures        3225
5392: Before me, showing me my brothers
5393: In the silent woods, the air, the water.
5394: And when the storm roars in the forest,
5395: When giant firs fell their neighbours,
5396: Crushing nearby branches in their fall,       3230
5397: Filling the hills with hollow thunder,
5398: You lead me to the safety of a cave,
5399: Show me my own self, and reveal
5400: Your deep, secret wonders in my heart.
5401: And when the pure Moon, to my eyes,           3235
5402: Rises, calming me, the silvery visions
5403: Of former times, drift all around me,
5404: From high cliffs, and moist thickets,
5405: Tempering thought’s austere delight.
5406: Oh, I know now that nothing can be            3240
5407: Perfect for Mankind. You gave me,
5408: With this joy, that brings me nearer,
5409: Nearer to the gods, a companion,
5410: Whom I can no longer do without,
5411: Though he is impudent, and chilling,
5412: Degrades me in my own eyes, and with          3245
5413: A word, a breath, makes your gifts nothing.
5414: He fans a wild fire in my heart,
5415: Always alive to that lovely form.
5416: So I rush from desire to enjoyment,
5417: And in enjoyment pine to feel desire.         3250

5507: As a stream pours from melted snow:
5508: You’ve so filled her heart, and now,
5509: Your stream again is shallow.                    3310

5512: To that poor little ape of flesh and blood,

5516: Over the old City wall, sees it lifting.

5558:

5564: So made the opportunity as well.

5571: Let me warm myself with her charms!

5574: The creature without aim or rest,
5575: A torrent in the rocks, still thundering down,     3350
5576: Foaming eagerly into the abyss?

5578: In a hut there, on a little Alpine field,
5579: So, her first homely life you’d find,
5580: Hidden there in that little world.                 3355

5582: Was not great enough,
5583: To grasp the cliffs, and take them,
5584: And crush them into dust!
5585: I still must undermine her peaceful life!          3360
5586: You, Hell, must have your sacrifice.
5587: Help, Devil, curtail the anxious moment brewing.
5588: What must be, let it be, and swiftly!
5589: Let her fate also fall on me,
5590: And she and I rush to ruin!                        3365
5591: 
5592: Mephistopheles
5593:

5595: Go in and comfort her, you fool!
5596: When a brain, like yours, no exit sees,
5597: It calls it the end of all things, too.
5598: Praise him who keeps his courage fresh!            3370
5599: Or you’ll soon get quite be-devilled, there.
5600: I find nothing in the world so tasteless,
5601: As a Devil, in despair.

5606: ‘My peace is gone,

6059: Part I Scene XIX: Night
6060: 
6061: (The Street in front of Gretchen’s door.)

6063: Valentine (A soldier, Gretchen’s brother.)
6064: 
6065: When I have sat, and heard the toasts,         3620
6066: Where everyone makes good his boasts,
6067: And comrades praised, to me, the flower
6068: Of maidenhood, and loud the hour,

6071: I sat in my own peace secure,
6072: Listening to the boastful roar,

6074: And take a full glass in my hand,
6075: Saying: ‘Each to his own, but I’ll             3630

6077: Who, to my Gretel, can compare

6080: Some cried out: ‘He’s quite correct,           3635
6081: She’s an ornament to all her sex.’

6449: Part I Scene XXI: Walpurgis Night
6450: 
6451: (The Hartz Mountains, in the region of Schierke and Elend.)
6452: 
6453: (Faust, Mephistopheles.)
6454: 
6455: Mephistopheles
6456: 
6457: Don’t you just long for a broomstick?                         3835
6458: I wish I’d the sturdiest goat to ride.
6459: Like this, the journey’s not so quick.
6460: 
6461: Faust
6462: 
6463: So long as my legs can do the trick,
6464: This knotted stick will do me fine.
6465: Why do we need a shorter way! –                               3840
6466: To wander this labyrinth of valleys,
6467: Climb all these cliffs and gullies,
6468: From which the waters ever spray,
6469: That’s a delight enchants the day!
6470: Spring stirs already in the birches,                          3845
6471: And even the fir tree knows it now:
6472: Shouldn’t our limbs feel it search us?
6473: 
6474: Mephistopheles
6475: 
6476: Truly, I don’t feel a thing!
6477: It’s winter in my body, still,
6478: On my path I want it frosty, snowing.                         3850
6479: How sadly the Moon’s imperfect circle
6480: With its red belated glow, is rising,
6481: So dim its light that at every step
6482: You scrape a rock, or else a tree!
6483: Ah, there, a will o’ the wisp leapt!                          3855
6484: It’s burning fiercely, now, I see.
6485: Hey! My friend! May I ask your aid?
6486: Would you like to give us a blaze?
6487: Be so good as to light us up the hill!
6488: Will O’ The Wisp
6489: 
6490: With respect, I hope I’ll still be able,                         3860
6491: To keep my Natural light quite stable:
6492: We usually zig-zag here, at will.
6493: 
6494: Mephistopheles
6495: 
6496: Ha, ha! He thinks to play the human game.
6497: Go straight along now, in the Devil’s name!
6498: Or I’ll blow out your flickering spark!                          3865
6499: 
6500: Will O’ The Wisp
6501: 
6502: You’re master of the house, I’ll remark,
6503: And yes, I’ll serve you willingly.
6504: But think! The mount is magically mad today,
6505: And if a will o’ the wisp should lead the way,
6506: You mustn’t judge things too precisely.                          3870

6508: Faust, Mephistopheles, The Will O’ The Wisp (In alternating song.)
6509: 
6510: We it seems, now find ourselves.
6511: In the sphere of dreams and magic,
6512: Do us honour, guide us well
6513: So our journey will be quick,
6514: Through the wide, deserted spaces!                               3875
6515: Tree on tree now shift their places,
6516: See how fast they open to us
6517: And the cliffs bow down before us,
6518: And their long and rocky noses,
6519: How they whistle and blow, for us!                               3880
6520: Through the stones, and through the grasses,
6521: Stream and streamlet, downward, hurrying.
6522: Is that rustling? Is that singing?
6523: Do I hear sweet lovers’ sighing,
6524: Heavenly days, is that their babbling?                           3885
6525: What we hope for, what we love!
6526: And the echoes, like the murmuring
6527: Of those other days, are ringing.
6528: ‘Too-wit! Too-woo!’ sounding nearer,
6529: Owl there, and jay, and plover,            3890
6530: Are they all awake above?
6531: A salamander in the scrub, he’s
6532: Long of leg, and fat of belly!
6533: And every root like a snake,
6534: Over sand and rock all bent,               3895
6535: Stretches with a strange intent,
6536: To scare us, of us prisoners make:
6537: From the gnarled and living mass,
6538: Stretching towards those who pass,
6539: Fibrous tentacles. And mice                3900
6540: Multi-coloured, lemming-wise,
6541: In the moss and in the heather!
6542: And all the fire-flies glowing,
6543: Crushed together, tightly crowding,
6544: In their tangled cohorts gather.           3905

6546: Or are we climbing up the hill?
6547: All seems spinning like a mill,
6548: Rocks and trees, with angry faces
6549: Lights, now, wandering in spaces,          3910
6550: Massing: swelling at their will.

6552: Mephistopheles
6553: 
6554: Grasp me bravely by the coat-tail!

6556: Where, astonished you can see,
6557: Mammon glowing furiously.                  3915

6564: Scenting abysses in their night.
6565: There vapour rises: here cloud sweeps,     3920
6566: Here the glow burns through the haze,
6567: Now like a fragile thread it creeps,
6568: Now like a coloured fountain plays.

6570: In a hundred veins, down the vales,       3925

6574: Like showers of golden sand,

7052: 
7053: What delight! What pain!
7054: I can’t turn from her, again.
7055: Strange, around her lovely throat,
7056: A single scarlet cord adorns her,
7057: Like a knife-cut, and no wider!                 4205
7058: Mephistopheles
7059: 
7060: That’s right! I see it too: and note,
7061: She can carry her head under her arm,
7062: Since Perseus did her that fatal harm.
7063: Always desire for that illusion!
7064: Come on, climb this bit of mountain:        4210
7065: It’s as lively as the Vienna Prater,
7066: And if no one’s deceiving me,
7067: I’m looking at a genuine theatre.
7068: You’re showing?
7069: 
7070: Servibilis
7071: 
7072:            It’ll be on again shortly.
7073: A fresh performance: last of seven.         4215
7074: That number, for us, is traditional.
7075: An amateur’s written it, and then
7076: It’s amateurs who perform it all.
7077: Forgive me, sir, if I break off here,
7078: Since I’m the amateur curtain-raiser.       4220
7079: 
7080: Mephistopheles
7081: 
7082: That I find you on the Blocksberg’s good,
7083: Since I find you exactly where I should.
7084: Part I Scene XXII: A Walpurgis Night’s Dream
7085: 
7086:                            Or
7087: 
7088:          Oberon and Titania’s Golden Wedding.
7089: 
7090:              An Interlude (Intermezzo)
7091: 
7092: Theatre Manager
7093: 
7094: You brave stagehands, of Weimar,
7095: Take a rest, at least for today.
7096: Ancient mountains, misty vales are,             4225
7097: All the scenery for our play.
7098: 
7099: Herald
7100: 
7101: Fifty years we’ve passed by,
7102: To make this wedding golden,
7103: But let some argument arise:
7104: There’s gold in it, for me, then.               4230
7105: 
7106: Oberon
7107: 
7108: Spirits, where I am, be seen:
7109: Appear, all, at this moment:
7110: Fairy King, and Fairy Queen,
7111: Renew their old intent.
7112: 
7113: Puck
7114: 
7115: Puck comes shooting through the air,            4235
7116: And moves his feet, in time:
7117: After him a hundred, there,
7118: Share his joyful rhyme.
7119: Ariel
7120: 
7121: Ariel conducts his singing
7122: In pure and heavenly tones:               4240
7123: Ugly faces greet its ringing,
7124: But also lovely ones.
7125: 
7126: Oberon
7127: 
7128: Partners if you’d get along,
7129: Learn then from the two of us!
7130: If we in pairs would love for long,       4245
7131: Someone needs to separate us.
7132: 
7133: Titania
7134: 
7135: The sulky man, the wilful wife,
7136: So they might know each other,
7137: I’d show him all the Northern ice,
7138: And show her the Equator.                 4250
7139: 
7140: The Whole Orchestra (Tutti. Very loud.)
7141: 
7142: From fly-snout and midge-nose,
7143: And all of their relations,
7144: Frog and cricket, too, there flow
7145: These musical vibrations!
7146: 
7147: Solo
7148: 
7149: See, the bagpipes on their way!           4255
7150: Made from a soap-bubble.
7151: Hear the snail’s-twaddle play
7152: Through its stumpy nozzle.
7153: Spirit (Newly formed.)
7154: 
7155: Spider’s-feet and toad’s-belly,
7156: With useless winglets to ’em!
7157: A little creature, it can’t be
7158: But it makes a little poem.
7159: 
7160: A Tiny Couple
7161: 
7162: Little steps and high leaps,
7163: Through honeydew and fragrance here,
7164: You still won’t do enough it seems,    4265
7165: To climb into the atmosphere.
7166: 
7167: A Curious Traveller
7168: 
7169: A masquerade of mockery?
7170: Do I dare to trust my eyes?
7171: Oberon, that fair divinity,
7172: Do I see him here, tonight?            4270
7173: 
7174: The Orthodox
7175: 
7176: He’s no tail, and not a claw!
7177: And yet it’s him, it’s true:
7178: Like the gods of Greece, I’m sure,
7179: He must be a devil too.
7180: 
7181: Northern Artist
7182: 
7183: What I capture here today,             4275
7184: In truth is only sketchy:
7185: Yet I prepare myself, someday
7186: For my Italian journey.
7187: Purist
7188: 
7189: Ah! My bad luck brings me here:
7190: Since I haven’t been invited!             4280
7191: Of all the witches to appear,
7192: Only two are powdered.
7193: 
7194: Young Witch
7195: 
7196: Powder like a petticoat
7197: On an old, grey witch you’ll see,
7198: While I sit naked on my goat,             4285
7199: And show a fine young body.
7200: 
7201: Married Woman
7202: 
7203: We have too much experience,
7204: To moan about you, here, then!

7207: 
7208: Orchestral Conductor
7209: 
7210: Fly-snout and midge-nose,
7211: Don’t swarm around the naked!
7212: Frog and cricket, too, all know
7213: Your time, and don’t mistake it!
7214: 
7215: A Wind-Vane (Swinging to one side.)
7216: 
7217: Society, as one would like it done:       4295
7218: True pure brides along the slope!
7219: And young fellows, one for one,
7220: People quite brimful of hope!
7221: The Wind-Vane (Swinging to the other side.)
7222: 
7223: And if the ground doesn’t split,
7224: And swallow everyone,                                           4300
7225: I’ll be so amazed at it,
7226: I’ll leap into hell at once.

7229: 
7230: As insects we appear,
7231: With little claws we’re nipping,
7232: To do Satan, our Papa,                                          4305
7233: Due honour as is fitting.
7234: 
7235: Hennings (August Von Hennings, a literary enemy.)
7236: 
7237: See them, packed in a crowd,
7238: Naïve, together, poking fun!
7239: At last, they’ll even say, aloud,
7240: Their hearts were blameless ones.                               4310
7241: 
7242: Musagete (Controller of the Muses: Greek – epithet of Apollo)
7243: 
7244: Among this witches’ crew,
7245: I’d gladly lose my way:
7246: They’re easier to manage, too
7247: Than Muses, any day.
7248: 
7249: Former ‘Genius of the Age’
7250: 
7251: One was someone, among real folk.                               4315
7252: Come on, then: I can hold my end up!
7253: Like Germany’s Parnassus, look,
7254: The Blocksberg’s summit’s broad enough.
7255: Curious Traveller (Nicolai)
7256: 
7257: Say, who’s that haughty man?
7258: He walks with such proud steps.              4320
7259: He sniffs as only a sniffer-out can.
7260: ‘He smells out Jesuits.’
7261: 
7262: A Crane (Lavater)
7263: 
7264: I like to fish among the clear
7265: And the muddy levels:
7266: So the pious man appears                     4325
7267: Mixing with the devils.
7268: 
7269: A Child of This World (Goethe himself.)
7270: 
7271: To the pious man, as I’m aware,
7272: Every place is fitting,
7273: So you build, on the Blocksberg here,
7274: Many a house of meeting.                     4330
7275: 
7276: A Dancer
7277: 
7278: Does some new choir succeed?
7279: I hear a distant drum.
7280: ‘No! It’s the booming in the reeds,
7281: Of bitterns, in unison.’
7282: 
7283: A Dancing Master
7284: 
7285: How they lift their legs, this lot!          4335
7286: As best they can, they all take flight!
7287: The cripples skip, the clumsy hop,
7288: And don’t care at all what they look like.
7289: A Fiddle-Player
7290: 
7291: The ragged mob all hate so much,
7292: They’d gladly crush the others.      4340
7293: Here the bagpipe draws them, just
7294: As Orpheus’ lyre the creatures.

7296: The Dogmatist
7297: 
7298: I won’t declare it’s madness, now,
7299: Or show myself too critical.
7300: The devil must exist somehow,        4345
7301: Or how could we act the devil?
7302: 
7303: The Idealist
7304: 
7305: The fantasy in my mind,
7306: For once, is too despotic.
7307: Truly, if I am all, I find
7308: Today I’m idiotic!                   4350
7309: 
7310: The Realist
7311: 
7312: Here’s real pain, at hand,
7313: It annoys me so to see it:
7314: For the first time, here I stand,
7315: Unsteady, on my feet.
7316: 
7317: A Believer in the Supernatural
7318:

7321: Since from the devil I infer
7322: Some much more virtuous spirit.

7325: These little flames a-hunting go,

7338:

7391: Part I Scene XXIII: Gloomy Day
7392: 
7393: (A Field. Faust, Mephistopheles.)
7394: 
7395: Faust
7396: 
7397: In misery! Despair! Wandering wretchedly on the face of the earth, for ages,
7398: and now imprisoned! That kind, unfortunate creature, locked up in prison as
7399: a criminal, and lost in torment! To this! This! – Treacherous, worthless
7400: spirit, you hid it from me! – Stand there, then! Roll the devil’s eyes in your
7401: head, in anger! Stand there, and defy me with your unbearable presence!
7402: Imprisoned! In irredeemable misery! Delivered up to evil spirits, and the
7403: judgement of unfeeling men! And you’ve troubled me meanwhile with
7404: tasteless diversions, concealed her growing misery from me, and left her
7405: helpless in the face of ruin!
7406: 
7407: Mephistopheles
7408: 
7409: She is not the first.
7410: 
7411: Faust
7412: 
7413: Dog! Loathsome Monster! – Change him, infinite Spirit! Change the worm
7414: into his dog-form, in which he often liked to scamper in front of me, at
7415: night, rolling at the feet of the unsuspecting traveller, and clambering on his
7416: shoulders when he fell. Change him into his favourite likeness, so he can
7417: crawl on his belly in the sand in front of me, and I can trample him,
7418: depraved thing, under my feet! – ‘Not the first!’ – Misery! Misery! That no
7419: human spirit can grasp. That more than one being should sink into the depth
7420: of this wretchedness: that the first, writhing in its death-pangs, under the
7421: eyes of Eternal Forgiveness, did not expiate the guilt of all the others! It
7422: pierces to the marrow of my bones, the misery of this one being – and you
7423: smile calmly at the fate of thousands!
7424: 
7425: Mephistopheles
7426: 
7427: Now we’re out of our wits again, already, at the point where men’s brains
7428: are cracked. Why did you enter into partnership with us, if you can’t go
7429: through with it? Would you take wing, and yet be free of dizziness? Did we
7430: thrust ourselves on you, or you on us?
7431: Faust
7432: 
7433: Don’t gnash your greedy jaws at me! It disgusts me! – Great and glorious
7434: Spirit, you who revealed yourself to me, nobly, who know my heart and
7435: soul, why shackle me to this disgraceful companion, who feeds on injury,
7436: and at the last on ruin?
7437: 
7438: Mephistopheles
7439: 
7440: Have you finished?
7441: 
7442: Faust
7443: 
7444: Save her, or woe to you! May the weightiest curse fall on you for a thousand
7445: ages!
7446: 
7447: Mephistopheles
7448: 
7449: I can’t undo the bonds of the Avenger, nor loose his bolts. – ‘Save her!’ –
7450: Who was it dragged her to ruin? I or you?
7451: 
7452: (Faust looks around, wildly.)
7453: 
7454: Would you grasp the lightning? A good thing it has not been allowed you
7455: miserable mortals! To crush the innocent one who replies is the tyrant’s way
7456: to free oneself of an embarrassment.
7457: 
7458: Faust
7459: 
7460: Take me to her! She shall be freed!
7461: 
7462: Mephistopheles
7463: 
7464: And the danger you expose yourself to? Be aware, the guilty blood from
7465: your hands lies on the town. Avenging spirits hover over the place of death,
7466: and lie in wait for the murderer’s return.
7467: Faust
7468: 
7469: And not from yours, too? Murder, and death in this world, be on you,
7470: monster! Take me there, I say, and free her.
7471: 
7472: Mephistopheles
7473: 
7474: I’ll take you: listen to what I can do! Have I all the powers of heaven and
7475: earth? I’ll confuse the jailor’s mind: you take possession of the key, and
7476: bring her out, hand in human hand! I’ll keep watch: magic horses are ready:
7477: I’ll carry you away. That, I can do.
7478: 
7479: Faust
7480: 
7481: Away!

7489: 
7490: Mephistopheles
7491: 
7492: I don’t know what they’re cooking and brewing.                      4400

7509: Part I Scene XXV: A Dungeon
7510: 
7511: (Faust, with a bunch of keys and a lamp, in front of an iron door.)
7512: 
7513: A long-forgotten shudder grips me,                                    4405
7514: I’m gripped by all of Mankind’s misery,
7515: Here behind these damp walls, she
7516: Lives: and all her guilt’s illusory.
7517: Do I tremble, then, to free her!
7518: Do I dread, once more, to see her!                                    4410
7519: On! Fear adds to death’s proximity.
7520: 
7521: (He grips the lock. She sings within.)
7522: 
7523: My mother, the whore
7524: She killed me!
7525: My father, the rogue,
7526: He gnawed me!                                                         4415
7527: Little sister alone
7528: Laid out the bone
7529: In the cool of the clay:
7530: Then I was a sweet bird on the stone.
7531: Fly away! Fly away!                                                   4420

7534:

7536: Hears the chains, the straw’s rustling.

7751:

7760: From here to everlasting rest,                 4540
7761: And not a step further would

7763:

7767: 
7768: Margaret
