7772: To be forced to beg is a bitter existence,
7773: And cursed too with an evil conscience!
7774: To wander among strangers, bitter,
7775: And even then I’d still be captured!
7776: 
7777: Faust
7778: 
7779: I’ll stay beside you.                          4550
7780: Margaret
7781: 
7782: Quickly! Quickly!
7783: Save my poor baby!
7784: Away! Down the ridge,
7785: Now, by the brook,
7786: Over the bridge,                            4555
7787: Into the wood,
7788: Left, where the plank is,
7789: There, in the pool.
7790: Seize it now: you!
7791: It’s trying to rise,                        4560
7792: It’s moving still!
7793: Save it! Save it!
7794: 
7795: Faust
7796: 
7797: Be sensible!
7798: Only one step, and then you’re free!
7799: 
7800: Margaret
7801: 
7802: If we were on the mountain, only!           4565
7803: There my mother sits, on a stone,
7804: And oh, the cold, it grips me!
7805: There my mother sits on a stone,
7806: And wags her head, so heavy.
7807: No sign, no nod, for me, I’m sure           4570
7808: Her sleep’s so long: she’ll wake no more.
7809: She slept, while we took our pleasure.
7810: That was such a time to treasure!
7811: 
7812: Faust
7813: 
7814: Here all’s useless, speech or prayer:
7815: I’ll take you from this place: I’ll dare.   4575
7816: 
7817: Margaret
7818: 
7819: Let me alone! No, no force!
7820: Don’t grip me so murderously, oh,
7821: I’ve done all else to please you so.
7822: 
7823: Faust
7824: 
7825: The day breaks! Dearest! Dearest!
7826: 
7827: Margaret
7828: 
7829: Day! Yes, it’s dawn! The last I’ll see:                     4580
7830: My wedding day, that was to be!
7831: Tell no one you’ve been with Gretchen. Ah, bright glance!
7832: It’s done with: all in vain!
7833: We two will meet again:                                     4585
7834: But not in the dance.
7835: The crowd gather, without speech.
7836: The streets, the square,
7837: Can’t hold them, there.
7838: The bell tolls, the wand breaks.                            4590
7839: Now, they seize and tie me!
7840: I’m dragged already to the block.
7841: The blade that quivers over me,
7842: Has quivered before over every neck.
7843: Silent the world, now, as the grave!                        4595
7844: 
7845: Faust
7846: 
7847: Oh, would that I’d never seen the light!
7848: 
7849: Mephistopheles (Appears outside.)
7850: 
7851: Away! Or you’ll be lost, tonight.
7852: Useless staying and praying! Chattering!
7853: The horses are shivering,
7854: The dawn breaks, clear.                                     4600
7855: Margaret
7856: 
7857: What rises in the doorway, here?
7858: Him! Him! Send him away!
7859: Why is he here in this holy place?
7860: He wants me!
7861: 
7862: Faust
7863: 
7864:                              You will live!
7865: 
7866: Margaret
7867: 
7868: God of Judgement! To you, myself I give!       4605
7869: 
7870: Mephistopheles (To Faust)
7871: 
7872: Come! Now! Or I leave you both to stew.
7873: 
7874: Margaret
7875: 
7876: Father, save me! I belong to you!
7877: Angels! In Holy Company,
7878: Draw round me: guard me!
7879: Heinrich! For you, I fear.                     4610
7880: 
7881: Mephistopheles
7882:

7884:

7886: 
7887:             She is saved!

7897: Part II Act I Scene I: A Pleasant Landscape
7898: 
7899: (Faust is lying on flowery turf, tired and restless, trying to sleep. A circle of
7900: tiny, graceful spirits hovers round him.)
7901: 
7902: Ariel (Chanting, accompanied by Aeolian Harps.)
7903: 
7904: When the springtime blossoms, falling,
7905: Shower down, and cover all things,
7906: When the fields with greener blessing                                      4615
7907: Dazzle all the world of earthlings,
7908: Little elves, but great in spirit,
7909: Haste to help, where help they can,
7910: And, be he holy, be he wicked,
7911: Pity they the luckless man.                                                4620
7912: 
7913: You, hovering in airy circles, round his head
7914: Show yourselves in proud elf-form, instead,
7915: Calm all the fierce resistance of his heart,
7916: Remove the bitter barbs of sharp remorse,
7917: Free him from past terrors, by your art.                                   4625
7918: Four are the watches night makes in its course,
7919: At once, now, mercifully, let the dark depart.
7920: Let his head sink down on pillow’s coolness,
7921: Next sprinkle him with dew from Lethe’s stream:
7922: Then let his joints be free of cramps and stiffness,                       4630
7923: So that he’s strong enough to greet day’s gleam:
7924: Elves exert your sweetest right,
7925: Return him to the holy light!
7926: 
7927: Choir (Singly, and two or more, alternately and together.)
7928: 
7929: When the balmy breezes smother
7930: All the green-encircled land,                                              4635
7931: Sweetly fragrant and mist-covered,
7932: Twilight gathers all around.
7933: Sweet peace then whispers softly,
7934: Rocks the heart on childhood’s shores,
7935: And on the eyelids, tired and weary,
7936: Closes daylight’s golden doors.
7937: Here the night’s already passing,
7938: Sacred stars set, star by star,
7939: Great lights, and the lesser glittering,
7940: Sparkling near, and gleaming far:           4645
7941: Sparkling, where the lake reflects her,
7942: Gleaming bright in cloudless height,
7943: Protecting the deep bliss of rest, there,
7944: Moon, in splendour, rules the night.
7945: 
7946: The hours have vanished now, already        4650
7947: Joy and pain have flown away,
7948: You are whole! Recover, wholly:
7949: Trust the sight of breaking day.
7950: Greening valleys, swelling hills there,
7951: Rise from out their shadowy sleep:          4655
7952: And, drifting in its waves of silver,
7953: On to harvest, flows the wheat.
7954: 
7955: Wish then, to achieve your wishes,
7956: Gaze up, at the brightness there!
7957: You are lightly tangled: this is            4660
7958: Sleep, a shell, so now emerge!
7959: Don’t delay, walk bravely, tall,
7960: When the crowd waits, hesitating:
7961: The noblest man achieves his all,
7962: By seeing, and then, swiftly, taking.       4665
7963: 
7964: 
7965: Ariel
7966: 
7967: Listen! Hear the hour nearing!
7968: Ringing out to spirit-hearing,
7969: Now, the new day is appearing.
7970: Doors of stone creak and chatter,
7971: Phoebus’ wheels roll and clatter,           4670
7972: What a din the daylight’s bringing!
7973: Trombone- and trumpeting,
7974: Eyes amazed, and ears ringing,
7975: The Unheard drops out of hearing.
7976: Slip into the flowers presence,                       4675
7977: Deeper, deeper, lie there silent,
7978: In the pebbles, where the leaves bend:
7979: If it strikes you, you’ll be deafened.
7980: 
7981: Faust
7982: 
7983: Life’s pulses beating now, with new existence,
7984: Greet the mild ethereal half-light round me:          4680
7985: You, Earth, stood firm tonight, as well: I sense
7986: Your breath is quickening all the things about me,
7987: Already, with that joy you give, beginning
7988: To stir the strengthening resolution in me,
7989: That strives, forever, towards highest Being. –       4685
7990: Now the world unfolds, in half-light’s gleam,
7991: The wood’s alive, its thousand harmonies singing,
7992: While through the valleys, misted ribbons stream:
7993: And heavenly light now penetrates the deep:
7994: Twigs, branches shoot, with fresher life it seems,    4690
7995: From fragrant gulfs, where they were sunk in sleep:
7996: Colour on colour lifts now from the ground,
7997: As leaf and flower with trembling dewdrops weep –
7998: And a paradise reveals itself, all round.
7999: Gaze upwards! – The vast mountain heights             4695
8000: Already with the solemn hour resound:
8001: They are the first to enjoy the eternal light
8002: That later, for us, will work its way below.
8003: Now, to the sloping Alpine meadows bright,
8004: It gives a fresh clarity, a newer glow,               4700
8005: And step by step it reaches us down here: –
8006: It blazes out! – Ah, already blinded, though
8007: I turn away, my eyesight wounded, pierced.
8008: So it is, when to the thing we yearn for
8009: The highest wish so intimately rehearsed,             4705
8010: We find fulfilment opening wide the door:
8011: And then, from eternal space, there breaks
8012: A flood of flame, we stand amazed before:
8013: We wished to set the torch of life ablaze,
8014: A sea of fire consumes us, and such fire!             4710
8015: Love, is it, then? Or hate? This fierce embrace,
8016: The joy and pain of alternating pyres,
8017: So that, gazing back to earth again,
8018: We seek to veil ourselves in youth’s desire.
8019: Let the sun shine on, behind me, then!               4715
8020: The waterfall that splits the cliffs’ broad edge,
8021: I gaze at with a growing pleasure, when
8022: A thousand torrents plunge from ledge to ledge,
8023: And still a thousand more pour down that stair,
8024: Spraying the bright foam skywards from their beds.   4720
8025: And in lone splendour, through the tumult there,
8026: The rainbow’s arch of colour, bending brightly,
8027: Is clearly marked, and then dissolved in air,
8028: Around it the cool showers, falling lightly.
8029: There the efforts of mankind they mirror.            4725
8030: Reflect on it, you’ll understand precisely:
8031: We live our life amongst refracted colour.
8032: Part II Act I Scene II: The Emperor’s Castle: The Throne Room
8033: 
8034: (A council of state waits for the Emperor. Trumpets.)
8035: 
8036: (Enter court attendants of all kinds, splendidly dressed. The Emperor
8037: approaches the throne: the Astrologer is to his right.)
8038: 
8039: The Emperor
8040: 
8041: I greet you all, the loved, and true,
8042: Gathered here from far and wide: -
8043: I see a wise man’s at my side,                                          4730
8044: But where on earth’s the fool?
8045: 
8046: Attendant
8047: 
8048: Right behind your mantle there,
8049: He suddenly tumbled on the stair,
8050: They dragged away the pile of fat.
8051: Dead: or drunk? No man knows that.                                      4735
8052: 
8053: A Second Attendant
8054: 
8055: At once, and at a wondrous pace,
8056: Another came to take his place.
8057: Quite extravagantly dressed,
8058: Yet troubling, since he’s so grotesque:
8059: Guards closed the door in his face,                                     4740
8060: Their halberds held crosswise too –
8061: Yet here he comes, the daring fool!
8062: 
8063: Mephistopheles (Kneeling in front of the throne.)
8064: 
8065: What is cursed, and yet is welcomed?
8066: What’s desired, yet chased away?
8067: What’s always carefully defended?                                       4745
8068: What’s abused: condemned, I say?
8069: What do you not dare appeal to?
8070: What will all, happily, hear named?
8071: What stands on the step before you?
8072: What’s banished from here, all the same?                 4750
8073: 
8074: The Emperor
8075: 
8076: For once, at least, spare us your babble!
8077: This is no time or place for riddles,
8078: They’re a matter for these gentlemen. –
8079: Solve it! I’ll gladly hear it all again.
8080: I fear my old fool’s wandered far in space:              4755
8081: Come to my side, here, and take his place.
8082: 
8083: (Mephistopheles places himself on the Emperor’s left.)
8084: 
8085: Murmurs From the Crowd
8086: 
8087: A newer fool – for newer cares –
8088: Where’s he from? – How’d he get there? –
8089: The old one fell – He’s all done in –
8090: He was fat – Now this one’s thin –                       4760
8091: The Emperor
8092: 
8093: So now, my faithful and beloved,
8094: Welcome here from near and far!
8095: We meet beneath a lucky star,
8096: Since health and luck are written above.
8097: But tell me, why in days like these,                     4765
8098: When we’ve conquered care,
8099: And carnival masks are all our wear,
8100: And delightful things are waiting,
8101: We trouble ourselves with debating?
8102: Yet since you say we have to do it,                      4770
8103: It’s settled then, and we’ll go to it.
8104: 
8105: The Chancellor
8106: 
8107: The highest virtue, like a sacred halo
8108: Circles the Emperor’s head: and so
8109: He alone may validly exercise it:
8110: Justice! – All men love and prize it,                    4775
8111: What all ask, yet wish they could do without,
8112: The people look to him to hand it out.
8113: But ah! What help can human wit deliver,
8114: Or kindly heart, or willing hand, if fever
8115: Rages wildly through the state, and evil          4780
8116: Itself is broodingly preparing evil?
8117: Look about, from this height’s extreme,
8118: Across the realm: it seems like some bad dream,
8119: Where one deformity acts on another,
8120: Where lawlessness by law is furthered,            4785
8121: And an age of crime is discovered.
8122: Here one steals cattle, there, a wife,
8123: Cross, cup and candlestick, from the altar,
8124: And boasts of it for many a year,
8125: His skin’s intact, and so’s his life.             4790
8126: Then they take their claims to court
8127: The judge, in pomp, on his high cushion,
8128: Meanwhile there grows a furious roar,
8129: From swelling tides of revolution.
8130: They insist it’s crime and disgrace,              4795
8131: With their accomplices beside them,
8132: And ‘Guilty!’ is the verdict in a case,
8133: Only where Innocence is its own defence.
8134: So all the world will slash and chop,
8135: Destroying just what suits themselves:            4800
8136: How then can that true sense develop
8137: That shows the morally acceptable?
8138: At last the well-intentioned man
8139: Yields to the bribe, the flatterer:
8140: And the judge who can’t convict, is hand          4805
8141: In hand with the criminal offender.
8142: I’ve painted in black, but I’d rather draw
8143: Its image in the deeper colour that I saw.
8144: 
8145: (Pause)
8146: 
8147: The conclusion’s inescapable:
8148: If all men suffer when all cause trouble,         4810
8149: Then His Majesty himself is harmed.
8150: The Commander in Chief
8151: 
8152: How riotous things are in this wild age!
8153: They all lash out, and are lashed, these days,
8154: And everyone is deaf to all command.
8155: The citizen behind his wall,                            4815
8156: The knight in his cliff-top tower,
8157: Have sworn to defy us all,
8158: And hold fast to their power.
8159: The impatient mercenaries
8160: Impetuously demand their pay,                           4820
8161: And if we owed them less, already
8162: They’d be off, and march away.
8163: If one forbids what all desire,
8164: He’s disturbed a hornet’s nest:
8165: The kingdom, they should keep entire,                   4825
8166: Is plundered, and distressed.
8167: They’d like to wreak a wild disorder,
8168: Half the world has been dissolved:
8169: There are still kings beyond our border,
8170: But none of them think they’re involved.                4830
8171: 
8172: The Treasurer
8173: 
8174: In allies, then, who’d put their trust!
8175: The subsidies they promised us,
8176: Like water pipes are all blocked up.
8177: And, Sire, in all your wide estate,
8178: Who’s benefited from the take?                   4835
8179: Wherever you go, there’s some new pup,
8180: Who declares his independence.
8181: We watch, while they carry on:
8182: We’ve given away our rights, and hence,
8183: No rights are left for us, not one.                     4840
8184: Our parties too, however called,
8185: Can’t be depended on today:
8186: They like to praise, and blame: it’s all
8187: Impartial both their love and hate.
8188: They’re resting: they take cover,
8189: The Ghibelline, and Guelph.                             4845
8190: Now, who’ll help his neighbour?
8191: Each man just helps himself.
8192: The golden doors are fastened tight,
8193: Men scrape and scratch and glean, all right,         4850
8194: But our coffers still are empty.
8195: 
8196: The Steward
8197: 
8198: What evils, too, I must endure!
8199: We try to save each day, I’m sure,
8200: But every day sees greater need:                     4855
8201: So, daily, some new torment’s mine.
8202: The cooks, alas, have all they want:
8203: Boar, pheasant, hare and venison,
8204: Ducks and peacocks, chickens, geese,
8205: Payment in kind, and guaranteed,
8206: They keep coming all the time,                       4860
8207: But in the end we’re short of wine.
8208: Though cask on cask once filled the cellar,
8209: The best of vintages, and names, there,
8210: These noble lords can drink forever,
8211: And haven’t left a single drop.                      4865
8212: The council too must have their fill,
8213: They grasp their tankards tight until,
8214: Under the table, they have to stop.
8215: Now I’ll count the cost, you’ll see,
8216: The moneylenders won’t spare me,                     4870
8217: The advances that they give gladly,
8218: Will eat the future years, on top.
8219: Pigs don’t have time to fatten: instead
8220: Men seize the pillows from your bed,
8221: Even the bread from your table’s gone.               4875
8222: 
8223: The Emperor (After reflection, to Mephistopheles.)
8224: 
8225: Fool, do you know anything else that’s wrong?
8226: Mephistopheles
8227: 
8228: Me? Nothing at all! I see splendour, as I must,
8229: Around me, of you and yours! – Lack trust,
8230: Where Majesty commands so, without question,
8231: Where ready force scatters the enemy faction?               4880
8232: Where strong wills, with wit to understand,
8233: Active and various, are all at hand?
8234: What, for some evil purpose, could combine,
8235: For darkness, then, where such stars shine?
8236: 
8237: Murmurs
8238: 
8239: Here’s a rogue – who understands –                          4885
8240: He’ll tell lies – as long as he can –
8241: I wonder too – what lies behind –
8242: And what’s in front? – A project of some kind –
8243: 
8244: Mephistopheles
8245: 
8246: In this world, what isn’t lacking, somewhere, though?
8247: Sometimes it’s this, or that: here what’s missing’s gold.   4890
8248: True you can’t just rake it up from the floor,
8249: But wisdom knows the mines where one gets more.
8250: In mountain veins, foundation walls,
8251: Coined and un-coined golden hoards,
8252: And ask me, now, who’ll bring it to the light:              4895
8253: One gifted with Mind’s power and Nature’s might.
8254: 
8255: The Chancellor
8256: 
8257: Mind and Nature – don’t speak to Christians so.
8258: That’s why men burn atheists, below,
8259: Such speech is dangerous, all right,
8260: Nature is sin, and Mind’s the devil,                        4900
8261: It harbours within it, Doubt, that evil,
8262: Their misshapen hermaphrodite.

8264: Two kinds of men are still at hand
8265: Worthy alone to defend the throne:                          4905
8266: The Saints are they, and the Knights:
8267: They enter life’s uncertain fights,
8268: Rewards of Church and State they own:
8269: Firm in their resistance, check
8270: The confused aims of everyman.                        4910
8271: No, Nature and Mind are heretics!
8272: Wizards! Ruining town and land.
8273: And you, with brazen impudence still
8274: Invoke them here in this high circle:
8275: You’re fostering the corrupted will,                  4915
8276: Fools are always hand in hand.
8277: 
8278: Mephistopheles
8279: 
8280: By this I recognise a most learned lord!
8281: What you can’t feel lies miles abroad,
8282: What you can’t grasp, you think, is done with too.
8283: What you don’t count on can’t be true,                4920
8284: What you can’t weigh won’t weigh, of old,
8285: What you don’t coin: that can’t be gold.
8286: 
8287: The Emperor
8288: 
8289: You won’t sort out our faults like that,
8290: Will Lenten sermons make men fat?
8291: I’m tired of the eternal ‘if and when’:               4925
8292: We’re short of gold, well fine, so fetch some then.
8293: 
8294: Mephistopheles
8295: 
8296: I’ll fetch what you wish, and I’ll fetch more:
8297: Easy it’s true, but then easy things weigh more:
8298: It’s there already, yet how we might achieve it,
8299: That’s the tricky thing, knowing how to seize it.     4930
8300: Just think how, in those times of consternation,
8301: When a human flood drowned land and nation,
8302: People were so terrified, everywhere,
8303: They hid their treasures, here and there.
8304: So it was when mighty Rome held sway,                 4935
8305: And so it goes on, yesterday and today.
8306: Still buried in the earth, why, there it is:
8307: The earth is the Emperor’s, so it’s his.
8308: 
8309: The Treasurer
8310: 
8311: For a Fool his aim’s not out of sight:
8312: It’s true, that’s an old Imperial right.                4940
8313: 
8314: The Chancellor
8315: 
8316: Satan lays out his gilded nets, for you,

8318: 
8319: The Steward
8320: 
8321: Only bring them to court: I’ll welcome the sight,

8323: 
8324: The Commander in Chief
8325: 
8326: The Fool’s clever, to promise what each of us needs:    4945
8327: A soldier will never ask from whence it all proceeds.
8328: 
8329: Mephistopheles

8331: If you think I’m cheating you, maybe,

8334: So ask him: how are the Heavens now?                    4950

8336: Murmurs
8337: 
8338: Two rogues, there – already known –
8339: Fool and Dreamer – so near the throne –

8341: The Fool plays – the Wise Man speaks, in time –
8342: The Astrologer (Speaks, with Mephistopheles prompting him.)
8343: 
8344: The Sun, himself, he is of purest gold:                       4955
8345: Mercury, messenger, of riches told:
8346: Venus has bewitched you all, and she
8347: Looks on you, soon and late, quite lovingly:
8348: The chaste Moon’s mood holds fast:
8349: Mars won’t harm: his strength won’t last:                     4960
8350: And Jupiter remains the loveliest sight:
8351: While Saturn’s great, but far away and slight.
8352: His metal we don’t greatly venerate,
8353: Light of worth, though leaden in its weight.
8354: Yes! When Sun and Moon are conjoined fine,                    4965
8355: Silver and gold will make the whole world shine:
8356: The rest as well in turn are all achieved,
8357: Palaces, gardens proud, and rosy cheeks:
8358: All this he brings this highly knowledgeable man:
8359: He can deliver, too, what nobody else here can.               4970
8360: 
8361: The Emperor
8362: 
8363: The words they say, I hear them twice,

8365: 
8366: Murmurs
8367:

8373: Mephistopheles
8374: 
8375: They stand around: they’re all amazed,
8376: They don’t trust what can be found,
8377: One babbles about deadly nightshade,
8378: The other of some jet-black hound.                            4980
8379: What matter if one thinks I’m jesting,
8380: Or another calls it sorcery,
8381: If the soles of their feet are itching,
8382: If their firm step totters towards me.
8383: All can feel the secret working                4985
8384: Of Nature’s everlasting power,
8385: And from its deepest lurking,
8386: A living vein shall rise and flower.
8387: When every member twitches,
8388: When all looks strange to your eyes,           4990
8389: Make up your minds, be delvers,
8390: Here the players, there the prize!
8391: 
8392: Murmurs
8393: 
8394: It’s like a lead-weight on my feet –
8395: My arm’s swollen – but then, it’s gouty –
8396: There’s a tickle here in my big toe –          4995
8397: All the way down my back it goes –
8398: From these signs, I’d say we’re near

8400: 
8401: The Emperor
8402: 
8403: Quick then! Don’t slope off there!
8404: Let’s test your froth of lies,                 5000
8405: Show us, all, this rarest prize.
8406: I’ll lay down the sword and sceptre,
8407: With my own noble hands, as well,
8408: If you don’t lie, complete the work myself,
8409: And, if you lie, then send you down to Hell!   5005
8410: 
8411: Mephistopheles
8412: 
8413: I’ll find the way there anyway –
8414: Yet I really can’t exaggerate
8415: What’s lying round ownerless, everywhere.
8416: The farmer, ploughing the furrows, lays bare
8417: A crock of gold the clods unfold:              5010
8418: Seeks saltpetre from damp limy walls,
8419: And finds there golden rolls of gold,
8420: In his poor hands: frightened by all.
8421: What caverns exist to be blown open,
8422: Through what shafts and cuttings then,            5015
8423: Burrow those gold-divining men,
8424: Those neighbours of the Underworld!
8425: Secure in vast ancient cellars, find,
8426: Golden plates, bowls, cups for wine,
8427: In rows, and heaps where they were hurled:        5020
8428: Goblets fashioned out of rubies,
8429: And if they wants to try their uses,
8430: Beside them there’s the ancient fluid.
8431: Yet – I would trust the expert though –
8432: The wooden casks rotted long ago,                 5025
8433: The wine makes tartar, in the liquid.
8434: Not just gold, and jewels, fine
8435: But the essence then of noble wine
8436: Terror hides, and night, as stark.
8437: So quiz the wise untiringly:                      5030
8438: It’s trivial, by day, to see:
8439: Mystery: houses in the dark.
8440: 
8441: The Emperor
8442: 
8443: See to it then! What use is it out of sight?
8444: Whatever’s valuable must see the light.
8445: Who knows a rogue for certain but by day?         5035
8446: At night all cows are black, and cats are grey.
8447: The pots down there, full of golden weight –
8448: Drive your plough, and, ploughing, excavate.
8449: 
8450: Mephistopheles
8451: 
8452: Take hoe and spade: and dig yourself,
8453: Labouring will make you great,                    5040
8454: A herd of golden calves, you’ll help
8455: To rise from out their buried state.
8456: Then with delight, without delay,
8457: You can, yourself, your love array:
8458: Glittering colours, shining gems, will best       5045
8459: Enhance your majesty, and her loveliness.
8460: The Emperor
8461: 
8462: Quick then, quick! How slow it always is!
8463: 
8464: The Astrologer (Prompted by Mephistopheles.)
8465: 
8466: Sire, restrain your urgent passion, please.
8467: First let all your pleasant pastimes go:
8468: Distracted natures won’t achieve the goal.            5050
8469: First we must atone for them in quiet,
8470: Lower things are gained by the higher.
8471: Who wants the good, must first be good:
8472: Who wants delight, must calm the blood:
8473: Who longs for wine, treads ripened grapes:            5055
8474: Who hopes for miracles, strengthens then his faith.
8475: 
8476: The Emperor
8477: 
8478: So let the time be passed in merriment!
8479: Ash Wednesday will achieve our grave intent.
8480: And we can celebrate, wild Carnival,
8481: More riotously, meanwhile, after all.                 5060

8485: Mephistopheles
8486: 
8487: How merit and luck are linked together
8488: These fools can’t see, no, not a one:
8489: If they’d the Philosopher’s Stone, as ever,
8490: There’d lack a philosopher for the stone.
8491: Part II Act I Scene III: A Spacious Hall with Adjoining Rooms
8492: 
8493: (Arranged and decorated for a Carnival Masque.)

8495: Herald
8496: 
8497: In our German lands, fear no evil,                              5065
8498: Dance of Death or Fool, or Devil:
8499: There’s a cheerful feast, here: wait.
8500: Our Sire, on his Roman travels,
8501: Has, for his profit, and our revels,
8502: Crossed the highest Alpine levels,                              5070
8503: And gained himself a happier State.
8504: The Emperor kissed the holy slipper,
8505: First, won sovereign rights, and as,
8506: He was gifted with the crown, there,
8507: Accepted a fool’s cap, for us.                                  5075
8508: We’re all newly born, now:
8509: Every sophisticated man,
8510: Pulls it snug over ears and brow:
8511: He seems a poor fool, but he’ll vow
8512: To wear it wisely as he can.                                    5080
8513: I see they’re gathering already,
8514: Hesitant alone, or paired off intimately:
8515: Chorus on chorus pushing through.
8516: In, and out, quite undeterred:
8517: And end up where they were before, too.                         5085
8518: With its hundred thousand scenes of the absurd,
8519: The World itself is just one giant Fool.
8520: Flower Girls (Singing, accompanied by mandolins.)
8521: 
8522: Dressed to win your praises,
8523: We are here tonight,
8524: Young Florentine ladies,                                   5090
8525: At the German Court of light.
8526:

8528: To adorn our tawny hair:
8529: Silken threads, silken gear,
8530: They play their own part here.                             5095
8531:

8533: Worth your praise, without a doubt,
8534: Our shining-flowers, by hand we sew,
8535: So they bloom year in, year out.
8536: 
8537: All kinds of coloured snippets,                            5100
8538: Placed with perfect symmetry:
8539: You might mock us bit by bit, yes,
8540: But the whole attracts you see.
8541:

8543: Flower Girls, and very smart:                       5105

8584: A marvellous flower grew from the moss!
8585: Never known before to Nature,
8586: Yet Fashion brought it us.                                           5135

8588: A Fancy Bouquet

8593: Many of us will still please you,
8594: She, I’d like, most to possess us,                                   5140

8599: Rosebuds
8600: 
8601: Many-coloured fancies may
8602: Form the fashion of the day,                                         5145
8603: Strange and curious of shape,
8604: Such as Nature never made:
8605: Stalks of green and bells of gold,
8606: Show in tresses all untold! –
8607: Yet we – remain here, covered up:                                    5150

8610: Then the rosebuds are in flame,
8611: Who would do without such pleasures?

8648: A Mother (With her daughter.)
8649: 
8650: Child, when you came to light,
8651: I dressed you in your little hat:
8652: Your face was so sweet and bright,                                    5180
8653: And your body was soft, at that.
8654: I thought you’d soon be a bride,

8830: Atropos

8832: I, the eldest, I, the spinning                                    5305
8833: Am lumbered with this time: I’ve
8834: Need of lots of pondering, thinking,
8835: To yield the tender threads of life.
8836: 
8837: So you may be soft and supple,
8838: I sift through the finest flax:                                   5310
8839: Drawn through clever fingers, double
8840: Fine, and even, smooth as wax.
8841: 
8842: If you wish all joy and dancing,
8843: Excessive now, in what you take,
8844: Think about those threads: their ending.                          5315
8845: Then, take care! The threads might break.
8846: Clotho
8847: 
8848: Know that in these latter days,
8849: I was trusted with the shears:
8850: Since our eldest sister’s ways,
8851: Failed to help men, it appears.         5320
8852: 
8853: She dragged all her useless spinning,
8854: Endlessly to air and light,

8856: Were clipped and buried out of sight.

8859: Myself, in my younger years,

9055: This good baton’s masterstroke!
9056: Twist and turn now: it’s no joke! –
9057: See how the twin dwarfish ape,
9058: Rolls into a foul lumpish shape!              5475
9059: A wonder – the lump’s an egg, on cue,
9060: It swells and then it cracks in two:
9061: Now a pair of twins appear,
9062: An adder and a bat roll clear.
9063: One through the dust is swiftly winding,      5480
9064: The black one’s flitting round the ceiling.
9065: They hurry outside, in company,
9066: I wouldn’t choose to be number three.
9067: 
9068: Murmurs
9069: 
9070: Lively now! There’s dancing there –
9071: No! I’d much rather be elsewhere –            5485
9072: Can’t you feel some ghostly race
9073: Fly about us, through this place? –
9074: Something just rushed through my hair –
9075: Round my feet, it’s flying, where? –
9076: None of us are injured though –               5490
9077: But we all are frightened so –
9078: All the fun is spoilt completely –
9079: As those creatures wished, you see.
9080: 
9081: The Herald
9082: 
9083: Since I play the herald’s role,
9084: As this masquerade unfolds,               5495
9085: I watch sternly at the door,
9086: In case some devious outlaw
9087: To this happy place, comes creeping:
9088: Never yielding, never wavering.
9089: Through the window, though, I fear        5500
9090: Airborne spectres enter here:
9091: From magic and from devilry
9092: Alas, I cannot set you free.
9093: All this makes the dwarf suspicious,
9094: Now! From behind, a new masque issues.    5505
9095: And I must dutifully explain
9096: The meaning of the forms, again.
9097: But I can’t easily announce
9098: What cannot be understood:
9099: Help me explain it, if you would! –       5510
9100: See it wander through the crowd?
9101: A splendid chariot, a four-in-hand,
9102: Rolling through them, where they stand:
9103: But it doesn’t split the people,
9104: I see no one’s crushed at all.            5515
9105: Colours glitter in the distance,
9106: Sundry wandering stars for instance,
9107: A magic-lantern-like performance.
9108: It blows along, a storm’s assault.
9109: Make way, there! I shudder!
9110: 
9111: The Boy Charioteer
9112:                             Halt!         5520
9113: Dragons, your wings restrain,
9114: Feel your accustomed rein,
9115: Control yourselves, if I control you,
9116: Sweep away when I inspire you –
9117: Let us do honour to this place!           5525
9118: Look round, a widening display
9119: Of admirers, circle now on circle.
9120: Herald, now, then! As you will,
9121: Before we leave you all,
9122: Describe us, and say our name:              5530
9123: Since we’re allegorical,
9124: You should know us, plain.
9125: 
9126: Herald
9127: 
9128: No, indeed, I can’t tell your name:
9129: I’ll try and describe you all the same.
9130: 
9131: The Boy Charioteer
9132: 
9133: So try!
9134: 
9135: The Herald
9136: 
9137:                            I must confess   5535
9138: To young and handsome, before the rest.
9139: You’re a half-grown boy: yet a woman
9140: Would prefer to see you fully grown.
9141: You seem to me a wooer, in future,
9142: Out of her house, a real seducer.           5540
9143: 
9144: The Boy Charioteer
9145: 
9146: Let’s hear more! Go on: go on,
9147: Find the riddle’s bright solution.
9148: 
9149: The Herald
9150: 
9151: Dark eyes that shine: night-black hair
9152: Which brightly jewelled bands enclose:
9153: And what a dainty garment flows             5545
9154: From shoulder down to ankle, there:
9155: With purple hem its glittering shows!
9156: One might take you for a girl:
9157: Yet for good or ill, you’d be,
9158: Prized already by any girl,                 5550
9159: She’d teach you your ABC.
9160: 
9161: The Boy Charioteer
9162: 
9163: And he, who like a splendid vision,
9164: Sits on the chariot, enthroned there?
9165: 
9166: The Herald
9167: 
9168: He seems a king, a rich and kind one,
9169: Blessed are they who gain his favour!       5555
9170: He has no further need to strive,
9171: His eyes observe whatever’s lacking,
9172: And to spread his pure delight,
9173: Is more to him than joy and owning.
9174: 
9175: The Boy Charioteer
9176: 
9177: You daren’t stop there: what you see,       5560
9178: You must describe it precisely.
9179: 
9180: The Herald
9181: 
9182: I can’t express all the dignity.
9183: But the glowing moon face, I see,
9184: The full mouth, the bright cheeks, then
9185: That shine beneath the jewelled turban:     5565
9186: Rich comfort in the clothes he’s wearing!
9187: What shall I say about his bearing?
9188: As a ruler he seems known to me.
9189: 
9190: The Boy Charioteer
9191: 
9192: Plutus the God of Riches, this is he!
9193: He’s come himself in all his splendour,     5570
9194: The Emperor wished greatly he were here.
9195: The Herald
9196: 
9197: Explain your own what and how to me!
9198: 
9199: The Boy Charioteer
9200: 
9201: I am Extravagance: I am Poetry:
9202: I am the Poet, who is self-perfected
9203: When his special gift is squandered.                     5575
9204: Yet I’m immeasurably wealthy,
9205: Like Plutus, worth as much as he,
9206: I adorn, enliven, dance and feast,

9208: 
9209: Herald
9210: 
9211: Your boasting makes you handsomer,                       5580
9212: But let’s see all your skill appear.
9213: 
9214: The Boy Charioteer
9215: 
9216: Just watch me snap my fingers, now,
9217: The chariot will gleam and glow.
9218: There a string of pearls appear!
9219: 
9220: (He continues to snap his fingers, in all directions.)
9221: 
9222: Golden jewels for neck and ear:                          5585
9223: Flawless combs and diadems,
9224: Set in a ring, rare precious gems:
9225: I scatter flames too, here and there,
9226: Waiting for their chance to flare.
9227: 
9228: The Herald
9229: 
9230: How the dear crowd snatch, I see!                        5590
9231: The giver’s soon in difficulty.
9232: He snaps out jewels, as in a dream,
9233: And they all snatch them, in a stream.
9234: But now a different trick, you see:
9235: What each has grasped so eagerly,                     5595
9236: Has gained him but a poor reward,
9237: The gifts already fluttering skyward.
9238: The pearls are loosened from their band,
9239: And beetles crawl there in his hand,
9240: The poor man shakes them off, instead                 5600
9241: They’re humming now around his head.
9242: Another, for some solid thing,
9243: Catches at a butterfly’s wing.
9244: That’s what the rascal’s promise means:
9245: He only lends them golden gleams!                     5605
9246: 
9247: The Boy Charioteer
9248: 
9249: You know how to announce masks: it’s true,
9250: But it’s not the herald’s task to search below
9251: The outer surface of existence:
9252: That requires a keener sense.
9253: Still I’m wary of all disputes.                       5610
9254: Lord, I’ll direct my speech and questioning to you.
9255: 
9256: (Turning towards Plutus.)
9257: 
9258: Have you not trusted me with the task, to stand
9259: And guide the tempest of your four-in-hand?
9260: Don’t I steer well, as you direct?
9261: Am I not there, when you expect?                      5615
9262: And don’t I know how to win
9263: The palm, for you, on daring wing?
9264: When I’ve fought for you in war, now,
9265: I’ve been successful every time:
9266: When laurel wreaths adorn your brow                   5620
9267: Have I not fashioned them with hand and mind?
9268: 
9269: Plutus
9270: 
9271: If I’m required to be a witness to it,
9272: I’d say: You are the spirit of my spirit.
9273: You always act according to my wishes,
9274: And as I gain myself, you too are richer.             5625
9275: To reward your services, I value now
9276: The green branch higher than my crown.
9277: One true word, then, for everyone:
9278: I’ve found delight in you, dear Son.
9279: 
9280: The Boy Charioteer
9281: 
9282: The greatest gifts from my hand,             5630
9283: See! I’ve scattered them around.
9284: On every head there’s the glow
9285: Of some little flame I throw:
9286: Leaping from one brow to another,
9287: Halts on him, then leaves his brother,       5635
9288: But rarely does the flame-let rise,
9289: And briefly flower in bright skies:
9290: For many, before they know, it’s vanished,
9291: Sadly, it’s burnt out, and finished.
9292: 
9293: Women (Chatting to each other.)
9294: 
9295: Up there, on the four-in-hand,               5640
9296: He’s certainly a charlatan:
9297: And there’s a clown perched behind,
9298: By hunger and thirst he’s been refined,
9299: Like nothing one’s ever seen before:
9300: Pinch, and he’ll feel nothing at all.        5645
9301: 
9302: The Starveling
9303: 
9304: Disgusting women, leave me alone!
9305: Not to come here again, I’ll know.
9306: When women kept to their hearths, then
9307: Avaritia, Greed: was my name:
9308: The houses were fine, all about,             5650
9309: Lots came in, nothing went out!
9310: I took care of cupboard and chest:
9311: That was a burden, to top the rest.
9312: But now in this younger age,
9313: Wives don’t know how to save,                5655
9314: And like all those wicked students,
9315: They have more desires than ‘talents’,
9316: And their men have much to suffer,
9317: Their debts are left about all over.
9318: They spend whatever they can extract,       5660
9319: On their lovers, and on their backs:
9320: They eat of the best, and drink deeper,
9321: With their wretched army of admirers:
9322: Which adds to the value of gold, for me:
9323: We’re manly fellows, the Miserly!           5665
9324: 
9325: Leader of the Women
9326: 
9327: Let dragon be miserly with dragon:
9328: In the end it’s merely lies, illusion!
9329: Men flock around, and turn the charm on,
9330: But they’re soon annoyance and confusion.

9332: The Crowd of Women
9333: 
9334: That Scarecrow! Give him a poke!            5670
9335: What’s the Wooden Rake threaten?
9336: We’ll all shun his ugly looks, then!
9337: Dragons of wood and paper: a joke!

9339: 
9340: The Herald
9341: 
9342: By my wand! Keep the peace! –               5675
9343: Though there’s no need for my assistance:
9344: Look at those grim monsters, how each
9345: Clears round itself a proper distance,
9346: Unfolding its quadruple wings, the beast.
9347: The dragons shake themselves, indignant,    5680
9348: With fiery throats, their tails rampant:
9349: The place is cleared: the people flee.
9350: 
9351: (Plutus descends from the chariot.)
9352: The Herald
9353:

9355: He beckons, and the dragons stir:
9356: From the chariot bearing Avarice,                  5685
9357: And gold, down comes the chest,
9358: See, there at his feet, it’s landed:
9359: It’s a wonder how it happened.
9360: 
9361: Plutus (To the Boy Charioteer)
9362: 
9363: Now you’ve left that troubling burden here,
9364: You’re free: so, fly now to your own sphere!       5690
9365: Not this! Where, confused, motley, wild,
9366: Distorted objects crowd around us, child.
9367: No: where you see clear, with sweetest Clarity,
9368: Self-possessed, trusting in your own self: flee,
9369: Where Goodness and Beauty may be viewed,           5695
9370: And there create your world – in Solitude!
9371: 
9372: The Boy Charioteer
9373: 
9374: So, I’ll be your worthy envoy then,
9375: So, I’ll love you like my dearest kin.
9376: Where you live, is Plenty: and where
9377: I am, all feel they gain in splendour.             5700
9378: And often hesitate in life’s uncertainty:
9379: Should they yield to you, or yield to me?
9380: Certainly your followers will have rest:
9381: Who follows me, with work’s forever blessed.
9382: My actions are never kept a secret,                5705
9383: I only have to breathe and I’m apparent.
9384: Farewell, then! You granted me my joy:
9385: But whisper low, and you shall have your boy!

9388: Plutus (Faust in disguise.)
9389:

9391: I strike the lock with the herald’s wand.            5710
9392: It’s open! Look! Vessels of noblest measure,
9393: Pour the golden blood through your hands,
9394: First it swells, roars, writhes as if it’s molten:

9396: 
9397: Various Shouts from the Crowd.
9398:

9400: The chest, right to the brim, it glows. –
9401: Golden vessels, molten too,
9402: Rolls of coins, turning too. –
9403: Minted ducats leaping,

9405: I see all, for which I’m yearning,
9406: On the floor there, burning! –

9481: And in clear mime make my address.
9482: Hands, feet, gesturing won’t cut the ice,

9487: The Herald
9488:

9492: It’s soft between his hands, although

9510: Tumult and Singing
9511: 
9512: The wild crowd come here, specially,
9513: From mountain-top, and wooded valley,
9514: Shouting forcefully, as they can:
9515: They celebrate the great god Pan.            5805
9516: They know what none can know,
9517: And into the empty circle flow.
9518: 
9519: Plutus
9520: 
9521: ‘I know you well, and your great Pan!
9522: Together these daring steps you plan.
9523: I know all that no one knows,
9524: And clear for you this narrow close.’        5810
9525: May good fortune follow them too!
9526: The strangest things may happen:
9527: They don’t know where they’re going to:
9528: Since they never look before them.
9529: 
9530: Wild Singing
9531: 
9532: You plaster people: you tinsel show!         5815
9533: Rough and coarse is how they go,
9534: Leaping: wild is their track ahead,
9535: Solid and sturdy is their tread.
9536: Fauns
9537: 
9538: The Faun flocks
9539: In happy dance,                          5820
9540: Oaken garlands,
9541: On curling locks,
9542: Fine pointed ears
9543: Through tangled hair,
9544: Snub noses, faces broad and flat,        5825
9545: The women can’t fault any of that:
9546: When the Fauns begin to prance,
9547: The loveliest won’t scorn the dance.
9548: 
9549: A Satyr
9550: 
9551: The Satyr’s leaping here behind,
9552: Goat’s foot, and lean of thigh,          5830
9553: Sinewy, skinny he’ll go by,
9554: And chamois-like, on mountain height,
9555: He looks around, and takes delight.
9556: He’s alive in the free air,
9557: Mocks at man, child, woman there,        5835
9558: Who deep in the valley’s damp flue,
9559: Think, cosily, they’re living too,
9560: While, still pure and undisturbed,
9561: To him alone is the upper world.
9562: 
9563: The Gnomes
9564: 
9565: The little crowd trips by there,         5840
9566: They don’t like to travel in pairs:
9567: In mossy clothes with lanterns bright,
9568: They pass together, quick and light,
9569: Each one passing on his own,
9570: Like glowing ants swarming home:         5845
9571: And always busy, here and there,
9572: Industrious, and everywhere.
9573: Kin to the ‘Little People’, known
9574: As surgeons to the rock and stone:
9575: ‘We bleed the mountains high,            5850
9576: We drain the deep veins dry:
9577: We hurl the metals round,
9578: With hearty greetings: Luck! Well found!
9579: And it’s always kindly meant: again,
9580: We’re the friends of all good men.                             5855
9581: Yet we the gold to light deliver,
9582: So men may steal, and covet ever,
9583: So princely hand won’t lack the steel
9584: That worldwide murder longs to deal.
9585: Who those three commandments breaks                            5860
9586: Scant heed of the other seven takes.
9587: But of all that we’re innocent:
9588: About it all, like us, be patient.’
9589: 
9590: The Giants
9591: 
9592: The wild men, we are named,
9593: Known in all the Hartz range:                                  5865
9594: Natural, plain, in all our antics,
9595: Appearing frightfully gigantic.
9596: A fir-tree trunk in each right hand,
9597: Round our body a thick band,
9598: A solid apron of branches, not                                 5870
9599: The bodyguard the Pope has got.
9600: 
9601: Nymphs in Chorus (Surrounding Great Pan, who is the masked Emperor.)
9602: 
9603: Here he’ll stand! –
9604: The world’s All,
9605: Is shown to all,
9606: In mighty Pan.                                                 5875
9607: You the happiest, surround him,
9608: In magic dances soar around him:
9609: Here now, serious and good, he
9610: Wishes all men to be happy.
9611: Under the curving roof of blue                                 5880
9612: He seems endlessly wakeful, too,
9613: Yet the streams flow gently for him,
9614: And the breezes gently rock him,
9615: And, when he sleeps at noon, the leaf
9616: Is motionless in the branches’ wreath:     5885
9617: The rich plants’ fragrant balsams there
9618: Fill all the still and silent air:
9619: The Nymph no longer dares to leap,
9620: And where she stands, falls fast asleep.
9621: But when his powerful shout,               5890
9622: Unexpectedly, rings out,
9623: Like thunder crack, or wave’s roar,
9624: Who knows what’s happening any more,
9625: The army’s witless in the fight,
9626: The hero in battle’s filled with fright.   5895
9627: So honour him, where honour’s due,
9628: And hail him, who led us to you!
9629: 
9630: A Deputation of Gnomes (To Great Pan.)
9631: 
9632: When the rich and shining goods,
9633: Spread threadlike through the deep,
9634: Then delicate divining rods,               5900
9635: Reveal what labyrinths keep.
9636: 
9637: Bending in our dark vaults, there,
9638: As troglodytes we’re measured,
9639: While in the purest daylight air,
9640: Gracious, you divide the treasure.         5905
9641: 
9642: Now we find we’ve discovered
9643: A marvellous fountain here,
9644: Promising, easily, to deliver
9645: Things that infrequently appear.
9646: 
9647: It all waits for your command:             5910
9648: Master, take and care for it: do.
9649: Every treasure in your hand,
9650: Helps the whole world too.
9651: Plutus (To the Herald.)
9652: 
9653: We must grasp things in the highest sense,
9654: And let what may come, come, with confidence.                      5915
9655: You’ve shown the highest courage once before.
9656: So now too what is fearful, we must try it:
9657: World, and posterity, will stubbornly deny it,
9658: So pen it faithfully in your report.
9659: 
9660: The Herald (Grasping the wand in Plutus’ hand, and assisting with the
9661: Masquerade.)
9662: 
9663: The dwarves lead on great Pan,                                     5920
9664: Gently, to the fiery fountain:
9665: It boils from the deep profound,
9666: Then sinks again, through the ground,
9667: And gloomy is its open round:
9668: Yet shows again the heat and glow.                                 5925
9669: Great Pan stands there, well disposed,
9670: Pleased with all this wondrous thing,
9671: Pearl foam, right, left, showering.
9672: How can he trust such a show?
9673: He bends to look inside, and so,                                   5930
9674: His beard gets caught within! –
9675: Who’s made that hairless chin?
9676: His hand hides it from our vision. –
9677: What follows is all clumsy action:
9678: The beard, on fire, flies back, soon                               5935
9679: Scorching garland, chest and head:
9680: Delight is turned to pain instead. –
9681: They rush to quench it all again,
9682: But none of them are free of flames,
9683: And how they flare and dart,                                       5940
9684: Exciting fire in every part:
9685: Wreathed in that element,
9686: The whole masked crowd is burnt.
9687: But what’s all this news about,
9688: Ear after ear, mouth after mouth!                                  5945
9689: O eternally unlucky night
9690: So little of it’s turned out right!
9691: Tomorrow’s dawn will declare
9692: What nobody wants to hear:
9693: In every ear we’ll hear it plain:             5950
9694: ‘The Emperor is in such pain.’
9695: O, would that it were something other!
9696: Burnt, Emperor and Court together.
9697: Cursed be those who led him astray,
9698: In resinous twigs did him array,              5955
9699: To rage, and bellow out that song,
9700: To the ruin of all that throng.
9701: O Youth, Youth will you never
9702: Restrict joy’s purest measure?
9703: O Power, Power, will you never,               5960
9704: Sense and Omnipotence treasure?
9705: The ‘forest’ too is soon in flames,
9706: The pointed tongues play their games,
9707: To the real wooden beams lick higher:
9708: We’re threatened by universal fire.           5965
9709: The cup of misery overflows,
9710: Who will save us? No one knows.
9711: See, Imperial splendour, by dawn’s light,
9712: Turned to a heap of ash, in a single night.
9713: 
9714: Plutus
9715: 
9716: That’s enough terror overhead,                5970
9717: Let help arrive here, instead! –
9718: Strike, you heavenly wand, with power,
9719: So the earth will ring and tremor!
9720: You, the wide realms of air,
9721: Fill with cool fragrance there!               5975
9722: Hurry down, to sweep around us,
9723: Cloudy mists and swelling vapours,
9724: Quench the thronging flames!
9725: Murmuring, trickling, fogs gather,
9726: Sliding, rolling, softly drenching,           5980
9727: Slipping everywhere, and quenching.
9728: You, the moist, who soothe forever,
9729: Change them all to gleaming weather,
9730: All these empty fiery games! –
9731: Threatening Spirits, that would harm,   5985
9732: We, by magic, will disarm.
9733: Part II Act I Scene IV: A Pleasure Garden in the Morning Sun
9734: 
9735: (The Emperor, his Court, Noblemen and Ladies: Faust and Mephistopheles
9736: dressed fashionably but not ostentatiously, both kneel.)
9737: 
9738: Faust
9739: 
9740: Sire, forgive the fiery conjuring tricks?
9741: 
9742: The Emperor (Beckoning to him to rise.)
9743: 
9744: More fun, in that vein, would be my wish. –
9745: At once, I saw myself in a glowing sphere,
9746: It seemed as if I were divine Pluto, there.                      5990
9747: A rocky depth of mine, and darkness, lay
9748: Glowing with flame: out of each vent played
9749: A thousand wild and whirling fires,
9750: And flickered in the vault together, higher,
9751: Licking upwards to the highest dome,                             5995
9752: That now seemed there, and now was gone.
9753: Through a far space wound with fiery pillars,
9754: I saw a long line of people approach us,
9755: Crowding till they formed a circle near,
9756: And paid me homage, as they do forever.                          6000

9758: I seemed the Prince of a thousand salamanders.
9759: 
9760: Mephistopheles
9761: 
9762: You are, Sire! Since every element
9763: Knows your Majesty, amongst all men.
9764: You’ve now proved the fire obedient:                             6005

9766: You’ll barely touch its pearl-strewn bed,
9767: A noble dome will rise round you, instead:
9768: You’ll see green translucent waves swelling
9769: Purple edged, to make the loveliest dwelling,                    6010
9770: And you will be its centre. At each step

9772: The very walls themselves delight in life,
9773: Flash to and fro, in swarming arrow-flight.
9774: Sea-wonders crowd around this sweet new sight,     6015
9775: Shoot past, still not allowed to enter quite.
9776: There, golden-scaled, bright sea-dragons play,
9777: The shark gapes wide, you smile in his face.
9778: However much your court attracts you now,
9779: You’ve never seen such an amazing crowd.           6020
9780: Nor will you part there from the loveliest:
9781: The Nereids will be gathering, curious,
9782: To this wondrous house, in seas eternally fresh,
9783: The youngest shy and pleasure-loving, like fish,
9784: The old ones: cunning. Thetis at the news,         6025

10067: Part II Act I Scene V: A Gloomy Gallery
10068:

10177: Have I not trafficked with the world?
10178: Learned the void, the void unfurled? –
10179: When I spoke with reason, as I descried,
10180: Contradiction, doubly loud, replied:
10181: Have I not fled, from hateful trickery,            6235
10182: Into the wild, into the solitary,
10183: And, not to lose all, and live alone,

10186:

10193: Seen clouds go by, Sun, Moon and star –                6245
10194: You’ll see none in the endless void, afar,

10217:

10237:

10242: 
10243: Faust
10244: 
10245: Yes, there’s no good for me in lethargy.

10248: Once seized by it, we feel Immensity deeply.
10249: 
10250: Mephistopheles
10251: 
10252: Then, descend! I might as easily say rise!            6275
10253: It’s all the same. Escape from what exists,
10254: Into the boundless realm where all Form lies!
10255: Delight in what’s no longer on the list:
10256: Where turmoil rolls along all cloudily:
10257: Then, far from your body, swing the key!              6280
10258: Faust (Inspired.)
10259:

10262: 
10263: Mephistopheles
10264:

10267: By its light you’ll see the Mothers,                    6285
10268: Some sit about, as they wish, the others,
10269: Stand and move. Formation, Transformation,
10270: Eternal minds in eternal recreation.
10271: Images of all creatures float, portrayed:
10272: They’ll not see you: they only see a shade.             6290

10278: 
10279: Mephistopheles (Watching him.)
10280: 
10281:                                         That’s right!
10282: It will close itself, and follow as a servant might:
10283: Exalted by your good luck, you’ll calmly rise,          6295
10284: And be back with it, before you’ve blinked your eyes.
10285: And, once you’ve brought it here all right,
10286: Call the Hero and Heroine from the night,
10287: The first man who has ever achieved it:
10288: It’s done, and you’re the one who did it.               6300

10290: The incense’ vapour will become divine.

10292: Faust
10293:

10295: Mephistopheles
10296:

11040: Still in all his coarse wrapping!
11041: Then he seemed a fount of wisdom,
11042: Since I didn’t understand him.
11043: He won’t find me so today,
11044: Fresh and new, I’m on my way!             6720
11045: 
11046: Sir, if in Lethe’s melancholy stream
11047: That bald nodding head’s not swum,
11048: See your grateful scholar come,
11049: Outgrown, his academic dream.
11050: I find you now, as I saw you:             6725
11051: I was another though: that’s true.
11052: 
11053: Mephistopheles
11054: 
11055: I’m glad the ringing brought you.
11056: I rated you once before as high:
11057: The caterpillar, the chrysalis too,
11058: Showed the bright future butterfly.       6730
11059: Your curly hair and pointed collar,
11060: Made you a childishly pleasing scholar.
11061: You never wore pigtails I believe? –
11062: And today you’re cropped like a Swede.
11063: I see you’re bold and resolute:                         6735
11064: But don’t go home too absolute!
11065: 
11066: Baccalaureus
11067: 
11068: My old master! We’re in our old places:
11069: But don’t think to renew time’s journey,
11070: And spare me words with dual-faces:
11071: I treat them now quite differently.                     6740
11072: You teased the true, and honest youth.
11073: It wasn’t difficult for you to do
11074: It’s what no one dares to do today.
11075: 
11076: Mephistopheles
11077: 
11078: Pure truth on the young is thrown away,
11079: The little beaks don’t like it, any way,                6745
11080: But afterwards when years have passed,
11081: And they’ve learnt it for themselves at last,
11082: And think it came from them, not school:
11083: Then we hear: ‘The Master was a fool.’
11084: 
11085: Baccalaureus
11086: 
11087: A rascal, maybe! – What teacher ever shows us           6750
11088: The Truth directly, underneath our noses?
11089: They know the way to make it seem more, or less,
11090: Now serious, now playful, as suits the children best.
11091: 
11092: Mephistopheles
11093: 
11094: There’s a moment given us for learning, truly:
11095: But you’re ready now to teach, yourself, I see.         6755
11096: For many moons, united with their suns,
11097: You the riches of experience have won.
11098: Baccalaureus
11099: 
11100: Experience! Mist and Foam!
11101: And not the Spirit’s equal.
11102: Confess! What one has known,                       6760
11103: Is not worth knowing at all.
11104: 
11105: Mephistopheles (After a pause.)
11106: 
11107: I’ve thought so for ages. I was a Fool,
11108: But I think that shallow now I’m sensible.
11109: 
11110: Baccalaureus
11111: 
11112: That pleases me! I hear pure Reason’s sound:
11113: The first old man of sense I’ve ever found.        6765
11114: 
11115: Mephistopheles
11116: 
11117: I sought for treasure, buried gold,
11118: And brought to light frightful coals.
11119: 
11120: Baccalaureus
11121: 
11122: Confess now, your skull, bald and old,
11123: Is worth no more than that empty poll.
11124: 
11125: Mephistopheles (Amiably.)
11126: 
11127: Do you know, my friend, how rude you seem to me?   6770
11128: 
11129: Baccalaureus
11130: 
11131: In German, one’s lying if one speaks politely.
11132: Mephistopheles (Wheeling his chair nearer to the proscenium and the
11133: audience.)
11134: 
11135: Up here I’m dazed by light and air:
11136: Shall I take shelter with you down there?
11137: 
11138: Baccalaureus
11139: 
11140: I find it arrogant that in times like these,
11141: A man wants to be what he no longer is.                           6775
11142: Man’s life is in his arteries, and when
11143: Are they so vibrant as in younger men?
11144: There the fresh blood full of strength
11145: Creates new life from its own life again.
11146: There all works, and things get done,                             6780
11147: The waverers fall, the capable get on.
11148: While we’ve conquered half the world,
11149: What have you done? Nodded, curled
11150: In the sun, dreamed, weighed, plan on plan.
11151: For sure, age is a chilling fever:                                6785
11152: The frost of whims and need ahead.
11153: When your thirtieth year is over,
11154: A man’s as good as dead.
11155: It would be best to seek an early grave.
11156: 
11157: Mephistopheles
11158: 
11159: That leaves the Devil nothing more to say.                        6790
11160: 
11161: Baccalaureus
11162: 
11163: Unless I will it, no Devil can exist.
11164: 
11165: Mephistopheles (Aside.)
11166: 
11167: The Devil will still trip you, in a bit.
11168: 
11169: Baccalaureus
11170: 
11171: This is youth’s noblest profession!
11172: The world was nothing before my creation:
11173: I drew the Sun out of the sea:                                  6795
11174: The Moon began her changeful course with me:
11175: The daylight decked my path to greet me,
11176: The Earth flowered, grew green, to meet me.
11177: At my command, in primal night,
11178: The stars in splendour swam to sight.                           6800
11179: Who, but I, loosed from its prison
11180: Cramped thought’s philistinism?
11181: I, quite free, as my spirit cites,
11182: Happily following my inner light,
11183: And speeding on, in delight,                                    6805
11184: Darkness behind: and all before me, bright.
11185: 
11186: Mephistopheles
11187: 
11188: Go forth in splendour, you primal man! –
11189: How could insight harm you, ever:
11190: Who can think of stupid things or clever,
11191: That past ages didn’t, long ago, understand.                    6810
11192: Yet there’s no danger from him, you see,
11193: He’ll think about it differently in time:
11194: Even if the grape-juice acts absurdly,
11195: In the end it changes into wine.
11196: 
11197: (To the younger members of the audience, who do not applaud.)
11198: 
11199: My words have left you cold, I gather,
11200: May it be so for you, sweet children:
11201: But think: the Devil’s a lot older,
11202: So you need to be old to understand him!
11203: Part II Act II Scene II: A Laboratory
11204: 
11205: (In the fashion of the Middle Ages: lots of heavy apparatus for strange
11206: purposes.)
11207: 
11208: Wagner (At the furnace.)
11209: 
11210: The fearful bell is sounding,
11211: The soot-black walls shudder.                                             6820
11212: My deepest expectation
11213: Will be unsure no longer.
11214: Soon the dark itself will lighten:
11215: Soon in the innermost phial,
11216: It will glow like living fire,                                            6825
11217: Yes, like the noblest ruby’s glow,
11218: Lightning flashing in the shadow.
11219: A clearest white light shines now!
11220: Ah, not to lose it once more! –
11221: Oh, God! Who’s rattling at the door?                                      6830
11222: 
11223: Mephistopheles (Entering.)
11224: 
11225: Greetings! And kindly meant now.
11226: 
11227: Wagner (Anxiously.)
11228: 
11229: Welcome, to the planet of the hour!
11230: 
11231: (Whispering.)
11232: 
11233: But stifle your breath, and words’ power,
11234: A noble work is likewise being weighed.
11235: 
11236: Mephistopheles (Whispering.)
11237: 
11238: What might it be?
11239: 
11240: Wagner (Whispering.)
11241: 
11242:                     A Man is being made.                                  6835
11243: Mephistopheles
11244: 
11245: A Man? And what loving couple
11246: Have you got hidden, up the chimney?
11247: 
11248: Wagner
11249: 
11250: God Forbid! How unfashionable!
11251: We’re free of all that idle foolery.
11252: The tender moment from which life emerged,        6840
11253: The charming power with which its inner urge,
11254: Took and gave, and clearly stamped its seal,
11255: First in a near, and then a further field,
11256: We now divest of all that dignity:
11257: Though the creatures still enjoy it, we,          6845
11258: As Men, with all our greater gifts, begin,
11259: To have, as we should, a nobler origin.
11260: 
11261: (He turns towards the furnace.)
11262: 
11263: It brightens! See! – Now there’s a real chance,
11264: That, if from the hundred-fold substance,
11265: By mixing – since mixing makes it happen –        6850
11266: The stuff of human life’s compounded,
11267: And distilled in a flask, well-founded,
11268: And in proper combination, grounded,
11269: Then the silent work is done.
11270: 
11271: (He turns again to the furnace.)
11272: 
11273: It will be! The mass is clearer!                  6855
11274: The proof comes nearer, nearer:
11275: What man praises in deepest Nature,
11276: Through Reason we dare to probe it,
11277: And what she organises, here,
11278: We’re now able to crystallise it.                 6860
11279: Mephistopheles
11280: 
11281: Who lives a while, gains much experience,
11282: And nothing new can happen on his journey.
11283: In years of travelling, and in my presence,
11284: I’ve seen, already, crystallised humanity.
11285: 
11286: Wagner (Up till now attending to the phial.)
11287: 
11288: It rises: flashes, there’s expansion           6865
11289: In a moment more it will be done.
11290: Great aims seem foolish at the outset:
11291: But we’ll laugh at Chance itself, yet,
11292: And brains, with thoughts to celebrate,
11293: In the future, a Thinker will create.          6870
11294: 
11295: (He inspects the phial, rapturously.)
11296: 
11297: The glass rings with sweet power,
11298: It darkens, clears: it must have being!
11299: In a delicate form I see appear
11300: A well-behaved little Man behaving.
11301: What can the world ask more, what can we?      6875
11302: Now that this mystery’s visible to each.
11303: Give ear to what these sounds may be,
11304: They make a voice: they’re forming speech.
11305: 
11306: Homunculus (From the phial, to Wagner.)
11307: 
11308: Now, father! That was no joke. How are you?
11309: Come: press me tenderly to your heart, too!    6880
11310: But not too hard, the glass may be too thin.
11311: It’s in the very nature of the thing:
11312: For the natural the world has barely space:
11313: What’s artificial commands a narrow place.
11314: 
11315: (To Mephistopheles.)
11316: 
11317: But you, Rascal, my dear Cousin, are you       6885
11318: Here at the right moment? I thank you, too.
11319: Good fortune’s led you here to me:
11320: Since I exist, I must be doing, you see.
11321: I’d like to begin my work today:
11322: You’re skilful at shortening the way.                            6890
11323: 
11324: Wagner
11325: 
11326: But first, a word! Till now I’ve had no direction,
11327: When old or young teased me with a question.
11328: For example: no one’s found out, ever,
11329: What makes body and soul fit together:
11330: Stick tight, as if there’ll be no separation,                    6895
11331: Yet always cause each other irritation.
11332: So then, -
11333: 
11334: Mephistopheles
11335: 
11336:                 Stop! I’d rather he told me,
11337: Why married people get by so wretchedly?
11338: You’ll never discover that, my friend.
11339: There’s work to do the little Man can tend.                      6900
11340: 
11341: Homunculus
11342: 
11343: What work’s to do?
11344:

11346: 
11347:              Employ your gifts on this!
11348:

11352:

11355: 
11356: Interesting!
11357:

11359: him.)
11360: 
11361:        Lovely surroundings! – Clear water
11362: In thick forest! Women there: undressing.
11363: The loveliest of all! – It’s getting clearer.                        6905
11364: One’s left, different from the rest, gleaming:
11365: Of highest race, for sure, a heavenly name.
11366: She places her foot in the transparent glow,
11367: Her noble body’s sweetly living flame
11368: Cools itself in the yielding crystal flow. –                         6910
11369: But what’s that rush of beating wings for:
11370: That thrashing, splashing, in the mirror?
11371: The lovely girls, intimidated, flee:
11372: Their queen, alone, looks on, composedly,
11373: To see, with a proud feminine pleasure,                              6915
11374: The Swan-Prince press against her knee, there,
11375: Forward yet tame. Familiar, he seems. –
11376: But suddenly a vapour heaves,
11377: And covers, with the veil it weaves,
11378: The loveliest of scenes.                                             6920
11379: 
11380: Mephistopheles
11381: 
11382: All the things that you could murmur!
11383: So little: and such a great dreamer.
11384: I see nothing –
11385: 
11386: Homunculus
11387: 
11388:         So I believe. You’re Northern,
11389: In the age of mist you’re born then,                                 6925
11390: In a jumble of priest-craft and chivalry,
11391: So how could your sight be free!
11392: You’re at home with darkness.
11393: (He gazes around.)
11394: 
11395: Brown repulsive, mildewed walls,
11396: Low, pointed arches, full of scrolls! –
11397: One wakes, and gives another pain,         6930
11398: On the spot, dead then, he’ll remain.
11399: Wooded founts, swans, naked beauty,
11400: That was his far-sighted dream:
11401: How could this place do duty!
11402: I can scarcely endure the scene.           6935
11403: Carry him off!
11404: 
11405: Mephistopheles
11406: 
11407:   I’d be happy: a last chance.
11408: 
11409: Homunculus
11410: 
11411: Order the soldier to the fight,
11412: Lead the maiden to the dance,
11413: Then everything’s done right.
11414: Even now, thinks, quick as light,          6940
11415: It’s Classical Walpurgis Night:
11416: That’s the best, if he were sent
11417: To his own true element!
11418: 
11419: Mephistopheles
11420: 
11421: I’ve never heard that event named, here.
11422: 
11423: Homunculus
11424: 
11425: How could it come to your ear?             6945
11426: Only Romantic ghosts, for you:
11427: A true ghost must be Classic too.
11428: Mephistopheles
11429: 
11430: Which path do we take there? Already

11432: 
11433: Homunculus
11434: 
11435: North-westward Satan, is your pleasure ground,        6950
11436: But this time we’re South-eastward bound –
11437: In wider space flows Peneus, the free
11438: By bushes, groves, and damp still bays:
11439: Its levels stretch to mountain ways,

11441: 
11442: Mephistopheles
11443: 
11444: Oh! Enough! And keep all the fight,
11445: Of tyranny and slavery, out of sight.

11447: They start the whole thing over again:
11448: And no one sees: they’re being re-aligned,            6960
11449: By Asmodeus, who works them from behind.

11451: Seen rightly, slave with slave is all the fight.
11452: 
11453: Homunculus
11454:

11456: Each man defends himself, as best he can,             6965
11457: From childhood, till, at last, he is a man.
11458: Just ask how we can get back there again.

11460: If you haven’t, leave it all to me.
11461: 
11462: Mephistopheles
11463:

11465: But I find that Pagan bolts have barred the way.
11466: The whole Greek race was never that much use!
11467: They dazzle with the senses’ freer play: it’s true:

11471: 
11472: Homunculus
11473:

11477:

11479:

11481: I once enquired about long ago.                    6980

11485: 
11486: Homunculus

11490: As before, the cloak can carry another,

11497: 
11498: Homunculus

11502: Unfold all your ancient parchments,
11503: Then, by rote, collect life’s elements,            6990
11504: And place them together with due care,
11505: Consider What, more deeply consider How.

11507: And find the last dot on the ‘i’, for now.

11509: Great effort will merit great reward, you’ll see:

11528: Part II Act II Scene III: Classical Walpurgis Night.
11529: The Pharsalian Fields.
11530: 
11531: (Darkness.)
11532: 
11533: Erichtho (The Thessalian Witch, see Lucan’s Pharsalia)
11534: 
11535: This night’s awesome feast, as so often in the past,        7005
11536: I enter now, I, Erichtho, the gloomy one:
11537: Not so abominable as the wretched poets
11538: Painted me, with excessive slander…they never
11539: Cease their blame or praise…I see the valley whiten
11540: With waves of tents that gleam greyer in the distance,      7010
11541: The after-image of that anxious, fearful night.
11542: How often it’s repeated! In eternity
11543: Acted out, again, forever…No one gives the realm
11544: To another: to the one whose power won it:
11545: Whose strength rules. Since each, incapable of ruling       7015
11546: His inner self, would gladly rule his neighbour’s will,
11547: In the manner that his proud mind dictates to him…
11548: But here a great instance was fought out, to the end,
11549: Of how force may battle against a greater force,
11550: Freedom’s lovely thousand-blossomed garland be torn,        7020
11551: And stubborn laurel be wound round the ruler’s brow.
11552: Here, Pompey dreams of his youth and former greatness,
11553: There, Caesar, listening, watches the balance tremble!
11554: It settles, and the world knows whom it sinks towards.
11555: The watch fires, glowing, send out their crimson flames:    7025
11556: The field exhales those images of squandered blood,
11557: And lured by the strange wondrous splendour of the night,
11558: A legion of Hellenic legends gather here.
11559: They hover around all the fires uncertainly,
11560: Or sit nearby, the fabled forms of ancient days….           7030
11561: The Moon, not full it is true, but of clearest light,
11562: Rises, scattering mild radiance everywhere:
11563: The ghostly tents vanish: the fires burn bluish now.
11564: But, over my head, what sudden meteor’s this?
11565: It shines, illuminates the material globe.                  7035
11566: I smell Life. It’s not fitting for me to approach
11567: Closer to the living, since I’m harmful to them:
11568: It gives me a bad name, and is no benefit to me.
11569: It sinks down already. I give way, thoughtfully!
11570: 
11571: (She Exits. The Airy Travellers speak from above.)
11572: 
11573: Homunculus
11574: 
11575: Once again float round the circle                    7040
11576: Over flames and shuddering horror:
11577: On the ground, and in the vale still,

11579: 
11580: Mephistopheles
11581: 
11582: It’s the same as through my old window
11583: In the grim and tangled north,                       7045
11584: Really loathsome ghosts below,
11585: I’m at home here: and there, of course.
11586: 
11587: Homunculus
11588:

11590: With gigantic steps, before us.
11591:

11595: Through the air above, she saw us.
11596: 
11597: Homunculus
11598: 
11599: Let her stride! Right away,
11600: Set the knight down there:
11601: He’ll return to life again,
11602: Once he breathes this mythic air.                    7055

11604: 
11605: Where is she?
11606: 
11607: Homunculus
11608: 
11609:                  We can’t say, I fear,
11610: But you can probably enquire here.
11611: Hurry now before it’s daylight,

11613: Who found his way to the Mothers’ side,        7060
11614: Won’t find this harder to survive.
11615: 
11616: Mephistopheles
11617: 
11618: On my own behalf too, I’m here:
11619: But I don’t know anything better

11624: 
11625: Homunculus
11626: 
11627: It shines like this, and rings.

11632:

11634: 
11635: Where is she? – But no further answer seek…    7070
11636: If this is not the soil she trod,
11637: Nor the wave that bathed her foot,
11638: It is the air that spoke her speech.
11639: Here! By a miracle, on Hellenic land!
11640: I feel, the earth, too, where I stand:         7075
11641: A fresh power glows in me, the Sleeper,
11642: So I am Antaeus-like in nature.
11643: And I find the strangest things lie here,
11644: First let me search this Labyrinth of fire.
11645: 
11646: (He moves away.)
11647: (On the Upper Peneus)
11648: 
11649: Mephistopheles (Looking around.)
11650: 
11651: And as I wander through these fires,                            7080
11652: I feel myself a total stranger: in the event,
11653: They’re mostly naked, a shirt here and there:
11654: The Sphinx shameless, the Gryphon impudent:
11655: And what’s more, curly-haired and winged,
11656: Before, behind, in eyes, reflected things…                      7085
11657: Of course, at heart, indecency’s my ideal,
11658: But I find the Antique is a little too real.
11659: One should control all with a modern mind,
11660: Overlay it with fashions of assorted kinds….
11661: Repulsive people! Yet still I have to meet them,                7090
11662: And, as a new guest too, correctly greet them…
11663: Luck to you, fair ladies, and men, you wise grey ones!
11664: 
11665: A Gryphon (Snarling. For the gold-guarding Gryphons see Herodotus’
11666: Histories.)
11667: 
11668: Not Grey ones! Gryphons! – No one likes the name
11669: Of something grey. Every word rings
11670: With what conditioned it: its origins:                          7095
11671: Grey, grievous, grumpy, gruesome, gravely, grimly,
11672: Similarly harmonious etymologically,
11673: Disharmonise us.
11674: 
11675: Mephistopheles
11676: 
11677:                        And yet, without deviation,
11678: You like the gryp in your proud name of Gryphon.
11679: 
11680: The Gryphon (Snarling continuously.)
11681: 
11682: Naturally! The relationship’s tried and tested:                 7100
11683: It was often censured, but more often praised:
11684: One grips maidens, money, gold,
11685: To the gripper, Fortune’s never cold.
11686: Giant Ants
11687: 
11688: You spoke of gold: we’ve collected lots of it,
11689: In rocks and caves, secretly, we’ve crammed it:                     7105
11690: The Arimaspi, discovered it all, one day,
11691: They’re laughing now: they took it far away.
11692: 
11693: The Gryphon
11694: 
11695: We’ll soon make them confess.
