12390: What an intolerable fuss!
12391: But we’ll not lose our place,
12392: Even if all hell shakes.
12393: Now a dome is lifted,                         7530
12394: Wonderful. He’s gifted
12395: It to us, the ancient one,
12396: Delos’ isle was his creation,
12397: Driven from out the wave,
12398: To bring Latona aid.                          7535
12399: He with striving, pushing, pressing,
12400: Arms straight, and shoulders bending,
12401: Like an Atlas in his action,
12402: Lifts rock and earth, in motion,
12403: Shingle, gravel, sand: the floors             7540
12404: All along our peaceful shores.
12405: Rips our vale’s quiet surface up,
12406: Crosswise, with a single cut:
12407: Fiercely, and unwearied,
12408: A colossal caryatid,                          7545
12409: Bears a fearsome weight of boulders,
12410: Still buried, downwards to his shoulders:
12411: But he’ll come no further, now,
12412: The Sphinxes’ place is here, we vow.
12413: Seismos
12414: 
12415: I myself achieved all this,                7550
12416: Man should admit it, finally:
12417: If I’d not jolted and shaken it,
12418: How could the world be so lovely? –
12419: How could your peaks stand so high,
12420: In the pure and splendid blue,             7555
12421: If I’d not pushed them to the sky,
12422: Picturesque and charming too?
12423: Then, thinking of my high ancestry,
12424: Night and Chaos, I behaved badly,
12425: And, a company of Titans, we               7560
12426: With Pelion and Ossa played madly,
12427: Romping round in youthful glee,
12428: Till, we tired of it, at last,
12429: And set both mountains, wickedly,
12430: On Parnassus, as a double hat….            7565
12431: There, now, Apollo’s sweet retreat,
12432: With the happy band of Muses.
12433: And Jupiter, thunderbolts complete:
12434: I even raised the high seat he uses.
12435: So now with monstrous striving             7570
12436: I’ve pushed this upwards, from the deep,
12437: And call, aloud, to their new being,
12438: The joyful dwellers of the steep.
12439: 
12440: The Sphinxes
12441: 
12442: One would think long ago,
12443: This was lifted to the sky,                7575
12444: Had we not seen from down below,
12445: How it wormed its way on high.
12446: A bushy forest covers it,
12447: And rock on rock is piled around:
12448: Sphinxes don’t care about it,              7580
12449: It won’t disturb our sacred ground.
12450: The Gryphons
12451: 
12452: Gold in leaves, and gold in spangles,
12453: Through the cracks, see, it tremble.
12454: Don’t you rob us of our treasure,

12456: 
12457: Chorus of Ants
12458:

12460: Threw to the sky,

12462: Quick, climb it on high!
12463: Rapidly in and out!                     7590

12465: Every crumb about’s
12466: Worth you can seize.
12467: You must uncover
12468: Even the slightest,                     7595

12471: You must be everywhere,
12472: Swarming around: then,
12473: Only bring gold here!                   7600

12476: The Gryphons
12477:

12481: Great treasures they protect.           7605

12483: The Pygmies (Classical Dwarves.)
12484: 
12485: We’ve acquired some room,
12486: How, it isn’t clear.

12491: Where a rock is lifted,
12492: Dwarves are there, on hand.
12493: Men and maids, quick and busy,
12494: Exemplary, every pair:              7615

12496: A similar race lived there.

12498: Thankfully our fate is blessed:
12499: Mother Earth is always kind,        7620

12502: The Dactyls (Little Ironworkers.)
12503:

12506: The Littlest Ones, she can make

12512: A convenient place!

12514: Strength, never shirk!
12515: While we’re in peace,               7630

12517: To furnish the horde
12518: With armour and sword.

12527: Secretive fire,
12528: Fetch coals as you should.

12556: Carry to our airy zones!
12557: All already slaughtered,
12558: Blood is reddening the water,            7665
12559: Misshapen dwarfish passions,
12560: Steal the herons’ noblest gems.

12562: Those fat-bellied bow-legged serpents.
12563: You our armies’ members,                 7670
12564: Files of ocean-wanderers,

12571: Mephistopheles (On the plain.)
12572: 
12573: Northern witches were easily controlled,
12574: But over foreign spirits I’ve no hold.
12575: The Blocksberg’s a most convenient locale,
12576: Wherever you are, you’ll find yourself there still.
12577: Dame Ilse watches for us, from her tall stone,        7680
12578: And Heinrich’s still awake on his high throne,
12579: At Elend, the Snorers snore away,
12580: All’s done for a thousand years and a day.

12582: The Earth won’t swell up beneath his feet?….          7685
12583: I wander happily through a level valley,
12584: And in a moment there, thrown up behind me,
12585: A mountain, true it’s hardly to be called one,

12605: He hobbles forwards,                                  7705

12607: Trailing his leg, mind:

13056: 
13057: I’m amazed no poet’s had the intelligence             7995
13058: To sing of you. Tell me, how can that be?
13059: I’ve never seen you properly painted:
13060: The chisel should only try to carve you,
13061: Not the likes of Pallas, Venus, Juno.
13062: 
13063: The Phorkyads
13064: 
13065: Deep in solitude and stillest night,                  8000
13066: No one ever thought to show us three aright.
13067: 
13068: Mephistopheles
13069: 
13070: How could they? Here, concealed from view.
13071: You can’t see anyone: and they can’t see you.
13072: You need to achieve a suitable place,
13073: Where art and splendour share the space,              8005
13074: Where every day, as walking, living heroes,
13075: With giant steps, each block of marble goes.
13076: Where –
13077: 
13078: The Phorkyads
13079: 
13080:          Be silent, and don’t tempt us to roam!
13081: What use would it be to us, to be better known?
13082: Born in the night, and related to the night,          8010
13083: To ourselves, almost: to others quite out of sight.
13084: 
13085: Mephistopheles
13086: 
13087: In that case, there’s little more to say:
13088: One can oneself to others still betray.
13089: One eye’s enough for three, one tooth as well:
13090: Then it should be mythically possible,                8015
13091: To contain three beings in two,
13092: And leave me the third form, too.
13093: For a little while.
13094: A Phorkyad
13095: 
13096:       What do you think? Shall we try?
13097: 
13098: The Others
13099: 
13100: Let’s! – But without the tooth and eye.
13101: 
13102: Mephistopheles
13103: 
13104: Now you’ve denied me the best features of all:   8020
13105: How can I show your strict and perfect form?
13106: 
13107: A Phorkyad
13108: 
13109: Shut one eye, that’s easy to do,
13110: Let one greedy tooth show too,
13111: In profile you’ll at once achieve
13112: A sisterly likeness, to deceive.                 8025
13113: 
13114: Mephistopheles
13115: 
13116: Many thanks! Done!
13117: 
13118: The Phorkyads
13119: 
13120:                    Done!
13121: 
13122: Mephistopheles (As a Phorkyad, in profile.)
13123: 
13124:             Already I’m one,
13125: Of Chaos’s well-beloved sons!
13126: 
13127: The Phorkyads
13128: 
13129: We’re Chaos’s daughters, of undisputed right.
13130: 
13131: Mephistopheles
13132: 
13133: O shame, now I’ll be called a hermaphrodite.
13134: The Phorkyads
13135: 
13136: What a beauty in our sisterly trio!         8030
13137: We’ve two eyes, and two teeth now.
13138: 
13139: Mephistopheles
13140: 
13141: I’ll hide myself from every eye, as well,
13142: And frighten devils in the lakes of Hell.
13143: 
13144: (He exits.)
13145: Part II Act II Scene V: Rocky Coves in the Aegean Sea
13146: 
13147: (The Moon, lingering, at the zenith.)
13148: 
13149: The Sirens (Lying on the cliffs round about, playing flutes and singing.)
13150: 
13151: Though the Thessalian witch-women
13152: Wickedly, dragged you down to them,                                    8035
13153: With their horrors, long ago, in the dark,
13154: Look quietly down, now, from the arc
13155: Of night, on waves of glittering sparks:
13156: Mildly flashing, bright crowds, these:
13157: Shine now upon the swelling seas,                                      8040
13158: Which raise themselves from the deep!
13159: We’re sworn to serve you, thus,
13160: Sweet Luna, show grace to us.
13161: 
13162: The Nereids and Tritons (As marvels of the deep.)
13163: 
13164: Sound out loud, with clearer tones,
13165: Ringing through the sea’s wide zones:                                  8045
13166: Call the peoples of the deep!
13167: Before the storm’s ravening face,
13168: We sank to the stillest place,
13169: Now we’re drawn, by singing, sweet.
13170: See, how we’ve adorned ourselves,                                      8050
13171: In our great delight, as well,
13172: With our crowns, so nobly gemmed,
13173: And our belts with spangles hemmed!
13174: These spoils, now, before you, we lay,
13175: Treasures, shipwrecked here, and swallowed,                            8055
13176: Your enticing songs they followed,
13177: You the daemons of our bay.
13178: 
13179: The Sirens
13180: 
13181: We know well, in ocean freshness,
13182: Fishes play in slippery smoothness,
13183: Flickering lives, devoid of pain:                                      8060
13184: Yet you festive crowds that stray
13185: We would rather find today,
13186: That you’re more than fish, again.
13187: 
13188: The Nereids and Tritons
13189: 
13190: Before we came to meet you,
13191: We were thinking of that too:                 8065
13192: Speed away now, sisters: brothers!
13193: It only needs the slightest journey,
13194: For most effective proof that we,
13195: Certainly, are more than fishes.
13196: 
13197: (They swim off.)
13198: 
13199: The Sirens
13200: 
13201: They’ve vanished in a moment!                 8070
13202: To Samothrace they’re bent,
13203: Gone, with a favourable breeze.
13204: What is it they think they’ll see,
13205: In the realm of the noble Cabiri?
13206: They’re gods! But wondrously strange,         8075
13207: Always causing their forms to change,
13208: Never knowing what they might be.
13209: Stay at your clear height,
13210: Sweet Luna, graceful light,
13211: So we’ll remain nocturnal,                    8080
13212: Not chased by the diurnal!
13213: 
13214: Thales (On the shore, to Homunculus.)
13215: 
13216: I’d gladly lead you to old Nereus:
13217: His home’s not far away and cavernous,
13218: But his head, it’s of the very stubbornest,
13219: He’s a sour-top, and quite the nastiest.      8085
13220: The whole human race can’t satisfy
13221: Him, the grumbler, and needn’t try.
13222: Yet to him the future is revealed,
13223: And so all show respect, and yield
13224: Him honour in his high position:              8090
13225: He’s done quite well by many a one.
13226: 
13227: Homunculus
13228: 
13229: Then let’s try him, and hurry on!
13230: My glass and flame won’t fail our mission.
13231: 
13232: Nereus (The sea-god.)
13233: 
13234: Are those human voices, in my ear?
13235: How quickly my deepest anger stirs!                 8095
13236: Forms, reaching for the gods, in their endeavour,
13237: Yet condemned to be themselves, forever.
13238: In ancient times I had heavenly rest,
13239: Yet drove myself to act well to the best:
13240: And then, when I’d finished what I’d done,          8100
13241: It was quite clear that nothing had been won.
13242: 
13243: Thales
13244: 
13245: And yet, Old Man of the Sea, we trust you:
13246: You’re the Wise: so don’t drive us from you!
13247: See this flame, he’s almost human, really,
13248: He yields himself to your advice, completely.       8105
13249: 
13250: Nereus
13251: 
13252: What advice! Has Mankind valued my advice?
13253: A wise word’s frozen in a stubborn ear.
13254: No matter how often some harsh action strikes,
13255: People remain as self-willed as before.
13256: I warned Paris himself, in a fatherly way,          8110
13257: Before the foreign girl tempted him to stray.
13258: He stood bravely on the shore of Greece,
13259: And I told him what my Spirit could see:
13260: The smoke-filled air, the streaming blood,
13261: Glowing timbers, slaughter’s flood,                 8115
13262: Troy’s day of judgement, caught in verse,
13263: Its horrors known for ten thousand years.
13264: The old man’s words seemed idle to the young,
13265: He followed his need, and Ilium was gone –
13266: A bloody corpse, frozen with ancient pain,           8120
13267: For Pindus’ eagles, a literary gain.
13268: Ulysses too! Didn’t I tell him about
13269: Circe’s wiles, that Cyclopean lout?
13270: The indecision in his own shallow mind,
13271: And all of it! What benefit did he find?             8125
13272: Till, late indeed, the ocean favoured him more,
13273: And brought him, wave-tossed, to a friendly shore.
13274: 
13275: Thales
13276: 
13277: Such behaviour brings the wise man pain,
13278: Yet the good will chance it all again.
13279: An ounce of thanks will still please them deeply,    8130
13280: Outweighing tons of ingratitude completely.
13281: And it’s nothing slight we ask of you:
13282: The boy here wants to exist, and wisely too.
13283: 
13284: Nereus
13285: 
13286: Don’t ruin such a rare mood as this!
13287: Greater needs await me, today, than his:             8135
13288: I’ve summoned all my daughters here to me,
13289: The Dorides, the Graces of the Sea.
13290: Neither Olympus, nor your lands can show
13291: Such lovely forms, with such delicate flow,
13292: They fling themselves, with graceful actions,        8140
13293: From sea-horses to Neptune’s stallions,
13294: Blending so sensitively with the element,
13295: That they seem made of foam, to all intent.
13296: In a play of colours, on Venus’ chariot shell,
13297: Galatea, the loveliest, comes to me, as well,        8145
13298: Who, since Cypris turned away from us,
13299: Rules as the new divinity of Paphos.
13300: And so, heiress, for ages now, the sweet one,
13301: Holds town, and temple, chariot and throne.
13302: Away! It’s time for a father’s enjoyments,           8150
13303: Hearts without hate, lips without judgements.
13304: Away, to Proteus! Ask that wondrous man:
13305: How man exists, and changes, if he can.
13306:

13308: 
13309: Thales
13310: 
13311: We’ll achieve nothing by that game,
13312: Meet Proteus: he’ll vanish, just the same:   8155
13313: And if he stays, he’ll only tell you,
13314: What will amaze you, and confuse you.

13316: Well, make tracks, then, and we’ll try!

13544: Part II Act II Scene VI: The Telchines of Rhodes
13545: 
13546: (The Telchines, on sea-horses and dragons, wielding Neptune’s trident.)
13547:

13549: 
13550: Oh, we are the ones who once forged Neptune’s trident,               8275
13551: With which he controls the tumultuous torrent.
13552: When the thunder erupts from the heavens, and rumbles,
13553: Neptune will reply to those terrible grumbles:
13554: And however the lightning zig-zags above us,
13555: Breaker upon breaker beneath will splash upwards:                    8280
13556: And whatever struggles between them in terror,
13557: Long hurled all about, the deep seas will devour:

13561: The Sirens
13562: 
13563: You, to Helios consecrated,                                          8285
13564: You, with bright day’s blessing freighted,

13566: Luna’s high worship rules again!

13568: The Telchines
13569: 
13570: Loveliest goddess of all in your sphere above!
13571: To hear your brother praised, is something you love.                 8290
13572: To blessed Rhodes lend an ear, now, from the sky,
13573: Where an endless Paean, to him, rises on high.
13574: He begins the day’s course: he ends it again,
13575: He eyes us all with his radiant fiery eye, then.
13576: The mountains, the city, the sea and the strand,                     8295
13577: Please the great god, lovely and bright is the land.
13578: No mist drifts above us, and if one appears,
13579: A ray, and a breeze: and the island shows clear!
13580: There the high god’s in hundreds of statues displayed,
13581: As a youth, and a giant, the mild and the grave.                     8300

13585:

13589: They melt and shape untiringly:
13590: And once, in bronze, it’s plain to see,
13591: They think they’ve caught the very best.
13592: What happens at last to these proud ones?

13594: An earthquake tosses to the sky:
13595: Long since, they’re all melted down.
13596: Earth’s toil, whatever else it may be,
13597: Is nothing still, but drudgery:
13598: The waves grant a life that’s better:        8315
13599: I’ll bear you to eternal waters,

13601:

13641: What’s that ring of little clouds, set

13649:

13659: Learnt in ancient times, as well.

13663: That can please the real man,

13667: Psylli and Marsi (Peoples of Italy and North Africa. On sea-bulls, sea-

13738: Accept the youngsters here, as men:
13739: I can’t myself grant what you ask,                              8410
13740: Since Zeus alone can make it happen.
13741: The waves that heave and rock you
13742: Leave no place for love to stand,
13743: So when this inclination leaves you,
13744: Send them quietly back to land.                   8415
13745: 
13746: The Dorides
13747: 
13748: Sweet boys, you are so dear to us,
13749: But sadly we must separate:
13750: We asked eternal faithfulness,
13751: But the gods forbid that fate.
13752: 
13753: The Young Men
13754: 
13755: We’re the valiant sailor lads,                    8420
13756: If you’d refresh us further,
13757: We’ve never had it quite so good
13758: And we’ll never have it better.
13759: 
13760: (Galatea approaches on her shell-chariot.)
13761: 
13762: Nereus
13763: 
13764: It’s you, my darling!
13765: 
13766: Galatea
13767: 
13768:                             O father! Delight!
13769: Linger, you dolphins, I’m gripped by the sight.   8425
13770: 
13771: Nereus
13772: 
13773: Past already, they’re moving past,
13774: Wheeling in circular motion:
13775: What care they for the heart’s deep emotion!
13776: Ah, if they’d just take me with them, at last!
13777: And yet, a single glance gives here,              8430
13778: Something that will last all year.
13779: Thales
13780: 
13781: Hail! Hail! Anew!
13782: How happy I feel, too,
13783: Pierced by the Beautiful and True….
13784: All things came from the watery view!               8435
13785: All things are sustained by water!
13786: Ocean, grant us your realm forever.
13787: If you didn’t produce the clouds,
13788: No flowing streams would be allowed,
13789: The rivers wouldn’t roar and shout,                 8440
13790: The streams would never bubble out,
13791: Where would hill, plain, and world be then?
13792: The freshness of life’s what you maintain.
13793: 
13794: An Echo (A chorus from the collective circles.)
13795: 
13796: The freshness of life flows back from you, again.
13797: 
13798: Nereus
13799: 
13800: Floating, turning, they change place,               8445
13801: Far off, no longer face to face:
13802: In extended linking circles,
13803: Appropriate to the festival,
13804: The countless company’s weaving.
13805: But Galatea’s throne of shell,                      8450
13806: I see it clearly: see it still.
13807: It gleams like a star,
13808: Through the throng,
13809: A crowd, the Beloved shines among!
13810: Though just as far,                                 8455
13811: It shimmers bright and clear,
13812: Always true, and near.
13813: 
13814: Homunculus
13815:

13817: Whatever I may shine on,
13818: Is all sweet and fair.                              8460
13819: Proteus
13820: 
13821: In this living ocean,
13822: You light’s shining motion,
13823: First rings in splendour there.
13824: 
13825: Nereus
13826: 
13827: At the heart of the throng, what mystery
13828: Offers itself for our eyes to see?                   8465
13829: What shines round the shell, at Galatea’s feet?
13830: Now waxing powerful, now gentle and sweet,
13831: As if it were fed by the pulses of Love.
13832: 
13833: Thales
13834: 
13835: Homunculus, drawn there by Proteus….
13836: Those are the symptoms of imperious yearning,        8470
13837: I’d expect now the sound of an anguished ringing:
13838: He’ll shatter himself on the glittering throne:
13839: He glitters, he flashes, already, it’s done.
13840: 
13841: The Sirens
13842: 
13843: What fiery wonder transfigures the waves, there,
13844: As one on another sparkles and breaks, there?        8475
13845: It flashes and flickers and brightens towards us:
13846: The nocturnal tracks of the bodies shine round us,
13847: And everything near is surrounded with flame:
13848: So let Eros rule, now: who started the game!
13849: Hail to the sea! Hail to the waves!                  8480
13850: Circled, now, by the sacred blaze!
13851: Hail to water! Hail to fire!
13852: Hail to the rarest sweet desire!
13853: 
13854: All In Chorus
13855: 
13856: Hail, the gently flowing breeze!
13857: Hail, hidden caverns of the seas!                    8485
13858: Be honoured now, for evermore,
13859: You, the Elemental four!
13860: Part II Act III Scene I: Before the Palace of Menelaus in Sparta
13861: 
13862: (Helen enters with the Chorus of Captive Trojan Women. Panthalis is leader
13863: of the Chorus.)
13864: 
13865: Helen
13866: 
13867: I, Helen the much admired yet much reviled,
13868: Come from the shore, where recently we landed,
13869: Still drunk with the violent rocking of those waves                 8490
13870: That from Phrygian heights on high-arched backs,
13871: By Poseidon’s favour, and the East Wind’s power,
13872: Carried us here to the coast of my native land.
13873: There, below us, beside his bravest soldiers
13874: King Menelaus, now, celebrates his return.                          8495
13875: But you, bid me welcome, you, the lofty house
13876: Tyndareus my father built when he returned,
13877: Close by the slope of Pallas Athene’s hill:
13878: Here, where with Clytemnestra, in sisterhood, I
13879: And Castor and Pollux, grew and happily played:                     8500
13880: You, more nobly adorned than all Sparta’s houses.
13881: Be greeted by me, you honoured double doors!
13882: Once, Menelaus the shining bridegroom came
13883: To me, through your friendly inviting portals,
13884: I, the one singled out from among so many.                          8505
13885: Open to me once more, so that I might fulfil,
13886: The King’s command, truly, as a wife should.
13887: Let me pass! And let everything be left behind,
13888: That raged round me, till now, so full of doom.
13889: For since, light in heart, I left this place behind,                8510
13890: Seeking out Venus’ temple, in sacred duty,
13891: Where instead a Trojan robber abducted me,
13892: Many things have happened, men, far and wide,
13893: Gladly tell of, though she’s not so glad to hear them,
13894: Round whom the story grew, and myth was spun.                       8515
13895: 
13896: Chorus
13897: 
13898: O marvellous woman, don’t disdain
13899: Inheritance of the noblest estate!
13900: For the highest fate’s granted to you alone,
13901: The glory of beauty that towers above all.
13902: The Hero’s name sounds his advance,                   8520
13903: And proudly he strides:
13904: But he bows down, most stubborn of men,
13905: Before conquering Beauty, in mind and sense.
13906: 
13907: Helen
13908: 
13909: Enough of that! I’m brought here by my husband,
13910: I’ve been sent ahead by him, now, to his city:        8525
13911: But what the meaning of it is I can hardly guess.
13912: Do I come as his wife? Do I come as the Queen?
13913: Or a sacrifice, for a Prince’s bitter pain,
13914: And the ill fortune long endured by the Greeks?
13915: I’m conquered: but am I a prisoner? I can’t tell!     8530
13916: True, the Immortals appointed Fame, and Fate,
13917: As the two ambiguous, doubtful companions
13918: Of Beauty, to stand here at this threshold with me,
13919: The gloomy, threatening presences by my side.
13920: Even in the hollow ship my husband seldom             8535
13921: Gazed at me, or spoke an encouraging word.
13922: He sat in front of me, as if in evil thought.
13923: But scarcely had the foremost ship’s prow greeted
13924: Land, in that deep bay Eurotas’ mouth has made,
13925: Than he spoke to us, as the gods had urged him:       8540
13926: ‘Here my soldiers will disembark in ordered ranks,
13927: I’ll muster them, ranged along the ocean’s-shore:
13928: But you’ll go on, ever on along the banks
13929: Of sacred Eurotas, shining with bright orchards,
13930: Guide the horses through gleaming water meadows,      8545
13931: Till of your lovely journey you make an end,
13932: Where Lacedemon, once a rich spreading field,
13933: Surrounded by austere mountains, was created.
13934: Walk through the high-towered house of princes,
13935: And summon the capable old Stewardess                 8550
13936: Along with the maidservants I left behind,
13937: Let her display the store of rich treasure to you,
13938: That which your father left, and that I myself
13939: Have added to, amassing it in war and peace.
13940: You’ll find it all still in the most perfect order:    8555
13941: It is a prince’s privilege that he should find
13942: That all is loyalty, on returning to his house,
13943: All that he’s left behind still in its proper place.
13944: Since no slave has the power to effect a change.’
13945: 
13946: Chorus
13947: 
13948: Let this treasure, so steadily massed,                 8560
13949: Bring you delight, now, in eye and breast!
13950: For the necklace bright, and the crown of gold,
13951: Were resting, and darkening, in proud repose:
13952: But enter now, and claim them all,
13953: They’ll quickly respond.                               8565
13954: I love to see Beauty itself compete
13955: Against gold and pearls and glittering gems.
13956: 
13957: Helen
13958: 
13959: So again there came my lord’s imperious speech:
13960: ‘When you’ve examined all of it in due order,
13961: Take as many tripods as you think you’ll need,         8570
13962: And as many vessels as sacrifice requires,
13963: To fulfil the customs of the sacred rites.
13964: Take cauldrons, and basins, and circular bowls:
13965: The purest of water from the holy fountains,
13966: In deep urns: take care that you’ve dry wood too,      8575
13967: Such as will quickly catch fire, and hold all ready:
13968: And finally don’t forget a well-honed knife:
13969: Everything else I’ll leave for your decision.’
13970: So he spoke, at the same time urging my going:
13971: But he who commanded marked out nothing living         8580
13972: To be slain: to honour the Olympian gods.
13973: Essential, but I’ll think no more about it,
13974: And leave all things in the hands of the gods:
13975: They fulfil whatever is in their mind to do,
13976: Whether or not we think it good or evil:               8585
13977: In either case we mortals must endure it.
13978: Often the priest’s heavy axe has been lifted,
13979: From the bowed neck of the sacrificial victim,
13980: So he could not slaughter it, being hindered,
13981: By enemies near, or the gods’ intervention.        8590

13989: Unannounced, to Mankind:                           8595

13991: Troy still burned: did we not see
13992: Death in our faces, shameful death:

13994: Your friends, happily serving,                     8600

14040: Panthalis (As leader of the Chorus.)
14041:

14043: And turn your eyes towards the open doorway!
14044: Sisters, what do I see! Surely the Queen returns        8640

14046: What is it, great Queen? What can you have met with,
14047: Within the halls of your house, instead of greetings,
14048: To cause you such trembling? You can hide nothing,
14049: Since I see your reluctance written on your brow,       8645
14050: And amazement competes there with noble anger.
14051: 
14052: Helen (Who has left the doors open, in her turmoil.)
14053: 
14054: A daughter of Zeus is stirred by no common fear,
14055: No lightly passing hand of Terror can touch her:
14056: Only the Horror that the womb of ancient Night,
14057: Raised from chaos, and shaped in its many forms,        8650
14058: In glowing clouds that shoot, upwards and outwards,
14059: From the peak’s fiery throat, to shake the hero’s breast.
14060: So here today the Stygian gods have marked
14061: The entrance to my house with terror: and gladly
14062: I’d take myself far away, like a guest let go,                8655
14063: Far from this often trodden, long yearned for threshold.
14064: But no! I’ve retreated here now, into the light,
14065: And you Powers will drive me no further, whoever
14066: You are. Rather, I’ll think of some consecration,
14067: So the hearth-fire, cleansed, greets the wife, as the lord.   8660
14068: 
14069: The Leader of the Chorus
14070: 
14071: Noble lady, reveal to your maidservants here,

14073: 
14074: Helen
14075: 
14076: You’ll see what I saw yourselves, with your own eyes,
14077: If ancient Night has not, straight away, swallowed it,
14078: That shape of hers: withdrawn it to her heart’s depths.       8665
14079: But I’ll picture it to you in words, so you’ll know:
14080: As, with those recent orders in mind, I trod,
14081: Gravely, through the palace’s innermost room,
14082: Awed by the silence of the gloomy corridors,
14083: No sound of busy labour greeting my ears,                     8670
14084: No sound of prompt, diligent effort meeting my eye,
14085: No Stewardess appeared, and no maidservants,
14086: No courtesy such as usually greets the stranger.
14087: But as I approached closer to the hearth stone
14088: Beside the glowing ashes that remained, I saw                 8675
14089: A veiled woman, vast shape, seated on the floor,
14090: Not like one who’s asleep, but one deep in thought.
14091: I summoned her to work, with words of command,
14092: Thinking she was the Stewardess whom my husband,
14093: Had placed there perhaps, with foresight, when he left.       8680
14094: But she still sat there, crouched and immoveable:
14095: At last, stirred by my threats, she raised her arm,
14096: As if she gestured me away from hearth and hall.
14097: I turned aside from her, angrily, and sped,
14098: To the steps where the Thalamos is adorned                    8685

14100: Suddenly that strange shape sprang up from the floor,
14101: Barring my way, imperiously, showing herself,

14103: A shape so weird that mind and eye were troubled.             8690

14106: See for yourselves! She even dares the daylight!
14107: Here am I mistress, till the King, my lord, shall come.
14108: Phoebus, beauty’s friend, drives the horrid spawn of Night    8695

14181: Phorkyas (The transformed Mephistopheles.)
14182: 
14183: The saying is old, with meaning noble and true,
14184: That Beauty and Shame, together, hand in hand,             8755
14185: Never pursue the same path, over green Earth.
14186: Such ancient, deep-rooted hatred lives in both,
14187: That whenever they meet, by chance, on the way,
14188: The one will always turn her back on her rival.
14189: Then quickly and fiercely each goes on, again,             8760
14190: Shame downcast, but Beauty mocking in spirit,
14191: Till in the end Orcus’ dark void shall take her,
14192: If age hasn’t, long before then, tamed her pride.
14193: So now I find you, impudent, come from abroad,
14194: With overflowing arrogance, like the cranes,               8765
14195: Their noisily croaking ranks, high overhead,
14196: Their long cloud, sending its creaking tones, down here,
14197: Tempting the quiet traveller to look upwards:
14198: Yet they pursue their way, while he follows his:
14199: And that’s the way it will be with us as well.             8770
14200: What then are you, wild Maenads or Bacchantes,
14201: That dare to rage round the great royal palace?
14202: Who are you, then, who howl at this high house’s
14203: Stewardess, like a pack of bitches, at the moon?
14204: Do you think it’s hidden from me what race you are?        8775
14205: You brood, begotten in battle, raised on slaughter,
14206: Lusting for men, the seducers and the seduced,
14207: Draining the soldiers’ and the citizens’ powers!
14208: To see your crowd’s like watching a vast swarm
14209: Of locusts settle here, darkening the fields.           8780
14210: You the wasters of others labour! Nibbling,
14211: Destroying, the ripening crops of prosperity!
14212: Defeated, bartered, sold in the market, you!

14214: Helen
14215: 
14216: Who abuses the servants before the mistress,
14217: Presumptuously usurping a wife’s true rights?           8785
14218: Only to her is it given to praise whatever’s

14221: They provided to me, when Ilium’s great might,

14226: A lord asks how slaves serve, not what they are.

14856: Part II Act III Scene II: The Inner Court of The Castle

14896: How a company of handsome youths approach
14897: With lingering step, in dignified order,
14898: Marching in ranks. Who gave out the command                          9155
14899: To marshal them, and so quickly arranged
14900: All this youthful team of so handsome a race?
14901: What shall I admire most? Is it the graceful step,
14902: Or the curls of hair on the palest of brows,
14903: Or the rounded cheeks with a peach’s blushes,                        9160
14904: And like it also, in their silkiest down?

14926: 
14927: (What the Chorus has described takes place. After the boys and squires have

14951: May hear a prompt confession of your guilt.

14953: Because of his keen vision to gaze about

14955: At heaven’s spaces, and the breadth of earth,       9200
14956: To report whatever moves here or there,

14963: In honour of the guest. Now he forfeits
14964: His guilty life, and would have shed his blood      9210

14998: Wall, and tower? Bolted gate?                  9235
14999: Mist, it rose, and cleared the mist,
15000: Came the Goddess here in state!
15001: I surrendered heart and eye
15002: Drinking in the gentle light:
15003: How that beauty blinds, and I                     9240
15004: Was blinded wholly by the sight.
15005: 
15006: I forgot the watchman’s duty,
15007: And the promised trumpet call:
15008: Threaten then, now, to destroy me –
15009: Anger lies in Beauty’s thrall.                    9245
15010: 
15011: Helen
15012: 
15013: I cannot punish this evil that I brought here,
15014: With me. Ah me! What a fierce fate it is
15015: Pursues me, so that everywhere I possess
15016: The hearts of men, and that they neither spare
15017: Themselves nor anything else of worth.            9250
15018: They steal, seduce, fight: rushing to and fro,
15019: Demigods, heroes, gods, even daemons
15020: Led me in my wanderings, here and there.
15021: Alone I’ve confused the world, doubly so:
15022: Now I bring threefold, fourfold woe on woe.       9255
15023: Take this innocent away: let him go.
15024: It’s no shame to be deceived by the gods.
15025: 
15026: Faust
15027: 
15028: O Queen, amazed, I see them both together:
15029: The certain archer, and the stricken prey:
15030: I see the bow, from which the shaft was loosed,   9260
15031: That wounded him. Arrow after arrow,
15032: Now strikes me. Imagining the feathered whirr
15033: Of arrows crossing every court and hall.
15034: What am I now? My walls you make unsafe
15035: My most faithful servants, you make rebels,       9265
15036: Already I fear my army too obeys
15037: A victorious and unconquered lady.

15039: And all that I have vainly imagined mine?
15040: Freely and loyally, before your feet,             9270
15041: Let me acknowledge you as Mistress,
15042: Whose presence wins you throne and ownership.
15043: 
15044: Lynceus (Carrying a chest, with men bringing others.)
15045: 
15046: Queen, once more I advance!
15047: The rich man begs a glance,
15048: He sees you and at a glimpse,                           9275
15049: He’s a beggar, and a prince.
15050: 
15051: What am I now? What was I once?
15052: What’s to be willed? What’s to be done?
15053: What use the eye’s clearest sight!
15054: It glances from your royal might.                       9280
15055: 
15056: From the Eastwards we pressed on,
15057: And suddenly the West were gone.
15058: So wide and long the people massed,
15059: The first knew nothing of the last.
15060: 
15061: The first rank fell: the next stood fast,               9285
15062: The third ranks’ lances unsurpassed:
15063: Each man was like a hundredfold,
15064: Thousands died there, all untold.
15065: 
15066: We pressed forwards: we stormed on,
15067: We were masters, then were gone:                        9290
15068: And where I ruled as chief today,
15069: Tomorrow robbed, and stole away.
15070: 
15071: We looked – and rapid was that look:
15072: The loveliest women there we took,
15073: We took the oxen from the stall,                        9295
15074: We took the horses, took them all.
15075: 
15076: But my delight was to discover
15077: The rarest things I could uncover:
15078: And what other men might grasp,
15079: To me was only withered grass.                          9300
15080: I was on the trail of treasure,
15081: Whatever my sharp eye could measure,
15082: In every pocket I could see,
15083: Every chest was glass to me.
15084: 
15085: Heaps of gold, they were mine,            9305
15086: And the noblest gems I’d find:
15087: Yet now the emeralds alone
15088: Are worthy to adorn your throne.
15089: 
15090: Sway there now ‘twixt ear and lip,
15091: You pearly spheres from oceans deep:      9310
15092: A place the rubies dare not seek,
15093: So pale beside your rosy cheek.
15094: 
15095: And so the riches, every prize,
15096: I set down here before your eyes:
15097: Before your feet I gladly yield,          9315
15098: The spoils of many a bloody field.
15099: 
15100: As many chests as I’ve brought you,
15101: I’ve many iron caskets too:
15102: Let me follow your path still

15104: 
15105: You’d scarcely mounted to the throne,
15106: When all bowed down, to you alone,
15107: Wisdom, riches, worldly power,
15108: Before your grace, that very hour.
15109: 
15110: I held it all fast: that is true          9325

15112: I thought its worth was plain to see,
15113: But now it’s nothing much, to me.
15114: 
15115: Everything I’ve owned will pass
15116: From me like mown and withered grass.     9330

15119: Faust
15120: 
15121: Quickly, remove the heap that boldness won,

15124: Hides in its lap: you offer these few things

15127: Of unseen splendours! Let the vaulted halls

15135: Lynceus
15136: 
15137: What the lord commands is nothing,
15138: For the servants, a mere plaything:

15140: Over blood and treasure too.

15143: Near this form of noble gold,

15145: Near the riches of her face

15148: Helen (To Faust.)
15149:

15152: Its lord, and so secures this place for me.

15163: 
15164: So many wonders do I see, and hear                 9365

15168: Each sound seeming to give way to the next,
15169: And when a word gave pleasure to the ear,          9370

15180: Helen
15181: 
15182: You’ll tell me how to speak with lovely art?

15184: Faust
15185: 
15186: It’s easy, it must pour forth from the heart.

15190: Helen

15192:                           - who else is burning.   9380

15222: 
15223: Women, used to men’s desires,
15224: Are not particular,
15225: They are proficient.                                 9395

15241: Helen

15251: Helen

15256: Faust

15260:

15262: 
15263: Spell the letters in love’s primer,
15264: Only loving, pass your time here,                9420

15282: Rash disturbance! Insistent, she comes pushing in here:               9435

15295: He deserves the ladies’ favour,
15296: Who, in their defence, shall fight.                                   9445
15297:

15299:

15302: You, the prime of northern beauty,

15304:

15321: At her feet lay vale and mountain,

15323: 
15324: Germans, with your walls and towers,
15325: Defend Corinth and her bays!

15328:

15338:

15340: In lands, possessed of every right:

15343:

15346: Chorus
15347: 
15348: Who wants the loveliest for himself,
15349: First, above everything,
15350: Would be wise to have weapons about him:
15351: He might well gain by flattery                  9485

15354: The sly, and insidious tempt her from him,

15357:

15359: And think him nobler than the rest,
15360: Since he combines wisdom and strength,
15361: So that the powerful show obedience,

15364: Each as much for his own profit

15374: 
15375: Faust
15376:

15381: 
15382: In their rivalry they’ll protect you            9510
15383: Half-island ringed by leaping waves,

15389: That, long ago now, wondered at her,

15399: Let your country hold you in its power!              9525
15400: 
15401: And though you may endure the sun’s cold arrow
15402: Up there, on the mountain’s jagged height,
15403: See, how the rocky hillside’s green below, now,

15405: 
15406: The sources leap, all streams rush down as one,      9530
15407: Gorge, slope, and meadow are already green.

15412: The horned cattle tread the dizzy edge:              9535

15415: 
15416: Pan guards them too: and lively nymphs live there,
15417: In the damp fresh space of bushy clefts,
15418: And, yearning upward to the higher air,              9540

15421: Whose stubborn boughs stick out from them, in state:

15424: 
15425: Pure mother’s milk, in that still realm of shadows,

15427: Fruit’s not lacking, gift of fertile meadows,
15428: And from the hollow trunk drips honey mild.
15429: 
15430: Here well-being’s granted all the race,                9550
15431: Cheek and lips both to joy consent,
15432: Each one is immortal, in their place:
15433: And all there are healthy and content.
15434: 
15435: And thus the lovely child, of purest days,
15436: Grows, and achieves his father’s strength.             9555
15437: We’re amazed, the question’s still, always:

15439: 
15440: When Apollo took a shepherd’s form,
15441: The fairest of them was like the sun:
15442: Since, where pure Nature is the norm,                  9560
15443: Then all the worlds must move as one.
15444: 
15445: (Taking his seat beside her.)
15446: 
15447: So, this have you, and this have I achieved:

15449: Oh, know yourself from highest gods conceived,
15450: To the first world, alone then, you belong.            9565
15451: 
15452: No solid fortresses shall ring you round!
15453: In eternal youth, stands as it stood –
15454: So our stay with all delight be crowned –
15455: Arcadia in Sparta’s neighbourhood.

15457: You fled towards a happy destiny!
15458: Let our thrones as arbours now be found,

15460: 
15461: (The scene is completely transformed. Bowers are built against a range of
15462: rocky caverns. A shadowy grove runs to the foot of the rocks that rise on all

15466: Phorkyas
15467:

15470: To dream what I saw clearly with my own eyes.

15477: Chorus
15478:

15485: You’ve hardly rubbed your eyes, yet you’re already weary, children? 9585

15494: Phorkyas
15495:                                                         Sweetly sundered,
15496: From the world, alone they summoned me to grant them quiet service.
15497: At their side I stood there, honoured, yet still, as one who’s trusted, 9590
15498: Always gazed at something other, turning here and there at random.

15501: 
15502: Chorus
15503: 
15504: You speak as if a whole world’s space were hidden there inside, now,

15506: 
15507: Phorkyas
15508: 
15509: It’s true: you’re inexperienced, and its depths are unexplored!
15510: I felt, lost in contemplation, hall on hall there, court on court.
15511: In an instant laughter echoes, through the cavernous recesses:
15512: There I see a boy is springing, from his mother to his father,
15513: From his father to his mother, all is dandling and caressing,            9600
15514: And a foolish, a fond teasing, shouts of play, and cries of joy,
15515: Alternate, there, and I’m deaf.
15516: A naked wingless Spirit, like a faun, and yet no creature,
15517: Leaps across the solid floor, and the ground beneath responding,
15518: Sends him flying through the ether, till the second leap or so, there, 9605
15519: He can touch the cavern roof.
15520: Anxiously his mother’s calling: ‘Leap as often as you like, dear,
15521: But all flying is forbidden, so beware of taking flight.’
15522: And his loyal father warns him: ‘In the earth’s the power of swiftness,
15523: That will quickly send you flying: touch the ground then with your toe, 9610
15524: And like that son of Earth’s, Antaeus, you’ll soon find strength again.’
15525: So he leaps the rocky masses of the cavern, from a cornice,
15526: To another and around then, as a ball does when it’s thrown.
15527: But suddenly he’s vanished in a crevice of the cavern,
15528: And it seems he’s lost. His mother grieves for him, father comforts, 9615
15529: I stand there, wondering anxiously, but there again’s the vision!
15530: Do buried treasures lie there? Robes embroidered all with flowers,
15531: He has fittingly assumed.
15532: Tassels tremble from his shoulders, ribbons flutter round his chest,
15533: In his hand a golden lyre, like a miniature Apollo,                      9620
15534: He steps happily to the overhanging brink: amazing.
15535: And the parents in delight clasp each other to their hearts,
15536: What’s that shining round his temples? It’s hard to see what’s gleaming,
15537: Is it gold and gems, or flames, now, of the spirit’s supreme power?
15538: So he moves as if the stately boy’s proclaimed to us already          9625
15539: The future Lord of Beauty, in whose members the eternal
15540: Melodies are stirring: and so you too will also hear him,
15541: And you too will also see him, with the rarest show of wonder.
15542: 
15543: Chorus
15544: 
15545: Do you call this a marvel,
15546: Crete has begotten?                                                  9630
15547: Can you never have listened

15606: Phorkyas

15615: From the heart itself must pour,                                 9685

15617:

15619:

15621: By the sweet and flattering sound,
15622: We, renewed to life, are feeling,
15623: Moved to tears of joy, around.                                   9690
15624: 
15625: Let the sun be lost from heaven
15626: So it’s daylight in the soul,
15627: We’ll discover in the heart, then,

16066: 
16067: Panthalis
16068: 
16069: Quick now, girls! We’re all free of the magic now,
16070: That old Thessalian woman’s enthralling spell,
16071: That jangling dizziness of confusing sound,
16072: Troubling the ear, and more the inner sense.             9965
16073: Down to Hades! Since with solemn step the Queen
16074: Descended swiftly. Let her faithful servants’
16075: Footsteps follow her downward path without delay.
16076: We’ll find her beside the Unfathomable Throne.
16077: 
16078: Chorus
16079:

16081: Even in Hades they’re on top,
16082: Associating proudly with their peers,
16083: Persephone’s intimate company.
16084: But for us, then, in the background,
16085: Of the asphodel-meadowed depths,                         9975
16086: With their long rows of poplars,
16087: Their fruitless crowds of willows,
16088: What fun is there for us,
16089: Piping like bats at twilight,
16090: In cheerless, ghostly whispers?                          9980
16091: 
16092: Panthalis
16093: 
16094: Who wins no name, and wills no noble work,
16095: Belongs to the elements: so away with you!
16096: My own intense desire’s to be with my Queen,
16097: The individual’s loyalty and not just service.
16098:

16100: 
16101: All
16102: 
16103: We’re returned to the light of day,                      9985
16104: No longer individual, it’s true,
16105: We feel it, and we know it,
16106: But we’ll never go back to Hades.
16107: Ever-living Nature,
16108: Makes the most valid claim                                             9990
16109: On our spirits, and we on her.
16110: 
16111: A Section of the Chorus
16112: 
16113: We in all the thousand branches’ whispering tremors, swaying murmurs,
16114: Sweetly rocked, will lightly draw the root-born founts of being upwards,
16115: To the twigs: and now with leaves, and now with the exuberant blossom,
16116: We’ll adorn their floating tresses, freely thriving in the breezes.     9995
16117: Straight away, now, as the fruit falls, happy crowds and flocks will gather,
16118: For the picking and the tasting, swift-arriving, busy-thronging:
16119: Bending down, now, all around us, as before the early gods.
16120: 
16121: A Second Section of the Chorus
16122: 
16123: We, against the rocky cliff face, by the smooth far-gleaming mirror,
16124: We will nestle, softly moving, in the gentle waves that flatter:       10000
16125: Listening, hearing every echo, birdsong, now, or reedy fluting,
16126: To the fearful voice of Pan, too, we’ll provide a ready answer:
16127: To the murmuring, send a murmur: to the thunder roll our thunder,
16128: In earth-shaking repetition, in threefold, or tenfold echo.
16129: 
16130: A Third Section of the Chorus
16131: 
16132: Sisters! We, of nimbler senses, hurry onwards with the waters:         10005
16133: For the richly covered, far-off, mountain ranges each entice us.
16134: Ever deeper, ever downward, in meandering curves we’ll water
16135: First the meadows, then the pastures, then the house and the garden,
16136: Where the slender tips of cypress, over banks and watery mirror,
16137: Over all the landscape, mark it, soaring skywards in the air.          10010
16138: 
16139: A Fourth Section of the Chorus
16140: 
16141: Wander where you please, you others: we will circle, we will rustle
16142: Round the densely planted hillside, where the vine stock’s growing green:
16143: There, each day, we’ll pay attention to the cultivator’s passion,
16144: Watch his diligence and care, there: watch for its uncertain outcome.
16145: How he hoes, how he digs there, how he heaps, and prunes, and ties, 10015
16146: Prays to all the gods above him, most of all prays to the sun god.
16147: The effeminate one, Bacchus, gives scant thought to faithful servants,
16148: Rests in arbours, lolls in caverns, flirting with the youngest Faun.
16149: Whatsoever he might need there, for his half-befuddled dreaming,
16150: Is left for him in wineskins, stored around in jars and vessels,        10020
16151: Right and left, in cool recesses, gathered through the endless ages.
16152: But when the gods, that’s Helios we mean before all others,
16153: Cooling, wetting, warming, heating, fill the vineyard’s horn of plenty,
16154: Where the silent grower laboured, suddenly it’s all enlivened,
16155: And in every leaf there’s rustling, rustling now from vine to vine.     10025
16156: Baskets creaking, buckets rattling, the tubs are carried groaning,
16157: All towards enormous vats there, to the lusty treaders’ dance:
16158: So, then, all the sacred bounty, of the pure bred juicy harvest,
16159: Fiercely trodden, spurting, foaming, mingled there, is crudely squashed.
16160: Now the cymbals’ brazen clamour’s ringing boldly in our ears,           10030
16161: As Dionysus from his Mysteries is unveiled, and is revealed:
16162: Here with his goat-foot Satyrs, whirling goat-foot Satyresses,
16163: And Silenus’s, unruly, long-eared ass, that brays amongst them.
16164: Nothing’s spared! The cloven feet now, trample on all decency:
16165: All the senses whirl, bewildered: hideously, ears are stunned, there. 10035
16166: Drunkards fumble for their wine-cups, head and bellies over-full,
16167: Here and there one has misgivings, but can only swell the riot,
16168: Since to hold the latest vintage, one must drain the oldest skin!
16169: 
16170: (The curtain falls. Phorkyas in the proscenium rises to full height, steps
16171: down from her tragic buskins, removes her mask and veil, and reveals
16172: herself as Mephistopheles, to point the last lines, by way of epilogue.)
16173: Part II Act IV Scene I: High Mountains
16174: 
16175: (Fierce, jagged rocky peaks. A cloud approaches, pauses and settles on a
16176: projecting ledge. It parts.)
16177: 
16178: Faust (Steps out.)
16179: 
16180: Gazing at those deep solitudes beneath my feet,
16181: I tread the mountain brink with deliberation,                        10040
16182: Leaving the cloud-vehicle that carried me,
16183: Softly, through bright day, over land and ocean.
16184: Slowly, not dispersing, now, it moves away.
16185: With a rolling movement, travelling eastward,
16186: And the eye follows in wondering admiration.                         10045
16187: Moving it divides, wave-like and changeable.
16188: Yet it shapes itself – My eyes can’t deceive me! –
16189: I see, reclining there, nobly, on sunlit pillows,
16190: A godlike female form, though it’s immense!
16191: An image of Juno, Leda, or Helen herself,                            10050
16192: Royally lovely, floating before my eyes.
16193: Ah! It’s already melting! Formlessly huge
16194: And towering it hangs in far icy eastern hills,
16195: Reflecting deep meaning from fine fleeting days.
16196: Yet a soft, delicate band of mist still clings                       10055
16197: To head and body, coolly caressing: and cheers me.
16198: Now it lifts lightly, soars higher and higher, there,
16199: Condensing. Does its enticing shape deceive me,
16200: Like some long-forgotten joy of earliest youth?
16201: The first riches of the heart’s depths flow again:                   10060
16202: I’d liken it to Aurora’s Love, light-winged:
16203: The first, swiftly felt, scarcely understood glance,
16204: That outshines every treasure when it’s held fast.
16205: The lovely form rises, now, like spiritual beauty,
16206: Not melting further, but lifting through the air,                    10065
16207: And carries, far-off, the best of what I am.
16208: 
16209: (A seven-league boot strides forward: another follows immediately.
16210: Mephistopheles steps out of them. The boots stride off quickly.)
16211: 
16212: Now that I call real onward striding!
16213: But tell me why you’re all alone,
16214: Climbing here among the horrors,
16215: In these horrendous gulfs of stone?                     10070
16216: I know them well, but with another face,
16217: In truth, the floor of Hell’s a similar place.
16218: 
16219: Faust
16220: 
16221: You’re never short of a foolish fantasy:
16222: You’ve dusted that one off again I see.
16223: 
16224: Mephistopheles (Seriously)
16225: 
16226: When the Lord God – and I know why as well –            10075
16227: Banished us from the air to deepest deeps,
16228: There, where round and round the glow of Hell,
16229: An eternal inward self-fuelled fire leaps,
16230: We found we were too brightly illuminated,
16231: Quite crowded, and uncomfortably situated.              10080
16232: All the devils fell to fits of coughing,
16233: The vents above them and beneath them puffing,
16234: Hell swollen with the sulphur’s stench and acid,
16235: Gave out its gas! The bubble was so massive,
16236: That soon the level surface of the earth,               10085
16237: Thick as it was, was forced to crack and burst.
16238: So we all gained another mountain from it,
16239: And what was ground, before, now is summit.
16240: From this they deduced the truest law,
16241: Turn lowest into highest, to be sure,                   10090
16242: Since we escaped from fiery prison there,
16243: To excessive power in the freer air:
16244: An open mystery, yet well concealed,
16245: And only lately publicly revealed. (Ephesians vi:xii)
16246: Faust
16247: 
16248: To me the mountain masses are nobly dumb,                 10095
16249: I don’t ask why they are, or where they’re from.
16250: When Nature in herself was grounded
16251: The ball of Earth she neatly rounded,
16252: Delighting in the mountains and the deep,
16253: Setting rock on rock, and peak on peak,                   10100
16254: Sloping the hills conveniently downward,
16255: Softening them to vales, gently bounded.
16256: They grow green, and joyfully she ranges,
16257: Without the need for any violent changes.
16258: 
16259: Mephistopheles
16260: 
16261: Yes, so you say! It’s clear as day to you:                10105
16262: But he knows otherwise who saw it too.
16263: I was there, while the void seethed below,
16264: Enduring all that swollen, fiery tide:
16265: When Moloch’s hammer forged cliffs, at a blow,
16266: And flung the ruined mountains, far and wide.             10110
16267: Those foreign boulders scattered through the land:
16268: Who knows what forces left them high and dry?
16269: Philosophers all have failed to understand,
16270: The rocks are there, and we must let them stand,
16271: We’ve damaged them, already, where they lie.              10115
16272: Only the true believers, the people, know,
16273: And nothing will shake their fond opinion,
16274: They, since their wisdom ripened long ago,
16275: Say it’s due to Satan’s wonderful dominion.
16276: The traveller climbs, with faith’s crutch, over ridges,   10120
16277: Across the Devil’s rocks, and Devil’s bridges.
16278: 
16279: Faust
16280: 
16281: Yet it’s still worth noting, since every feature,
16282: Reveals what it is the Devil sees in Nature.
16283: Mephistopheles
16284: 
16285: What’s that to me! Let Nature be what she is!
16286: The Devil was there: that’s what I’d have you notice!               10125
16287: We’re the folk, you see, who achieve great things:
16288: The signs are tumult, force, and what nonsense brings! –
16289: But shall I make myself understood at last: it’s best:
16290: Did nothing at all of ours please you in the slightest?
16291: You’ve looked down, from immeasurable heights,                      10130
16292: On the riches of the world, and its splendid sights. (Matthew iv)
16293: Yet, hard as you may be to fire,
16294: Didn’t you feel some deep desire?
16295: 
16296: Faust
16297: 
16298: I did! I saw a mighty plan.
16299: Guess!
16300: 
16301: Mephistopheles
16302: 
16303:             Oh, that’s easily done.                                 10135
16304: I’d find myself some capital city,
16305: It’s core the citizens’ greedy plenty,
16306: Crooked alleys and pointed gables,
16307: Cabbage, turnips, onions, market tables:
16308: Butcher’s stalls where flies all cluster:                           10140
16309: Round the fattened joints, pass muster:
16310: Wherever you move, there you’ll find
16311: Stench and activity, intertwined.
16312: Then wide streets, and wider squares,
16313: Measured, elegant thoroughfares:                                    10145
16314: And, at their end, no gates to bar you:
16315: Just boundless far-flung suburbs too.
16316: There I love to see all the carriages go by,
16317: The noisy rushing about from side to side,
16318: The endless running to and fro,                                     10150
16319: Of scattered ants in ceaseless flow.
16320: And when I walk, and when I ride,
16321: I’d be the central point implied,
16322: A hundred thousand honouring me.
16323: Faust
16324: 
16325: That could never content me though.               10155
16326: A swelling crowd is fine to see,
16327: All well-fed in their way, agreed,
16328: Well-bred, well-taught, all the three –
16329: Yet you’ve only made more rebels grow.
16330: 
16331: Mephistopheles
16332: 
16333: For myself, I’d deliberately create               10160
16334: A pleasure house in a pleasant place.
16335: Woods, hills, fields, meadows, open ground,
16336: With splendid gardens all around.
16337: Between green walls of velvet leaves,
16338: Straight walks, where artful shadows please,      10165
16339: Waterfalls, spanning the rocks, in pairs,
16340: And all those kinds of water-jet affairs:
16341: Rising nobly, while all round the dish,
16342: A thousand little fountains hiss and piss.
16343: Then I’d have a hut, snug and convenient,         10170
16344: Where beautiful women might be content:
16345: And pass the boundless time away
16346: In the sweetest solitude, and play.
16347: Women, I say: since, one and all,
16348: I think of their loveliness in the plural.        10175
16349: 
16350: Faust
16351: 
16352: Sardanapalus! Modern and rural!
16353: 
16354: Mephistopheles
16355: 
16356: Then might one ask to know your yearning?
16357: It’s something daring: I’ve no doubt.
16358: Since the moon was near you in your journeying,
16359: Might it be moon-madness you’re about?            10180
16360: Faust
16361: 
16362: Not at all! This earthly round
16363: Grants space for some mighty thing.
16364: We’ll attempt what’s astonishing,
16365: New strength for daring work I’ve found.
16366: 
16367: Mephistopheles
16368: 
16369: And shall you earn more glory by it too?           10185
16370: One sees the heroines have been with you.
16371: 
16372: Faust
16373:

16375: The deed is all, and not the glory.
16376: 
16377: Mephistopheles
16378:

16380: The splendour of your bright success,              10190
16381: And inspire fools to foolishness.
16382: 
16383: Faust
16384: 
16385: All that’s far from you, indeed.
16386: What do you know of what Men need?
16387: Your contrary being, bitter, dire,
16388: What does it know of Man’s desire?                 10195
16389: 
16390: Mephistopheles
16391: 
16392: Let it all be as you wish it then!
16393: Trust fancy’s flight to me again.
16394: 
16395: Faust
16396: 
16397: My eyes were drawn towards the deepest ocean:
16398: It swelled, and heaped itself, upon itself,
16399: Then ebbed, and shook its waves again in motion,   10200
16400: Storming towards the wide shore’s level shelf.
16401: And that annoyed me: as the exuberance
16402: Of a free spirit, that values all its rights,
16403: Will transmit uneasy feelings to the dance
16404: Of the passionate blood that it excites.             10205
16405: I thought it chance: I gazed more intensely:
16406: The waves paused, rolled away from me,
16407: Far from what they’d reached in their pride:
16408: Time passes, and then once more comes the tide.
16409: 
16410: Mephistopheles (To the audience.)
16411: 
16412: There’s nothing new in that to greet my ears,        10210
16413: I’ve known it for a hundred thousand years.
16414: 
16415: Faust (Continuing passionately.)
16416: 
16417: It sweeps along, to whatever thousand ends:
16418: Fruitless itself, it fruitlessly extends:
16419: It swells and rolls and breaks and overwhelms
16420: The empty stretches of its barren realms.            10215
16421: There wave rules power-inspired wave, again
16422: Draws back – and yet still there’s nothing gained.
16423: If anything makes me despair, of my intent,
16424: It’s the aimless force of that wild element!
16425: Then my spirit dared to soar high above:             10220
16426: Here I must fight, and this I must remove.
16427: And it’s possible! – However tides may flow,
16428: At last they nestle round the hills below:
16429: So they are tamed in their exuberance,
16430: A modest height tops their proud advance,            10225
16431: A modest depth draws them forcefully on.
16432: Quick, through my mind, leapt plan after plan:
16433: Let rich enjoyment be mine for evermore,
16434: To keep the noble ocean from the shore,
16435: To channel all the wide and watery waste,            10230
16436: And urge it backwards to its own deep place.
16437: Step by step I know how to design it:
16438: That’s my desire, so be brave and promote it!
16439: (On the right, from the distance, behind the audience, the sound of drums

16441: 
16442: Mephistopheles
16443: 
16444: That’s trivial! Can you hear the distant drums?
16445: 
16446: Faust
16447: 
16448: War again! The wise man hates it when it comes.                       10235
16449: 
16450: Mephistopheles
16451: 
16452: War or peace, it’s wise to seize the chance,
16453: And gain advantage from the circumstance.
16454: One waits, one notes each favourable moment.
16455: Opportunity’s about, so Faust, be ardent!
16456: 
16457: Faust
16458: 
16459: Spare me all your riddles, if you please!                             10240
16460: Once and for all, say, what am I to seize?
16461: 
16462: Mephistopheles
16463: 
16464: Nothing was hidden from me on my journey:
16465: The noble Emperor’s consumed by worry.
16466: You know him. While we both supplied him,
16467: Those illusory riches in his hand, beside him,                        10245
16468: The whole world then was open to him.
16469: Young, the throne was granted to him,
16470: And it pleased him to assume, wrongly,
16471: That he could easily combine the two,
16472: Enjoy the essential and the lovely too:                               10250
16473: Both government and pleasure, jointly.
16474: 
16475: Faust
16476: 
16477: A fatal error! He who wishes to command
16478: Must make command his joy, and though
16479: His mind is full of all the noblest plans,
16480: What he intends, must let no other know.             10255
16481: What he whispers then in some faithful ear,
16482: Is done, and the world will be amazed to hear.
16483: So he’ll remain supreme, above them all,
16484: And noblest: pleasure comes before a fall.
16485: 
16486: Mephistopheles
16487: 
16488: That’s not the man! He enjoyed himself, and how!     10260
16489: Meanwhile anarchy brought the empire down,
16490: While great fought little, and orders crossed,
16491: And brothers fought with brothers, and were lost,
16492: Castle with castle, city against city,
16493: The guilds at war with the nobility:                 10265
16494: The bishops with their congregation:
16495: No friends, and only a hostile nation.
16496: In churches death and slaughter: through the gate
16497: Every merchant and trader swift to his fate.

16499: The word is ‘defend your life’. And so it goes.
16500: 
16501: Faust
16502:

16504: Then tumbles headlong, and lies there in pain.
16505: 
16506: Mephistopheles
16507: 
16508: None dared to criticise the situation,
16509: Each could, and would improve his station.           10275
16510: Even the smallest wished to be great enough.
16511: But for the best it proved a step too much.
16512: The capable declared, with energy:

16514: The Emperor can’t, and will not – let us choose      10280

16516: While each man achieves security,

16601:

16603:

16641: Here below, in this convenient valley:

16653: The hills aren’t steep, but there’s no ready access,

16655: We’re half-concealed, on undulating ground:                         10355

16673:

16694: Ruining the empire with their fighting,

16700:

16702: One sent for news, perhaps he’s had some luck!
16703:

16708: Probing, out to east and west,

16804: 
16805: On joyful days, when we greet our guests,              10455
16806: Who gather pleasantly, with happy jests,

17469: Stones from the sky, a shower of blood on their tents,    10860

17605: I too, in time, must leave all I still hold dear,
17606: It’s your duty then to name a new ruler, here.
17607: At our holy altar, crown and raise him high:
17608: What war begins ends peacefully, by and by.               10960
17609: 
17610: The High-Chancellor
17611: 
17612: With pride at heart, yet humble in gesture, too,
17613: We, the Earth’s noblest princes bow to you.
17614: So long as blood fills our loyal veins, then still
17615: Are we the body that obeys your every will.
17616: 
17617: The Emperor
17618: 
17619: Now, to conclude, let everything we’ve enacted            10965
17620: Be set down for the future, as we’ve contracted.
17621: As Lords you hold your possessions, free in fact,
17622: With this condition, that they remain intact.
17623: And what you have from us, whatever else is won,
17624: Shall descend in due measure to the eldest son.           10970
17625: The High-Chancellor
17626: 
17627: I’ll entrust it to parchment straight away,
17628: This weightiest statute to bless us, and the state:
17629: The Chancery will provide fair copy, and reveal
17630: You as confirmed, my Lords, by sign and seal.
17631: 
17632: The Emperor
17633: 
17634: And so I dismiss you that you may deliberate           10975
17635: Together, concerning this great day for our state.
17636: 
17637: (The Secular Princes exit.)
17638: 
17639: The Archbishop
17640: 
17641: The Chancellor leaves, the Bishop remains here,
17642: With this grave warning to offer in your ear.
17643: His paternal heart, anxiously, fears for you.
17644: 
17645: The Emperor
17646: 
17647: Speak, in this happy hour, what care’s on view?        10980
17648: 
17649: The Archbishop
17650: 
17651: With what bitter pain I find that even at this hour,
17652: Your hallowed head still toys with Satan’s power!
17653: True, you’ve secured the throne now, yet it seems,
17654: Sadly, scorning God, and the Pope’s great schemes.
17655: When he learns of it, swift punishment he’ll bring,    10985
17656: And destroy your sinful realm with holy lightning.
17657: He’s not forgotten how, at that earlier time,
17658: Of coronation, you freed the wizard: in crime.
17659: With your diadem, you injured Christianity,
17660: Striking a cursed head with the first act of mercy.    10990
17661: Now beat your breast and from your guilty measure,
17662: Give back to the holy shrine a little treasure:
17663: You, taught humility, devote to pious use, and good,
17664: The spacious stretch of hills where your tent stood.
17665: Where evil spirits gathered for your protection,         10995
17666: And the Prince of Liars secured your attention:
17667: Grant mount and forest deep, as far as they extend,
17668: And heights, the green slopes adorn, without end.
17669: Clear lakes rich in fish, countless streams that flow,
17670: Winding swiftly, that rush to the valleys below:         11000
17671: Then the broad vale itself, meadow, lawn and hollow:
17672: Show your remorse: gain the mercy that must follow.
17673: 
17674: The Emperor
17675: 
17676: I’m deeply fearful of this, my heavy sin:
17677: Yourself, mark out the borders of the scheme.
17678: 
17679: The Archbishop
17680: 
17681: First then the place profaned by such sinfulness,        11005
17682: Dedicate that to the service of heavenliness.
17683: Thick walls rise quickly, at the mind’s desire,
17684: Already the sun’s dawn glance lights the choir,
17685: The growing building takes the cross’s structure,
17686: The nave long and high, a delight to each believer:      11010
17687: Already as they press eagerly through the doors,
17688: A first peal rings through hills, down valley floors,
17689: From the high tower, that’s striving towards heaven,
17690: The penitent comes, to whom new life is given.
17691: That day of consecration – may it be soon! –             11015
17692: When your presence grants the greatest boon.
17693: 
17694: The Emperor
17695: 
17696: Let the pious mind proclaim so great an action,
17697: In praising the Lord, I’ll achieve my expiation.
17698: Enough! I already feel my mind’s exaltation.
17699: 
17700: The Archbishop
17701: 
17702: As Chancellor I require a formal proclamation.           11020
17703: The Emperor
17704: 
17705: A formal document: lay that before me,
17706: I’ll be pleased to sign whatever the Church agrees.
17707: 
17708: The Archbishop (Has taken leave, but turns back at the door.)
17709: 
17710: At the same time devote the total income of the land,
17711: As it arises, tithes, taxes, levies, to the work on hand,
17712: Forever. It needs to be maintained, fairly,                     11025
17713: And its careful upkeep will cost us dearly.
17714: From all that plunder, grant us a measure of gold,
17715: To build it quickly there, in that desert fold.
17716: Moreover we’ll need, I can’t help mentioning,
17717: Timber from far off, lime, slate, and such things.              11030
17718: Exhorted from the pulpit, the folk will haul it,
17719: The Church will bless the man who learns to serve it.
17720: 
17721: (He exits.)
17722: 
17723: The Emperor
17724: 
17725: The sin with which my soul is heavy, is full sore:
17726: Wretched Sorcerers have wounded me, once more.
17727: 
17728: The Archbishop (Returning, yet again, and bowing deeply.)
17729: 
17730: Pardon, my Lord! The Imperial shore was given                   11035
17731: To that disreputable man, I’ll excommunicate him,
17732: Unless you in penitence grant the Church, there, too,
17733: Its tithes, and gifts, and taxes: the whole of its revenue.
17734: 
17735: The Emperor (In a bad humour.)
17736: 
17737: That land doesn’t exist, it lies there under the sea.
17738: 
17739: The Archbishop
17740: 
17741: Who’s patient, and is right, his time is yet to be.             11040
17742: For us, your word must wait on one man’s desire.
17743: (He exits.)
17744: 
17745: The Emperor (Alone.)
17746: 
17747: I might as well sign away the whole wide empire.
17748: Part II Act V Scene I: Open Country
17749: 
17750: The Wanderer
17751: 
17752: Yes! Here are the dusky lindens,
17753: Standing round, in mighty age.
17754: And here am I, returning to them,       11045
17755: After so long a pilgrimage!
17756: It still appears the same old place:
17757: Here’s the hut that sheltered me,
17758: When the storm-uplifted wave,
17759: Hurled me shore-wards from the sea!     11050
17760: My hosts are those I would bless,
17761: A brave, a hospitable pair,
17762: Who if I meet them, I confess,
17763: Must already be white haired.
17764: Ah! They were pious people!             11055
17765: Shall I call, or knock? – Greetings,
17766: If, as open-hearted, you still
17767: Enjoy good luck, in meetings!
17768: 
17769: Baucis (A little woman, very aged.)
17770: 
17771: Gentle stranger! Quietly, quietly!
17772: Peace! Let my husband rest!             11060
17773: Long sleep lends the elderly,
17774: Little time to work, at best.
17775: 
17776: The Wanderer
17777: 
17778: Tell me, Mother: are you that wife
17779: To whom thanks should be given:
17780: Who brought a young man back to life,   11065
17781: When wife and husband worked as one?
17782: Are you that Baucis who tirelessly
17783: Restored my almost-vanished breath?
17784: 
17785: (Her husband appears.)
17786: 
17787: Are you that Philemon, who bravely
17788: Saved my wealth from watery death?              11070
17789: Your swiftly burning fire,
17790: Your silvery sounding bell,
17791: In chance, dread and dire,
17792: Was the outcome that befell.
17793: And now let me walk about,                      11075
17794: And view the boundless ocean:
17795: Let me kneel, and be devout:
17796: Mind troubled with emotion.
17797: 
17798: (He walks on, over the downs.)
17799: 
17800: Philemon (To Baucis.)
17801: 
17802: Hurry now, and lay the table,
17803: Underneath the garden trees.                    11080
17804: Let him go: as in the fable,
17805: He’ll not credit what he sees.
17806: 
17807: (He follows, and stands beside the Wanderer.)
17808: 
17809: Where wave on wave, foaming wildly,
17810: Savagely mistreated you,
17811: See a garden planted, widely,                   11085
17812: See the Paradisial view.
17813: I was too old to seize the day,
17814: Unfit to work as long ago:
17815: And while my powers ebbed away,
17816: The tide extended its wide flow.                11090
17817: Clever Lords set their bold servants
17818: Digging ditches, building dikes,
17819: To gain the mastery of ocean,
17820: Diminishing its natural rights.
17821: See green meadow bordering meadow,              11095
17822: Field and garden, wood and town. –
17823: But it’s time to eat, so follow,
17824: Sunset is approaching now.
17825: See the sails, far away there,
17826: Seeking port before the night.                  11100
17827: The birds fly homeward through the air:
17828: Their harbour too heaves in sight.
17829: So gaze then, at the whole horizon,
17830: Where the blue sea used to flow,
17831: Right and left there, to your vision,   11105
17832: Densely peopled space below.
17833: Part II Act V Scene II: In the Little Garden
17834: 
17835: (The three of them at table.)

17853: 
17854: Philemon
17855: 
17856: Is the Emperor, then, at fault,                11115

17859: Crying out what was planned?

17861: The first bold step was made,                  11120

17863: A palace, quickly raised.
17864: 
17865: Baucis
17866: 
17867: For days, work rumbled on in vain,

17869: Where the night’s fires flamed,                11125
17870: Next day a dam would follow.
17871: Human blood was forced to flow,
17872: At night, rose the sound of pain:
17873: The seaward floating fiery glow
17874: Was a canal, come dawn again.         11130
17875: He’s a godless man: he’d steal
17876: Our hut, and our few acres:
17877: But like subjects we must kneel,
17878: When we boast such neighbours.

17883: Holding, on his new-won land!
17884:

17886:

17891:

17893: To watch the last glow of light,      11140
17894: Kneel, pray, and sound the bell,

17896: Part II Act V Scene III: The Palace
17897: 
17898: (Spacious pleasure-gardens: a broad straight canal. Faust in extreme old
17899: age, walking about, thoughtfully.)
17900:

17902: 
17903: The sun is fading, the last boats
17904: Sail swiftly to the harbour here.
17905: One large vessel gently floats,                                      11145
17906: Down the canal: and draws near.
17907: The bright flags flutter merrily,
17908: The masts are trimmed, in time:
17909: The boatmen all praise you gladly,
17910: Fortune celebrates your prime.                                       11150
17911: 
17912: (The little bell on the dunes rings out.)
17913:

17915: 
17916: Accursed ringing! Wounding me
17917: With shame: a treacherous blow:
17918: My realm’s laid out there, endlessly,
17919: But, at my back, this vexes so,
17920: Proclaiming, with its jealous sound:                                 11155
17921: My great estate is less than fine,
17922: The old hut, all the trees around,
17923: The crumbling chapel, are not mine.
17924: And even if I wished to rest there,
17925: A strange shadow makes me shudder,                                   11160
17926: It’s a thorn in my eye, and deeper:
17927: Oh! Would I were somewhere other!
17928:

17930: 
17931: The boat is sailing, brightly dressed,
17932: Towards us, on the evening breeze!
17933: Heaped, with boxes, sacks and chests,                                11165
17934: From its journey on the seas!
17935: (A splendid boat, richly and brightly loaded with foreign goods.)

17939: Chorus
17940: 
17941: Here we land,
17942: Already, here.
17943: Hail to our Lord,
17944: Our patron dear!                                                    11170

17948: Mephistopheles
17949: 
17950: We’ve proven ourselves in every way,
17951: Pleased, if we win our patron’s praise.
17952: We took two ships when we sailed before
17953: With twenty ships we dock, once more.
17954: What we’ve achieved, each fine thing,                               11175
17955: You’ll see from the cargo that we bring.
17956: The ocean’s freedom frees the mind
17957: There all thought is left behind!
17958: You only need a handy grip,
17959: You catch a fish, or take a ship,                                   11180
17960: And once you’re lord of all three,
17961: The fourth one’s tackled easily:
17962: The fifth one’s in an evil plight,
17963: You have the might, and so the right.
17964: You wonder what, and never how.                                     11185
17965: I know a little of navigation:
17966: War, trade, and piracy, allow,
17967: As three in one, no separation.

17969: 
17970: No thanks for us!
17971: No thanks at all!               11190
17972: As if we’ve brought
17973: A stench, that’s all.
17974: He pulls a
17975: Nasty face again:
17976: These royal goods               11195

17999: And coming to
18000: The splendid show,              11210

18003: He won’t be mean,
