18011: 
18012: (To Faust.)
18013: 
18014: This splendid fortune you embrace
18015: With wrinkled brow, and gloomy face!         11220
18016: Your noble wisdom has been crowned,
18017: Sea’s reconciled with solid ground:
18018: From the shore, on swifter track,
18019: The sea wills out the ship, and back:
18020: So speak, that here, from your spire,        11225
18021: Your arms might grip the world entire.
18022: From this place the trench was cut,
18023: Here stood the first wooden hut:
18024: A little ditch was traced from here,
18025: Where now vessels’ wakes appear.             11230
18026: Your servants’ toil, your thought so wise,
18027: Have won the Earth and Ocean’s prize.
18028: From here on –
18029: 
18030: Faust
18031:                  – that accursed here!
18032: That always brings me wretched fear,
18033: To you who are so clever, I say it,          11235
18034: It gives my heart sting on sting,
18035: It’s impossible for me to bear it.
18036: I’m ashamed to even speak the thing.
18037: The old ones up there should yield,
18038: I want the limes as my retreat,              11240
18039: The least tree in another’s field,
18040: Detracts from my whole estate.
18041: There, to stand and look around,
18042: I’ll build a frame from bough to bough,
18043: My gaze revealing, under the sun,            11245
18044: A view of everything I’ve done,
18045: Overseeing, as the eye falls on it,
18046: A masterpiece of the human spirit,
18047: Forging with intelligence,
18048: A wider human residence.                          11250
18049: That’s the worst suffering can bring,
18050: Being rich, to feel we lack something.
18051: The bell’s chime, the lindens’ breeze,
18052: Like tombs in churchyards stifle me.
18053: The exercise of my all-conquering will            11255
18054: Is shattered in the sand, here, and lies still.
18055: How can I drive it from my nature!
18056: The bell peals, and I’m an angry creature.
18057: 
18058: Mephistopheles
18059: 
18060: It’s natural! Intense frustration
18061: Drives a man to desperation.                      11260
18062: Who doubts it! That clang I fear
18063: Falls cruelly on a noble ear.
18064: And that wretched bing-bang-bong,
18065: Through the clear evening sky, that gong,
18066: Is joined to every chance event,                  11265
18067: From first bath to last interment.
18068: As if between its bing and bong
18069: Life’s a dream, and then is gone.
18070: 
18071: Faust
18072: 
18073: Such obstinacy and opposition
18074: Diminishes the noblest position,                  11270
18075: Until in endless pain, one must
18076: Grow deeply weary of being just.
18077: 
18078: Mephistopheles
18079:

18083:

18085: You know the land, with my approval,

18109: Part II Act V Scene IV: Dead of Night
18110: 
18111: Lynceus, the Warder (Singing on the watch-tower of the palace.)
18112: 
18113: For seeing, I’m born,
18114: For watching, employed,
18115: To the tower, I’m sworn,                                          11290
18116: While the world, I enjoy.
18117: I gaze at the far,
18118: I stare at the near,
18119: The moon and the star,
18120: The forest and deer:                                              11295
18121: The eternally lovely
18122: Adornment, I view,
18123: And as it delights me
18124: I delight myself too.
18125: You, fortunate eyes,                                              11300
18126: All you’ve seen, there,
18127: Let it be as it may,
18128: Yet it was so fair!
18129: 
18130: (Pause.)
18131: 
18132: I’m not positioned here, on high,
18133: Just for my own enjoyment:                                        11305
18134: What horror, meant to terrify,
18135: Threatens from the firmament!
18136: I see sparks of fire gushing
18137: Through the lindens’ double night,
18138: Fanned by the wind’s rushing,                                     11310
18139: Ever stronger grows the light.
18140: Ah! Within, the hut is burning,
18141: Damp and mossy though it stand:
18142: Swift help, in this direction turning,
18143: Is needed, yet no aid’s to hand.                                  11315
18144: Ah! The pious old couple,
18145: So careful ever of the fire,
18146: Made a prey to smoke, to stifle,
18147: On this dreadful pyre!
18148: The flame burns on: glowing red,
18149: It’s now a blackened mossy pile:                 11320
18150: If only those good folk are rescued,
18151: From those fires of hell, run wild!
18152: A bright tongue of lightning heaves,
18153: Through the branches, through the leaves:        11325
18154: Breaking, snapping, catching swiftly,
18155: Withered branches flicker, glow.
18156: Why have I such powers to see!
18157: Why are mine the eyes that know!
18158: The little chapel now collapses,                 11330
18159: With the falling branches’ weight.
18160: Already with bright snakelike flashes,
18161: The treetops, gripped, meet their fate.
18162: Glowing crimson, to their hollow
18163: Roots, the trunks now burn with ease. –          11335
18164: 
18165: (A long pause. Chant.)
18166: 
18167: What used to please my eyes, below,
18168: Has vanished with the centuries.
18169: 
18170: Faust (On the balcony, towards the downs.)
18171: 
18172: What whining song is that, above?
18173: Too late its word and tone reach me.
18174: The watchman wails: yes, I’m moved:              11340
18175: Annoyed by this impatient deed.
18176: But let the lime-trees be erased,
18177: A horror now of half-burnt timber,
18178: A watchtower can soon be raised,
18179: To gaze around at boundless splendour.           11345
18180: From there I’ll see my new creation,
18181: One set aside for that old pair: at least,
18182: They’ll feel benign consideration,
18183: Enjoying their last days in peace.
18184: 
18185: Mephistopheles and the Three Warriors (Below.)
18186: 
18187: Here we come, and at the double:                 11350
18188: Pardon us! We’ve caused you trouble.
18189: We knocked, and knocked on the door,
18190: But it seemed locked for evermore:
18191: We rattled it, and shook it too,
18192: Until the planks broke in two:                  11355
18193: We called aloud, and threatened, then,
18194: But there was no reply, again.
18195: And as happens in such cases,
18196: They heard nothing, hid their faces:
18197: But we commenced without delay                  11360
18198: To drive the stubborn folk away.
18199: That pair knew scant anxiety,
18200: They died of terror, peacefully.
18201: A stranger, who was hiding there,
18202: And wished to fight, we tried to scare.         11365
18203: But in the fast and furious bout,
18204: From the coals that lay about,
18205: The straw took fire. Now all three,
18206: In that one pyre, burn merrily.
18207: 
18208: Faust
18209: 
18210: Were you deaf to what I said?                   11370
18211: I wanted them moved, not dead.
18212: This mindless, and savage blow,
18213: Earns my curse: share it, and go!
18214: 
18215: Chorus
18216: 
18217: The ancient proverb says of course:
18218: Yield willingly to a greater force!             11375
18219: While if you’re bold and opt for strife,
18220: You’ll stake your house, and home – and life.
18221: 
18222: (They exit.)
18223: 
18224: Faust (On the balcony.)
18225: 
18226: Stars hide their faces, and their glow,
18227: The fire sinks, and flickers low:
18228: A moist breeze fans the dying ember,            11380
18229: Bringing smoke and vapour closer.
18230: Quickly said, too quickly done, I fear! –
18231: Now, what hovers like a shadow, here?

18288: The Three
18289: 
18290: The clouds there are moving, and cover the stars!      11395
18291: Behind us, behind us! From far, oh, from far,
18292: He’s coming, our Brother, he’s coming, he’s – Death.
18293: 
18294: Faust (In the Palace.)
18295: 
18296: I saw four: but only three went away:
18297: I caught no meaning from the words they say.
18298: It sounded as if I heard – ‘Necessity’s breath’,       11400
18299: And then a gloomy rhyming word, like – ‘Death’.
18300: It rang hollow, ghostly, subdued, to me.
18301: Even now I’ve not won my liberty.
18302: If I could banish Sorcery from my track,
18303: Unlearn the magic-spells that draw me back,            11405
18304: And stand before you, Nature, as mere Man,
18305: It would be worth the pain of being Human.
18306: So was I, a seeker in the darkness,
18307: Cursing both self and world, in wickedness.
18308: Now the air is filled with phantom shapes,             11410
18309: It’s hard to see how anyone escapes.
18310: Though day may smile on us with rational gleams,
18311: The night entwines us in a web of dreams:
18312: We come happily from the fields of youth,
18313: A bird croaks: what? Misfortune: is our truth.              11415
18314: Cloaked with superstitions, soon and late:
18315: It’s wedded to us, warns us: shows our fate.
18316: And so, alone, intimidated, we stand.
18317: The door creaks, yet no one is at hand.
18318: 
18319: (Anxiously.)
18320: 
18321: Is anyone there?
18322: 
18323: Care
18324:                     The answer must be, yes!                11420
18325: 
18326: Faust
18327: 
18328: And you, who then are you?
18329: 
18330: Care
18331: 
18332:                              I am your guest.
18333: 
18334: Faust
18335: 
18336: Be gone!
18337: 
18338: Care
18339: 
18340:                I am here, in my proper place.
18341: 
18342: Faust (First angered, then composed, addressing himself.)
18343: 
18344: Take care: of magic spells show not a trace.
18345: Care
18346: 
18347: Though the ear choose not to hear,
18348: In the heart I echo, clear:                  11425
18349: Savage power I exercise,
18350: Transformed I am, to mortal eyes.
18351: On the land, and on the ocean,
18352: Evermore the dread companion,
18353: Always found, and never sought,              11430
18354: Praised, as well as cursed, in thought. –
18355: Have you yourself not known Care?
18356: 
18357: Faust
18358: 
18359: I sped through the World that’s there:
18360: Gripped by the hair every appetite,
18361: And let go those that failed to delight,     11435
18362: Let those fly that quite escaped me.
18363: I’ve desired, achieved my course,
18364: Desired again, and so, with force,
18365: Stormed through life: first powerfully,
18366: But wisely now: and thoughtfully.            11440
18367: Earth’s sphere’s familiar enough to me,
18368: The view beyond is barred eternally:
18369: The fool who sets his sights up there,
18370: Creates his own likeness in the air!
18371: Let him stand, and look around him well:     11445
18372: This world means something to the capable.
18373: Why does he need to roam eternity!
18374: Let him grasp what is firm reality.
18375: So let him wander down his earthly day:
18376: And if ghosts haunt him, go on his way,      11450
18377: Find joy and suffering in striding on,
18378: Dissatisfied with every hour that’s gone.
18379: Care
18380: 
18381: When of man I take possession,
18382: Then his whole world is lessened:
18383: Endless gloom meets his eyes,        11455
18384: No more suns will set or rise,
18385: Though intact, to outer sense,
18386: He lives in the dark, intense,
18387: Never knowing how to measure
18388: Any portion of his treasure.         11460
18389: Good and ill are merely chance,
18390: He starves, food in his hands:
18391: Be it joy or be it sorrow
18392: He delays it till tomorrow,
18393: Waiting for the future, ever,        11465
18394: Finding his fulfilment, never.
18395: 
18396: Faust
18397: 
18398: Be gone! And don’t come near me!
18399: Such nonsense I’ll not understand.
18400: Away, with your evil litany,
18401: Sent to confuse the cleverest man!   11470
18402: 
18403: Care
18404: 
18405: Shall he come, or shall he go?
18406: All decision is denied him:
18407: In the middle of the road,
18408: He staggers, feeling round him.
18409: He’s ever more deeply lost,          11475
18410: Seeing everything star-crossed,
18411: Wearies himself and all the rest,
18412: Stifles as he holds his breath:
18413: Lifeless, but not yet gone under,
18414: Resists despair or surrender.        11480
18415: So, with an incessant rolling,
18416: A painful end, and hard going,
18417: Now free, and now constrained,
18418: In half sleep, poorly entertained,
18419: Confine him in a little space:                     11485
18420: Prepare him for Hell’s other place.
18421: 
18422: Faust
18423: 
18424: Unholy spectre! So you hand our race
18425: To the ravages of a thousand devils:
18426: Even transform our worthless days
18427: To a wretched knot of entangling evils.            11490
18428: It’s hard I know to free oneself from Demons,
18429: The strong spirit-bonds are not lightly broken:
18430: And yet, Care, I’ll not recognise you, nor even,
18431: That creeping power of yours, by any token.
18432: 
18433: Care
18434: 
18435: Feel it now, as on the wind,                       11495
18436: I, and my curse, depart, again.
18437: Lifelong, all you men are blind,
18438: Now, Faust, be so to the end!
18439: 
18440: (She breathes in his face, and departs.)
18441: 
18442: Faust (Now blind.)
18443: 
18444: The night seems deeper all around me,
18445: Only within me is there gleaming light:            11500
18446: I must finish what I’ve done, and hurry,
18447: The master’s word alone declares what’s right.
18448: Up from your beds, you slaves! Man on man!
18449: Reveal the daring of my favoured plan.
18450: Seize the tools: on with pick and spade!           11505
18451: Let the end-result be now displayed.
18452: Strict order, and swift industry
18453: Then the finest prize we’ll see:
18454: And so the greatest work may stand,
18455: One mind equal to a thousand hands.                11510
18456: Part II Act V Scene VI: The Great Outer Court of the Palace

18461:

18463: Quivering spirits of the dead,
18464: All you patchwork semi-natures,

18470: With half an impression,
18471: That it concerns a tract of land,
18472: Of which we’ll gain possession.

18474: Chains to measure ground on:                                  11520

18477: 
18478: Mephistopheles
18479: 
18480: Artistic effort’s not the prize:
18481: Carry it out in your own manner!
18482: Lay the longest one of you lengthwise,                        11525
18483: Then pile the turf on him, you others.
18484: Do as they once did for our fathers there,
18485: Dig out a somewhat lengthened square!
18486: Gone from a palace to a narrow place:
18487: It’s still as stupid an end for man to face.                  11530
18488: 
18489: The Spirits of the Dead (Digging with mocking gestures.)
18490: 
18491: When I was young and lived and loved,
18492: I thought it was very sweet:
18493: To happy sounds, and cheerful steps,
18494: I lifted up my feet.
18495: Now treacherous old age has clawed                                   11535
18496: Me with his crutch, since when
18497: I stumble at the grave’s wide door,
18498: Why do they leave it open!
18499: 
18500: Faust (Comes from the Palace, groping his way past the doorposts.)
18501: 
18502: How the clattering of shovels cheers me!
18503: It’s the crews still labouring on,                                   11540
18504: Till earth is reconciled to man,
18505: The waves accept their boundaries,
18506: And ocean’s bound with iron bands.
18507: 
18508: Mephistopheles (Aside.)
18509:

18513: The Water-demon, one vast feast.

18533: The depth of earth and gravel dug away.
18534: Mephistopheles (Half-aloud.)

18538: 
18539: Faust
18540: 
18541: A swamp lies there below the hill,
18542: Infecting everything I’ve done:                       11560
18543: My last and greatest act of will
18544: Succeeds when that foul pool is gone.
18545: Let me make room for many a million,
18546: Not wholly secure, but free to work on.
18547: Green fertile fields, where men and herds             11565
18548: May gain swift comfort from the new-made earth.
18549: Quickly settled in those hills’ embrace,
18550: Piled high by a brave, industrious race.
18551: And in the centre here, a Paradise,
18552: Whose boundaries hold back the raging tide,           11570
18553: And though it gnaws to enter in by force,
18554: The common urge unites to halt its course.
18555: Yes, I’ve surrendered to this thought’s insistence,
18556: The last word Wisdom ever has to say:
18557: He only earns his Freedom and Existence,              11575
18558: Who’s forced to win them freshly every day.
18559: Childhood, manhood, age’s vigorous years,
18560: Surrounded by dangers, they’ll spend here.
18561: I wish to gaze again on such a land,
18562: Free earth: where a free race, in freedom, stand.     11580
18563: Then, to the Moment I’d dare say:
18564: ‘Stay a while! You are so lovely!’
18565: Through aeons, then, never to fade away

18907: As their own prize, they’ve flown off to heaven:
18908: They’ve stolen a great, a unique treasure:
18909: That noble soul, mortgaged to my pleasure,               11830

18912: Who’d grant me my well-earned right?

18915: At great expense, shameful! And it’s gone:
18916: I’ve mishandled it all disgracefully,
18917: A common lust, an absurd passion,
18918: Swayed the hardened devil foolishly.

18920: With all these childish, stupid things,
18921: It was, in truth, no trivial Foolishness,
18922: That took possession of him in the end.
18923: Part II Act V Scene VII: Mountain Gorges, Forest, Rock, Desert
18924: 
18925: (Holy Hermits, divided in ascending planes, posted among the ravines.)
18926: 
18927: Chorus and Echo
18928: 
18929: Forests, they wave around,
18930: Over them, cliffs bear down,                                        11845
18931: Roots cling to rocky ground,
18932: Trunk upon trunk is bound,
18933: Wave after wave sprays up,
18934: Deep caves protecting us.
18935: Lions prowl silently,                                               11850
18936: Round us, still friendly,
18937: Honouring sacred space,
18938: Love’s holy hiding place.
18939: 
18940: Pater Ecstaticus (Hovering up and down.)
18941: 
18942: Eternal, fire of bliss,
18943: Glow of love’s bond this is,                                        11855
18944: Pain in the heart, seething,
18945: Rapture divine, foaming.
18946: Arrows, come, piercing me,
18947: Spears, compelling me,
18948: Clubs, you may shatter me,                                          11860
18949: Lightning may flash through me!
18950: So passes the nullity
18951: Of all unreality,
18952: And from the lasting star
18953: Shines Love’s eternal core.                                         11865
18954: 
18955: Pater Profundis (At a lower level.)
18956: 
18957: As this rocky abyss at my feet,
18958: Rests on a deeper abyss,
18959: As a thousand glittering streams meet
18960: In the foaming flood’s downward hiss,
18961: As with its own strong impulse, above,                              11870
18962: The tree lifts skywards in the air:
18963: Even so all-powerful love,
18964: Creates all things, in its care.
18965: Around me there’s a savage roar,
18966: As if the rocks and forests sway,            11875
18967: Yet full of love the waters pour,
18968: Rushing bountifully away,
18969: Sent to irrigate the valley here:
18970: The lightning that flashed down,
18971: Must purify the atmosphere,                  11880
18972: With poisonous vapours bound –
18973: They are love’s messengers, they tell
18974: Of what creates eternally around us.
18975: May it inflame me inwardly, as well,
18976: Since my spirit, cold and confounded,        11885
18977: Torments itself, bound in the dull senses,
18978: As sharp-toothed fetters’ agonising art.
18979: Oh, God! Calm my thoughts, pacify us,
18980: And bring light to my needy heart!
18981: 
18982: Pater Seraphicus (In the middle regions.)
18983: 
18984: What a mist of morning hovers                11890
18985: Through the pine-trees’ swaying hair!
18986: Can I guess what it might cover?
18987: A crowd of spirits live there.
18988: 
18989: Choir of Sacred Young Boys
18990: 
18991: Tell us, Father, where we wander,
18992: Tell us, Kind One, who we are?               11895
18993: We are happy: Being’s tender
18994: To all who are, all who are.
18995: 
18996: Pater Seraphicus
18997: 
18998: Young boys! Born at midnight’s hour,
18999: Mind and spirit half-unveiled,
19000: For your parents, a lost dower,              11900
19001: For the angels, profit gained.
19002: You can feel that one who loves
19003: Is near to you, so come to me:
19004: Yet of earthly ways and moves,
19005: You bear no traces, happily.                                   11905
19006: Rise into my eyes, those known
19007: Organs of the earthly life,
19008: You can use them as your own,
19009: Gaze at all the spaces wide!
19010: 
19011: (He absorbs them into himself.)
19012: 
19013: Those are trees: those are cliffs,                             11910
19014: A stream of water, rushing round,
19015: With gigantic leaps it lifts,
19016: Shortening its journey down.
19017: 
19018: The Young Boys (From within him.)
19019: 
19020: That’s indeed a mighty vision,
19021: But it’s gloomy here, you know,                                11915
19022: With fear and dread we’re all shaken.
19023: Father, Kind one, let us go!
19024: 
19025: Pater Seraphicus
19026: 
19027: Rise upwards to the highest sphere,
19028: Grow unnoticed there forever,
19029: While in pure eternal manner,                                  11920
19030: God’s presence makes you stronger.
19031: Such is the spirit’s libation,
19032: Blending with the freest air:
19033: Love’s eternal revelation,
19034: Bliss is unfolded there.                                       11925
19035: 
19036: The Choir of Young Boys (Circling round the highest summit.)
19037: 
19038: Hands now entwining,
19039: Joyfully circling round,
19040: Soaring and singing
19041: With sacred feeling’s sound!
19042: In the divinely taught,                                        11930
19043: Now you should trust:
19044: He whom your worship sought
19045: You’ll see at last.
19046: 
19047: The Angels (Soaring in the highest atmosphere, carrying the immortal part
19048: of Faust.)
19049: 
19050: He’s escaped, this noble member
19051: Of the spirit world, from evil,                                     11935
19052: Whoever strives, in his endeavour,
19053: We can rescue from the devil.
19054: And if he has Love within,
19055: Granted from above,
19056: The sacred crowd will meet him,                                     11940
19057: With welcome, and with love.
19058: 
19059: The Younger Angels
19060: 
19061: Every rose from the hands
19062: Of those penitents, loving, holy,
19063: Helped us win the victory,
19064: The highest work, completed, stands,                                11945
19065: The treasure of this soul we’ve won.
19066: Evil bowed to petals thrown,
19067: Devils fled the blows we threw.
19068: Instead of Hell’s hurts anew,
19069: They felt spirits’ loving pain:                                     11950
19070: Pierced with agony again
19071: The old devil-master too was gone.
19072: Shout with joy! All is done.
19073: 
19074: The More Perfect Angels
19075: 
19076: Carrying earthly remains
19077: Is hard to endure,                                                  11955
19078: Though they survive the flames,
19079: They are still the impure.
19080: Once a great spirit’s strength
19081: So tightly fits
19082: All the four elements,                                              11960
19083: No angel splits
19084: That double nature wed,
19085: The inwardly binding:
19086: To Eternal Love instead
19087: Is left the unwinding.                                                 11965
19088: 
19089: The Younger Angels
19090: 
19091: Misted on rocky heights
19092: Now we are feeling,
19093: Nearing our clearer sight
19094: Spiritual Being.
19095: These clouds are vanishing                                             11970
19096: A crowd I see, moving,
19097: Of sacred young men,
19098: Freed from their earthly gloom,
19099: Circling together,
19100: Delighting again,                                                      11975
19101: In the spring’s brighter bloom,
19102: In higher air.
19103: Let them together then,
19104: Lead him on: risen,
19105: Perfect, and there!                                                    11980
19106: 
19107: The Young Boys
19108: 
19109: Joyfully we receive
19110: Him as a chrysalis:
19111: So that we now achieve
19112: A pledge of our bliss.
19113: Let all the threads be lost                                            11985
19114: That now surround him!
19115: He is already blessed,
19116: Divine Love has found him.
19117: 
19118: Doctor Marianus (The transformed Faust: in the highest purest cell.)
19119: 
19120: Here is the freest view,
19121: Of spirit borne skywards.                                              11990
19122: There women moving too
19123: Drifting on upwards.
19124: The splendour I see within
19125: Garlands of stars,
19126: There, all the Heavens’ Queen        11995
19127: Shines from afar.
19128: 
19129: (Enraptured.)
19130: 
19131: Highest Queen of all the world!
19132: Let me, in the blue,
19133: With all heaven’s web unfurled,
19134: Know your mystery too.               12000
19135: Approve the tender, serious,
19136: Stir of the human heart,
19137: And in love’s sacred bliss,
19138: Raise it higher, through your art.
19139: Our courage is unconquerable         12005
19140: When you command on high:
19141: But our glow is gentler, still,
19142: When you are satisfied.
19143: Virgin, pure, of loveliest mind,
19144: Mother, in all nobility,             12010
19145: Peer to everything divine,
19146: Queen of our reality.
19147: Such light cloud fragments
19148: Wind all around her,
19149: They are the penitents,              12015
19150: Women so tender,
19151: All around her knees,
19152: Breathing the air, free,
19153: Desiring her mercy.
19154: You are the Virginal Mother,         12020
19155: It’s not surprising
19156: Those seduced by another
19157: Towards you are rising.
19158: Taken in weakness now,
19159: They are all harder to save:         12025
19160: Who can resist the power
19161: Of desires that enslave?
19162: How quickly the feet may slip
19163: On smooth, sloping ground!
19164: Who’s un-tempted by glance and lip,                               12030
19165: Or by flattering sounds?
19166: 
19167: (The Mater Gloriosa soars into space.)
19168: 
19169: Choir of Female Penitents
19170: 
19171: You soar, on high, now,
19172: Towards the eternal realm,
19173: Hear our pleading, though,
19174: You, the peerless one,                                            12035
19175: Oh, merciful one!
19176: 
19177: Magna Peccatrix (The sinful woman who anointed Christ’s feet, See Luke
19178: vii:36)
19179: 
19180: By the love that at the feet there
19181: Of your son, divine, transfigured,
19182: Let the tears like balsam flow there,
19183: Despite the Pharisees’ derision:                                  12040
19184: By the vessel, that so richly
19185: Spread its fragrance on the ground,
19186: By the locks of hair that softly
19187: Dried the holy feet, shed round –
19188: 
19189: The Woman of Samaria (The woman at the well, See John iv)
19190: 
19191: By the well, where once before                                    12045
19192: Abraham’s flocks were driven,
19193: By the jar, that cooled the Saviour,
19194: That to sacred lips was given:
19195: By the pure and flowing fountain,
19196: That poured out its clear water,                                  12050
19197: Overflowing, bright and certain,
19198: Through all the worlds, forever.
19199: 
19200: Mary of Egypt (Acta Sanctorum)
19201: 
19202: By the consecrated place
19203: Where the Lord’s body lay:
19204: By the warning arm, against my face,                     12055
19205: That thrust me far from the doorway:
19206: By my forty years’ repentance,
19207: Faithful, in that desert land:
19208: By the blissful final sentence
19209: That I wrote there on the sand –                         12060
19210: 
19211: All Three
19212: 
19213: Since you offer your presence
19214: To the worst sinner,
19215: The prize of penitence
19216: Soars upwards forever,
19217: Begrudge not this true soul,                             12065
19218: Who, this once, transgressed,
19219: Not knowing she might fall,
19220: Commensurate forgiveness!
19221: 
19222: A Penitent, Formerly Named Gretchen (Stealing closer.)
19223: 
19224: Oh, bow down,
19225: You peerless one,                                        12070
19226: You radiant one,
19227: Your face, in mercy, towards my bane!
19228: My true beloved,
19229: No longer clouded,
19230: Returns to me again.                                     12075
19231: 
19232: The Sacred Young Boys (Nearing, hovering in circles.)
19233: 
19234: With mighty limbs, already
19235: He is beyond us there,
19236: Returning to us, so richly,
19237: The rewards of our care.
19238: We were taken early                                      12080
19239: Out of life’s chorus:
19240: Yet he’s learned, so he
19241: Will gently teach us.
19242: The Penitent, Formerly Named Gretchen
19243: 
19244: Changed to himself, he’s scarce aware
19245: Of the spirits’ noble choir all around,     12085
19246: He hardly knows his new life, there,
19247: Already he’s so like the sacred crowd.
19248: See, how he’s thrown off every bond
19249: Of his old earthbound integument,
19250: And his first youth now’s re-found,         12090
19251: It shines through his ethereal garment.
19252: Allow me to teach him, here,
19253: The new light still blinds him so.
19254: 
19255: The Mater Gloriosa
19256: 
19257: Come! Rise towards the higher spheres!
19258: Gaining awareness of you, he will follow.   12095
19259: 
19260: Doctor Marianus (Bowing, in adoration.)
19261: 
19262: Gaze towards that saving gaze,
19263: All you, the penitent and tender,
19264: To all those blissful ways,
19265: Give thanks, and follow after.
19266: Let every finer sense, unseen,              12100
19267: Be offered to her service,
19268: Virgin, Mother now, and Queen,
19269: Goddess, grant your mercies!
19270: 
19271: The Mystic Choir
19272: 
19273: All of the transient,
19274: Is parable, only:                           12105
19275: The insufficient,
19276: Here, grows to reality:
19277: The indescribable,
19278: Here, is done:
19279: Woman, eternal,                             12110
19280: Beckons us on.
